title: CWYD v2 — Bug Registry
description: Canonical defect registry for CWYD v2. Records every observed defect (wrong or broken runtime behavior) with its root cause, fix, and cross-references to the daily worklog and the development plan.
author: CWYD Engineering
ms.date: 2026-06-14
topic: reference
keywords: bugs, defects, registry, v2, root cause, regression, recovery
estimated_reading_time: 14
---

## Purpose

This file is the canonical, file-based registry of **defects** in CWYD v2: behavior that is wrong, broken, or regressed against intent. It exists so bug history survives across sessions and is never trapped in ephemeral agent memory.

Record a bug here the moment it is observed, even before it is fixed. Update the same entry when it is fixed. Every entry is self-contained: a reader should understand the symptom, the root cause, and the fix without opening any other file.

## Relationship to the development plan

[development_plan.md](development_plan.md) §0.1 (backend) and §0.2 (frontend) are the **phase debt and task queues**: deferred work, refactors, and follow-ups that clear on each phase's end-of-phase audit cadence (Hard Rule #12). They are not a defect log.

The split:

* A **defect** (wrong or broken behavior) is recorded here in `bugs.md`. This is the canonical source of truth for defects.
* A **debt or task item** (deferred work, planned refactor, scoped follow-up) stays in the development plan debt queues.

When a defect also needs phase-audit visibility, the development plan keeps a one-line pointer row that references the `BUG-####` id here, and the full detail lives in this file. There is one source of truth per concern, never two.

## Conventions

### Identifiers

Bugs use a sequential, zero-padded id: `BUG-0001`, `BUG-0002`, and so on. Ids are never reused. The next free id is one greater than the highest id already in the registry.

### Closed-set fields

The registry uses three closed sets. Use only these values.

Area: `backend`, `frontend`, `infra`, `functions`, `docs`, `ci`.

Severity: `blocker` (nothing ships or a pipeline is dead), `high` (a core path is broken), `medium` (a path is degraded with a workaround), `low` (cosmetic or minor).

Status: `open`, `in-progress`, `fixed`, `wontfix`, `duplicate`.

### Placeholder rule

This file is tracked and may reach public GitHub. Never write real environment values (subscription, tenant, resource group, azd env name, resource suffix, identity ids, real FQDNs). Use the placeholder tokens defined in [adr/0019-no-env-specific-content-in-tracked-files.md](adr/0019-no-env-specific-content-in-tracked-files.md), for example `<SUFFIX>`, `<RESOURCE_GROUP>`, `<AZURE_SUBSCRIPTION_ID>`. Environment-variable names such as `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` are generic and may be written verbatim.

### How to add a bug

1. Allocate the next `BUG-####` id.
2. Add a row to the Registry table with status `open` (or `in-progress` if already being worked).
3. Add a `### BUG-####` subsection under Details with the symptom, root cause, fix, and references.
4. Cross-reference the day's worklog entry under [worklog/](worklog/), and add a pointer row in the development plan debt queue only if the defect needs phase-audit visibility.

| BUG-0013 | 2026-06-11 | 2026-06-14 | backend | medium | fixed | The Thinking/reasoning feed never shows **substantive** model reasoning: the backend emitted no model-`reasoning` SSE frames (only the canned KB-search narration), so the correctly-wired FE panel showed no thinking content. Live-verified on **both** orchestrators with a parametrized `tests/integration` test that forces each past the persisted cosmos `langgraph` override; that live run also caught BUG-0035. |

Inline `[docN]` markers now render as literal text; their clickable-citation behavior is deferred to BUG-0016. |

The v1 right-side citation detail column stays out of scope. |

Surfaces downstream of (and distinct from) the BUG-0020 MCP 401. |
| BUG-0022 | 2026-06-11 | 2026-06-12 | backend | medium | fixed | On the default `agent_framework` path an operator-authored instruction override (`cwyd_agent_instructions` in `RuntimeConfig`) was dropped: the orchestrator invoked the agent by name and used the server-side baked instructions (cached by identity, ADR 0008), so a saved prompt silently had no effect (it applied only on `langgraph`). Surfaced by audit during the BUG-0021 fix (GAP-2); fixed by the GA pattern (ADR 0025) resolving instructions per request via `build_agent` → `_resolve_definition`. |
| BUG-0023 | 2026-06-12 | 2026-06-12 | infra | high | fixed | The `post_provision` Foundry IQ knowledge-base seed wires the KB query-planning model to the o-series **reasoning** deployment (`AZURE_OPENAI_REASONING_DEPLOYMENT`, e.g. `o4-mini`), but the knowledge-base API only accepts **chat** models, so the KB PUT fails with `400 Unsupported model type ... ModelName must be either gpt-4o, ... gpt-5.1, ...`. Fixed by sourcing the KB model from the chat deployment (`AZURE_OPENAI_GPT_DEPLOYMENT`). |
| BUG-0024 | 2026-06-12 | 2026-06-12 | infra | high | fixed | Foundry IQ knowledge-base retrieval returns nothing (chat then refuses with the out-of-domain fallback, no citations): the knowledge base calls its query-planning chat model with the **search service's system-assigned managed identity** (KB model `authIdentity` is null → defaults to the search MI), but that identity has **no role** on the AI Services account, so the model call fails `401` (`lacks the required data action .../OpenAI/deployments/.../chat/completions/action`). The v2 Bicep grants `Cognitive Services OpenAI User` to the UAMI but never to the search service identity. |
| BUG-0025 | 2026-06-12 | 2026-06-12 | infra | high | fixed | The `agent_framework` chat returned the out-of-domain fallback with no citations: the KB retrieval tool is attached server-side as `MCPTool(project_connection_id=<search connection>)`, so the Responses API runs `mcp_list_tools` / retrieval **server-side under the project search connection's identity**, and the KB MCP endpoint rejected it with `401 Unauthorized` (`McpListTools(tools=[])` → no retrieval tool → the agent refuses). Root cause (confirmed against the read-only reference architecture): the tool pointed at the wrong connection category (`CognitiveSearch` / bare `AAD`, `useWorkspaceManagedIdentity: false`, no `audience`), which presents no usable bearer to the server-side MCP path. Fixed by creating a dedicated `cwyd-kb-mcp` **`RemoteTool` / `ProjectManagedIdentity`** connection (`audience: https://search.azure.com`), pointing `AZURE_AI_SEARCH_CONNECTION_NAME` at it, and granting the project MI `Search Service Contributor` (it already held `Search Index Data Reader`). Verified: the orchestrator now emits `mcp_call.completed`, `citation` frames, and a grounded `Benefit_Options.pdf` answer (no 401, no fallback). Distinct from BUG-0024 (the inner KB → model hop) and BUG-0020 (SDK-side connect, which the GA pattern bypassed by moving MCP server-side). |
| BUG-0026 | 2026-06-12 | 2026-06-12 | backend | medium | fixed | The `agent_framework` KB-search reasoning narration never reaches the FE "thinking" panel: `_update_to_events` emits the narration + `tool` event only for `function_call` content, but server-side Foundry-IQ KB retrieval (GA-FULL `MCPTool(project_connection_id=…)`) surfaces as `mcp_server_tool_call` content (name on `.tool_name`, not `.name`), so the branch is skipped and the grounded stream carries only `citation` + `answer`. Concrete mechanism behind BUG-0013's empty-panel symptom on the `agent_framework` path. |
| BUG-0027 | 2026-06-12 | 2026-06-14 | backend | medium | fixed | The FE "thinking" panel shows only animated dots during the multi-second retrieval wait. After BUG-0026 the KB-search narration ("Searching the knowledge base…") *is* emitted, but on the `agent_framework` path it fires from `_update_to_events` only when the `mcp_server_tool_call` block surfaces — which is *after* server-side Foundry IQ retrieval completes — so `reasoning`/`tool`/`citation`/`answer` all arrive in one burst at the end and the narration never shows *during* the wait; on `langgraph` retrieval runs in-code before any event, so nothing shows upfront either. The narration is correct but emitted too late to indicate activity during the wait. Fix: emit it upfront in the shared `run_chat` pipeline (after the safety guards, before the orchestrator runs), gated on a configured knowledge source (the router computes the flag), so every current + future orchestrator inherits during-the-wait narration with zero per-provider code; then drop the now-redundant late per-call narration from `agent_framework._update_to_events` (keep the `tool` event). |
| BUG-0028 | 2026-06-12 | 2026-06-14 | backend | high | fixed | The `langgraph` orchestrator returned the out-of-domain fallback for in-domain queries (e.g. "tell me about employee benefits"). Retrieval was healthy (client-side Azure AI Search returns 5 relevant hits, injected as a `[docN]` sources system message), but the ported strict v1 `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` "if the retrieved documents do not contain enough information … your only response is [fallback]" clause made `gpt-5.1` over-refuse on the raw chat-completion path. Confirmed with five guardrail-variant probes against the live model: a minimal prompt + the same sources grounds reliably; the strict guardrail refused 8/8 (temp 0.0 + default). `agent_framework` survives the same prompt because Foundry IQ presents KB results as authoritative tool outputs — so in `cosmosdb` mode the intended `agent_framework` path works, but in `postgresql` mode `langgraph` is the only path and this blocked answering entirely. Fixed (with operator consent — edits the BUG-0011-protected shared CWYD safety prompt) by softening the `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` grounding clause + the `CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY` in/out-of-domain section to a relevance-based "answer when relevant, even if brief" directive, while keeping an explicit ungrounded-creative-content ban (stories/poems/jokes/song lyrics), the exact fixed fallback string, and the BUG-0011 guardrail-wrapping invariant. Live-verified on `langgraph`: "employee benefits" grounded 3/3, "health plans" grounded, France + dragon-poem refused. The secondary `complete()` temperature/`max_tokens` threading was attempted but reverted (it surfaced BUG-0029) and deferred. |
| BUG-0029 | 2026-06-14 | 2026-06-19 | backend | medium | fixed | `FoundryIQ.chat()` sends the OpenAI Chat Completions `max_tokens` parameter, but `gpt-5.1` (and other gpt-5 / o-series chat models) reject it with `400 invalid_request_error` (`Unsupported parameter: 'max_tokens' is not supported with this model. Use 'max_completion_tokens' instead.`). Latent today because `BaseLLMProvider.complete()` (the `langgraph` chat path) does not thread `max_tokens`, so the parameter is never sent on that path; surfaced while attempting the BUG-0028 secondary fix (threading `openai_temperature` / `openai_max_tokens` through `complete()`), which made every `langgraph` chat 500 on `gpt-5.1`. That threading was reverted. Fix (separate unit): in `FoundryIQ.chat()` / `chat_stream()` send `max_completion_tokens` instead of `max_tokens` (the forward-compatible name for current Azure OpenAI chat models), then re-attempt threading the configured sampling settings through `complete()`; also confirm `gpt-5.1` accepts a custom `temperature` (gpt-5 reasoning models constrain it) before threading temperature. **Fixed 2026-06-19 (two parts):** (1) `FoundryIQ.chat()` / `chat_stream()` now send `max_completion_tokens` instead of the rejected `max_tokens` (identical semantics). (2) The configured sampling is threaded end-to-end so the admin `openai_temperature` / `openai_max_tokens` settings actually apply: `complete()` (base + the `FoundryIQ` override) forwards `temperature` / `max_tokens` to `chat()` (omitted on the reasoning branch, which reasoning models reject); the conversation router forwards `effective.openai_temperature` / `openai_max_tokens` into orchestrator construction; `langgraph` captures + forwards them to `complete()`; and `agent_framework` reads the effective admin-override values over the `settings.openai` env defaults. A live probe confirmed gpt-5.1 chat completions accepts `temperature` (0.0/0.7/1.0) + `max_completion_tokens` with no constraint (the temperature restriction is reasoning-path-only, BUG-0035, which `complete()` already routes around). Also cleaned `_to_openai_messages` to emit only `{role, content}` (no `metadata` / enum-role leak onto the wire). Full backend suite 1069 passed / 0 failed. |
| BUG-0030 | 2026-06-14 | 2026-06-15 | backend | high | fixed | The two orchestrators emit structurally different citations for the same corpus, so the FE renders inconsistent references. `langgraph` injects a numbered `[docN]: <content>` sources block into the prompt and post-processes the model's `[docN]` markers into `Citation(id="[doc1]", title="Benefit_Options.pdf")` — clean v1-style inline `[doc1]` + a friendly filename label. `agent_framework` grounds via the server-side Foundry IQ KB MCP tool, so the Responses model emits OpenAI **native** citation annotations (inline `【6:0†source】`) and `Content.annotations` whose `file_id`/`url` is the raw search-index document key (`mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>`); `citations_from_annotations` maps that raw id straight through, yielding inline `【6:0†source】` + a raw `mcp://…` source label with no filename. Net: the same question produces `[doc1]`+`Benefit_Options.pdf` on `langgraph` but `【6:0†source】`+`mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>` on `agent_framework`. Root cause: the shared `compose_cwyd_instructions` prompt carries the same `[docN]` citation rule for both, but it is honored only by `langgraph`'s in-prompt source injection; the Foundry IQ KB tool overrides the citation contract with its own native annotation format and surfaces document keys, not filenames. Distinct from the FE-only BUG-0014 / BUG-0015 / BUG-0016 (which all assume a `[docN]` marker already exists). Fix direction: normalize the `agent_framework` path in post-processing to the v1 shape — rewrite native `【N:M†source】` markers to `[docN]` and resolve the friendly filename (from the annotation `title` / KB metadata) so both orchestrators emit one `[docN]` + filename `Citation` shape. **Update 2026-06-14:** does NOT reproduce on the live deployment (real capture: inline `[doc1]` + `Citation(id="[doc1]", title="Benefit_Options.pdf")`); the integration lane now guards the normalized shape. **Fixed 2026-06-15:** operator chose fallback (b) — the `agent_framework` path backfills friendly `title`/`snippet`/`url` onto KB citations via an app-side by-key Search lookup (`enrich_kb_citations` ← `BaseSearch.get_document_by_key`), and a present-but-null `url` maps to `""` (a second `str(None)`→`"None"` site in `_to_result`, distinct from BUG-0033's annotation-boundary fix); live-confirmed `[doc1]` + `Benefit_Options.pdf` + snippet + `url=""`, no native markers — see Details. |
| BUG-0031 | 2026-06-14 | 2026-06-14 | backend | medium | fixed | The BUG-0011 guardrail-wrapping invariant holds only on the `agent_framework` path, not on `langgraph`, for operator-authored instruction overrides. `_resolve_definition` (agent_framework) wraps a saved `cwyd_agent_instructions` override via `compose_cwyd_instructions(text)` so the fixed `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` always bookends the authored persona; but `langgraph` receives `effective.cwyd_agent_instructions` — the raw stored override (the PATCH handler stores it un-wrapped and `resolve_effective_config` overlays that raw value) — and injects it directly as a SYSTEM message with no `compose_cwyd_instructions` call. So with an admin custom prompt, `agent_framework` keeps the guardrail (out-of-domain refusal + `[docN]` citation rule + fixed fallback) while `langgraph` drops it; BUG-0011's "authored text customizes the persona between the guardrail bookends, it does not replace them" invariant is enforced on only one path. In the default state (no override) both resolve to the already-wrapped `CWYD_AGENT.instructions`, so there is no divergence and current default-prompt testing is unaffected; the RAI write-time gate (`PROMPT_FIELDS`) still screens authored prompts, so the malicious-jailbreak vector of BUG-0011 is not reintroduced — what `langgraph` loses is the standing guardrail behaviors. Root cause: instruction composition is not a shared seam — the guardrail wrap lives only in `_resolve_definition` (read-time) and the default constant, with no equivalent on the langgraph wiring. Fix direction: compose the guardrail-wrapped instructions once in a shared seam consumed by both orchestrators (e.g. wrap in `resolve_effective_config` / the router, or in the `LangGraphOrchestrator` constructor) so both receive identical wrapped text; dovetails with the BUG-0030 shared-prompt/grounding-seam normalization. **Fixed** by introducing one shared composition seam, `resolve_cwyd_instructions(override_text)` in `definitions.py`, and routing both consumers through it: `resolve_effective_config` (the value `langgraph` injects as its SYSTEM prompt) and `_resolve_definition` (agent_framework) now each wrap the raw stored override via that single seam — exactly once each, no double-wrap — instead of two parallel/absent wraps. The three composition references collapse to one; an override is guardrail-wrapped identically on both paths and the no-override case stays byte-identical to `CWYD_AGENT.instructions`. Router-boundary + DRY-contract tests added; full v2 suite green (2247 passed), `pyright --strict` clean on the touched files. |
| BUG-0032 | 2026-06-14 | 2026-06-19 | backend | low | fixed | The admin prompt-override round-trip can double-wrap the guardrail. `GET /api/admin/config` returns `cwyd_agent_instructions = CWYD_AGENT.instructions`, which is the **wrapped** default (`CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY` + `CWYD_GUARDRAIL`). If the FE editor pre-populates from that GET and the operator edits and re-saves, the stored override now contains the guardrail text; at runtime the shared `resolve_cwyd_instructions` seam wraps it again via `compose_cwyd_instructions`, so `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` appears twice in the effective instructions. Latent before BUG-0031 on `langgraph` (raw injection) but present on `agent_framework`; after BUG-0031 both paths wrap, so the double-wrap is now consistent across orchestrators. Not a safety hole — the guardrail is still present (duplicated, not dropped) and the RAI write-gate still screens the prompt — hence low severity; the cost is a redundant guardrail block bloating the system prompt and a confusing authoring UX. Root cause: `GET /config` exposes the wrapped default as the editable value, so the guardrail is part of the round-tripped text. **Fixed 2026-06-19:** both admin read endpoints now expose the editable persona **body** — `GET /api/admin/config` and the env baseline of `GET /api/admin/config/effective` return `CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY` (not the guardrail-wrapped `CWYD_AGENT.instructions`); the `/config/effective` override case already surfaced the raw authored override (itself a body). The runtime seam `resolve_effective_config` is unchanged — it still appends `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` exactly once when building the effective prompt — so the editor never seeds the guardrail and a seed-edit-save round-trip can no longer bake it into the stored override. `CWYD_AGENT` is now unused in `admin.py` (import swapped to `CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY`). Verification: updated three contract tests + added `test_config_effective_default_persona_excludes_guardrail` (asserts the guardrail is absent from the editable default on both GET surfaces); admin router + service suites 133 passed; full backend suite 1070 passed / 0 failed. (The stripping-on-re-wrap alternative was rejected per the bug doc as brittle string surgery.) |
| BUG-0033 | 2026-06-14 | 2026-06-14 | backend | low | fixed | `Citation.url` serializes as the string `"None"` (not `null` / `""`) on the `agent_framework` path. Observed in a live `POST /api/conversation` capture: `{"id": "[doc1]", "title": "Benefit_Options.pdf", "url": "None", ...}`. The Foundry IQ KB annotation has no usable URL, and a Python `None` is being stringified to `"None"` somewhere on the annotation → `Citation.url` path (`citations_from_annotations` reads `url = ann.get("url", "")`, so either the SDK annotation already holds the literal string `"None"` or a `str(None)` coercion leaks through). The FE could render this as a broken `None` link. Low severity (cosmetic wire defect; no grounding/safety impact). Fix direction: coerce a missing/`None` annotation URL to `""` at the `citations_from_annotations` boundary, after confirming whether the SDK annotation `url` is itself the literal `"None"`. Found via the new integration lane while capturing the BUG-0030 citation shape. **Fixed 2026-06-14:** the annotation string fields (`file_id` / `url` / `title` / `snippet`) now pass through a `_clean_annotation_field` boundary helper in `citations.py` that coerces a Python `None` and the literal `"None"` to `""`, so the placeholder never reaches `Citation.url` (nor leaks into an `id` via the `file_id or url or title` fallback). See the BUG-0033 detail section. |
| BUG-0033 | 2026-06-14 | 2026-06-14 | backend | low | fixed | `Citation.url` serializes as the string `"None"` (not `null` / `""`) on the `agent_framework` path. Observed in a live `POST /api/conversation` capture: `{"id": "[doc1]", "title": "Benefit_Options.pdf", "url": "None", ...}`. The Foundry IQ KB annotation has no usable URL, and a Python `None` is being stringified to `"None"` somewhere on the annotation → `Citation.url` path (`citations_from_annotations` reads `url = ann.get("url", "")`, so either the SDK annotation already holds the literal string `"None"` or a `str(None)` coercion leaks through). The FE could render this as a broken `None` link. Low severity (cosmetic wire defect; no grounding/safety impact). Fix direction: coerce a missing/`None` annotation URL to `""` at the `citations_from_annotations` boundary, after confirming whether the SDK annotation `url` is itself the literal `"None"`. Found via the new integration lane while capturing the BUG-0030 citation shape. **Fixed 2026-06-14:** the annotation string fields (`file_id` / `url` / `title` / `snippet`) now pass through a `_clean_annotation_field` boundary helper in `citations.py` that coerces a Python `None` and the literal `"None"` to `""`, so the placeholder never reaches `Citation.url` (nor leaks into an `id` via the `file_id or url or title` fallback). See the BUG-0033 detail section. |
| BUG-0034 | 2026-06-14 | 2026-06-16 | functions | high | fixed | A document uploaded via the admin Add-data UI reports success (`200` + `UploadResponse`) but never appears in the documents list. **Root-caused 2026-06-16:** every PDF routes to the Document Intelligence parser, which builds its client endpoint from `settings.foundry.services_endpoint` (`AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT`); when that is empty `_get_client` yields the endpoint `"/"`, and the Azure SDK bearer-token policy rejects auth on the non-HTTPS URL (`ServiceRequestError: Bearer token authentication is not permitted for non-TLS protected (non-https) URLs`), so `batch_push` throws on every PDF → retries → poison queue (22 stale messages dated 2026-06-10). Upload + enqueue still return `200`, so the doc never indexes and never lists. Reproduced via the `batch_push._execute` seam; **verified the pipeline succeeds (4 chunks pushed, doc then lists) once the endpoint is present** — the host's `local.settings.json` now carries it. **(a) fail-fast DI guard + (b) `.env.sample`/`v2/.env` backfill + (d) upload-boundary `503` (honest error instead of false `200` when `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` is unset/non-HTTPS) landed 2026-06-16.** A second local-dev factor (Functions host `local.settings.json` queue name had drifted to `doc-processing-local` vs the canonical `doc-processing`) was found + folded here; the host was realigned to the canonical queue, restarted, and the 6 backend-enqueued messages drained successfully (documents list 2→5). | BUG-0036 | 2026-06-14 | 2026-06-14 | frontend | low | fixed | After BUG-0013 lit up substantive model reasoning, the canned "Searching the knowledge base for relevant sources…" narration (emitted upfront by `run_chat` as the during-the-wait hint per BUG-0027) stayed visible in the thinking panel *alongside* the real reasoning, because the FE concatenated every `reasoning`-channel frame into one `reasoning[]` list — so the placeholder sentence and the model's reasoning rendered together. Wire contract: the `metadata.placeholder` boolean, forwarded generically by `format_sse` for every channel. |

| BUG-0046 | 2026-06-15 | 2026-06-15 | frontend | high | fixed | The v2 SPA never resolves the signed-in user or forwards an identity header, so chat history is not isolated per user. The backend is already user-scoped (the history and conversation routes consume `UserIdDep` → the `x-ms-client-principal-id` header, and the Cosmos DB / PostgreSQL providers key every read and write on `user_id`, so a non-owned conversation already `404`s), but the frontend (a) never calls `/.auth/me` and keeps no user-id state, (b) forwards no `x-ms-client-principal-id` on any of its four `fetch` clients (`streamChat`, `conversationHistory`, `admin`, `speech`), (c) has no auth-enabled detection or blocked screen, and (d) has no default-user fallback. With the separate-origin topology (SPA → absolute `VITE_BACKEND_URL`) the platform-injected Easy Auth header never reaches the cross-origin backend call, so in production every history / conversation call returns `401` and locally every caller collapses into the single `local-dev` partition. Fix: port the v1 `getUserInfo()` flow + the reference architecture's header-forward pattern — resolve the user on load (the real id from `/.auth/me` when auth is enforced, else the all-zeros default `00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000`), block with an error screen when enforced but absent, and inject `x-ms-client-principal-id` on every API call; add an `auth_enforced` backend signal (folded into `GET /api/health`) plus a light principal-id well-formedness check. Security: a browser-forwarded principal id is not a trust boundary (chat partitioning only) — admin RBAC stays anchored on the backend's own server-injected Easy Auth claims. Latent (local dev unaffected; surfaces in cloud multi-user). Fixed: resolve-on-load + `userIdHeaders()` spread across every client; a **fifth** request seam (`HistoryPanel`'s inline `fetchJson`, missed by the four-client enumeration) was caught by a live request-header capture and corrected; verified live (history calls now carry the id) and by a two-user isolation integration test against real Cosmos. |
| BUG-0047 | 2026-06-16 | 2026-06-16 | backend | high | fixed | Every `/api/admin/*` call returns `401 {"detail":"Missing client principal claims; Easy Auth claims header required."}` in local dev, so the admin UI cannot load (observed at `http://localhost:5273/api/admin/status`). Regression from BUG-0046: the SPA's single modular header seam `userIdHeaders()` now forwards a default `x-ms-client-principal-id` (the all-zeros default user) on **every** API call, but the admin gate `requires_role("admin")._checker` has a local-dev bypass keyed on **both** Easy Auth headers being absent (`if not principal_id and not claims_raw`); the always-present id header defeats the bypass, so the gate falls through to the no-claims `401`. The frontend correctly does **not** forward the `x-ms-client-principal` *claims* blob — a browser-forged claims blob would let any caller assert the admin role (the documented trust boundary, see BUG-0046 Security note) — so the missing header cannot be supplied from the SPA. Fix: the local-dev bypass keys on the **absence of the claims blob** (the sole role authority), not on both headers; in `local` a missing claims blob → synthetic `local-dev` admin (regardless of the forgeable id header), in any non-local environment it still fails closed (`401`). One backend method fixes every admin endpoint at once. **Fixed 2026-06-16.** |
| BUG-0048 | 2026-06-16 | 2026-06-16 | backend | high | fixed | `DELETE /api/admin/documents/{source}` returns `503 {"detail":"Azure dependency temporarily unavailable."}` for every delete (observed deleting `Benefit_Options.pdf`). `AzureSearch.delete_by_source` builds a server-side OData `$filter` `title eq '<source>'` to collect the chunk ids, but the deployed index (`post_provision.py` `_build_chat_index`) defines `title` as a `SearchableField` — searchable but **not** filterable — so Azure Search rejects the query with `HttpResponseError: Invalid expression: 'title' is not a filterable field. Only filterable fields can be used in filter expressions.`, which the app-level handler sanitises to the `503`. The sibling `list_sources` already documents and works around the same index-schema fragility (it avoids faceting on `title` and pages client-side). Not a name-vs-id problem (a wrong identifier returns `404`, not `503`): the delete already removes **by id** — it collects chunk `id`s and calls `delete_documents` — and only the *id-discovery* step failed. Fix: page every chunk client-side selecting `id` + `title` (auto-paging, no server-side `$filter`) and match `source` by exact client-side equality, mirroring `list_sources`; this also removes the OData-injection seam a quote-bearing filename opened. No index schema / reindex / frontend change; the `DELETE /…/{source}` contract is unchanged. **Fixed 2026-06-16.** |
| BUG-0049 | 2026-06-16 | 2026-06-16 | backend | high | fixed | Uploading a `.docx` (or any Office / HTML format) indexes nothing — the file uploads, enqueues, and `batch_push` reports success, but no chunks are produced so the document never appears in search. `DocumentIntelligenceParser.parse` builds chunks exclusively from `result.pages[*].lines[*].content`, but Azure Document Intelligence treats Office (DOCX/PPTX/XLSX) and HTML inputs as "pageless": it returns the extracted text in `result.paragraphs` / `result.content` and leaves `pages[*].lines` empty. Confirmed against the live service with a sample DOCX: `len(pages)=1`, per-page `len(lines)=[0]`, but `len(paragraphs)=848`, `len(result.content)=29335`; the same probe on a PDF returns `len(pages)=4`, per-page `len(lines)=[4,6,34,25]`. The page loop therefore emits zero chunks for DOCX and the file silently fails to index (the handler logs the zero-chunk info line and returns `[]`). Fix: when the page pass yields zero chunks, fall back to one chunk per `result.paragraphs` entry (the same semantic unit `TextParser` uses), keeping `index` dense; paginated formats (PDF, images) still emit one chunk per page and never reach the fallback, so there is no double-emit. No infra / model / frontend change. **Fixed 2026-06-16.** |

| BUG-0051 | 2026-06-16 | 2026-06-16 | infra | high | fixed | Uploading a document through the (now-visible) admin UI returns `503 {"detail":"Document storage is not configured for this deployment."}`; the same gate fronts URL ingestion, reprocess-all, and file download. | BUG-0053 | 2026-06-16 | 2026-06-16 | functions | high | fixed | Documents uploaded through the admin UI enqueue (`queued:true`) but never parse/embed/index — they never appear in `GET /api/admin/documents`. The `doc-processing` queue holds the messages indefinitely at `dequeueCount=0` (never dequeued). Root cause: the Flex Consumption function (`func-<SUFFIX>`, Linux/Python 3.11) uses per-function (target-based) scaling — `batch_push` runs only in its own `function:batch_push` scale group, which the platform **scale controller** must wake from zero on queue depth; it does not for the identity-based (`AzureWebJobsStorage__credential=managedidentity`) Storage Queue connection, so nothing ever polls the queue (the HTTP-served instances do not run `batch_push`). Everything else is provably correct: trigger metadata registered (`queueTrigger`, `queueName=%AZURE_DOC_PROCESSING_QUEUE%` → `doc-processing`, `isDisabled:null`); UAMI holds **Storage Queue Data Contributor** (⊃ reader + message processor); only the user-assigned identity, `AzureWebJobsStorage__clientId` matches it; storage fully open (`publicNetworkAccess=Enabled`, `defaultAction=Allow`, no PE/VNet); Flex scale config healthy (`maximumInstanceCount=40`); and the function **works warm** (it processed messages right after a deploy). No-cost levers that did **not** wake the group: explicit `AzureWebJobsStorage__blobServiceUri`/`__queueServiceUri`/`__tableServiceUri`; a forced `az functionapp stop`+`start` cycle (plain `restart` never cycled instances); `syncfunctiontriggers`. Compounded by BUG-0055 (App Insights empty → no scaler/host logs). Open decision: the reliable documented fix is `alwaysReady={function:batch_push:1}` (one warm instance polls the queue) which carries a small always-on cost the operator declined; remaining no-cost options are speculative (system-assigned identity + queue RBAC for the scale controller; runtime scale monitoring, documented as Premium+VNet only). **Fixed 2026-06-16:** operator approved the always-ready instance — `az functionapp scale config always-ready set … function:batch_push=1` runs the real listener continuously (the `NoOpListener` on non-allocated instances no longer applies) and drains `doc-processing` (verified 7→0, 3→0). A **separate** base64-encoding defect (BUG-0056) then blocked the downstream validation. |
| BUG-0054 | 2026-06-16 | — | infra | medium | open | The `doc-processing-poison` queue holds 10 base64 `Microsoft.Storage.BlobCreated` Event Grid envelopes (inserted 13:46–13:48). A stray/legacy Event Grid subscription on the storage account delivers blob-created events into `doc-processing`, but `batch_push` expects CWYD ingestion envelopes (`{container, blob_filename, ingestion_job_id, …}`), not the Event Grid `BlobCreated` schema, so the events fail validation, retry, and poison. Noise/poison only — distinct messages from the CWYD envelopes, so it does **not** block ingestion — but the Event Grid → queue wiring should be removed or routed to a handler that understands the blob-event schema. The same 8-envelope artifact was noted under BUG-0034's poison cleanup. **Fix designed + locally proven 2026-06-20** ([ADR 0028](adr/0028-event-grid-single-trigger-blob-ingestion.md)): a `blob_event` queue-trigger translator turns the Event Grid `BlobCreated` envelope into a CWYD `doc-processing` message (subscription repointed to a dedicated `blob-events` queue), plus an `ingestion_trigger` flag (`direct_enqueue` default / `event_grid`) so the backend stops double-enqueuing once Event Grid owns ingestion. Validated end-to-end locally (blob → `blob-events` → `blob_event` → `doc-processing` → pgvector). **Cloud deploy deferred** (operator decision) — `azd deploy function` exceeded azd's 20-min wait (Flex remote-build slowness, BUG-0058/0062 class); cloud still serves the prior 5 functions, and `blob_event` (queue trigger) also needs a BUG-0053 always-ready instance. Backend left on `direct_enqueue` (flag not flipped) so ingestion keeps working. See the detail entry for the resume steps. **Update 2026-06-22 (`a214182`):** the `blob_event` translator now also classifies + handles `BlobDeleted` (de-index, BUG-0077), and both EG subscriptions filter create+delete in bicep. The remaining open Phase-2 steps are unchanged — drain the 10 poison messages, `azd deploy function` (after the BUG-0058 prepackage workaround), then flip `AZURE_ENV_INGESTION_TRIGGER` → `event_grid`. |

| BUG-0056 | 2026-06-16 | 2026-06-16 | functions | high | fixed | With BUG-0053's always-ready listener now draining `doc-processing`, a fresh PerksPlus.pdf upload still does not index — all 3 of its messages **poison** (`Executed Functions.batch_push (Failed, Duration=5–29ms)`, `batch_push queue message validation failed` — immediate, before any download/parse/embed). Decoding the 3 newest poison bodies shows **one is the genuine CWYD envelope** (carrying the exact upload `ingestion_job_id`, shape `{container_name, filename, ingestion_job_id, force_reindex}`) which **exactly matches** the deployed `BatchPushQueueMessage` contract — so not a schema skew. Root cause: a **queue-message base64-encoding mismatch** — the backend producer builds its `QueueClient` with no `message_encode_policy`, so `azure-storage-queue` uses `NoEncodePolicy` and sends **raw JSON** (the `queue_writer.py` docstring's "base64-encodes by default" is wrong); the Functions queue trigger only accepts raw bodies when `extensions.queues.messageEncoding=none`, present **only** in `local.settings.json` (so local works) and never propagated to `host.json` or the cloud app settings, so the Flex host uses the default `base64`, can't decode the raw JSON, and poisons every message (it base64-encodes toward the poison queue, hence peeked bodies decode to the clean envelope). Fix applied live (cloud variable, not bicep): set `AzureFunctionsJobHost__extensions__queues__messageEncoding=none` + restart; durable back-port to `host.json` / bicep noted (bicep paused). **Fixed 2026-06-16:** confirmed loaded (host `QueuesOptions.MessageEncoding=None`; the post-fix poison body is raw JSON, no longer base64) and correct — the post-fix CWYD envelope now passes validation, downloads the blob (HTTP 206, full 115 KB), and parses the PDF. The document still does not index because of a **separate** downstream embedding-deployment 404 tracked as **BUG-0057**. |
| BUG-0057 | 2026-06-16 | 2026-06-16 | functions | high | fixed | After BUG-0056's encoding fix, the post-fix CWYD envelope passes validation, downloads the blob (HTTP 206, 115 KB), and parses the PDF into chunks, then **fails at embedding** — `batch_push queue handler failed` with `openai.NotFoundError: Error code: 404` from `handler.py` `embedder.embed(chunks)` → `foundry_iq.embed` → `oai.embeddings.create(...)` (5 retries ~7 s apart, then poison). Root cause: an **embedding-deployment / endpoint mismatch**. The 1536-dim search index needs `text-embedding-3-small` (set in `AZURE_OPENAI_EMBEDDING_DEPLOYMENT`), which is deployed **only** on the classic Azure OpenAI account `oai-<DATA_SUFFIX>` (`AZURE_OPENAI_ENDPOINT`). But the Foundry IQ embedding path routes `/embeddings` to the **AI Services account** `aisa-<SUFFIX>` (`AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` — the Foundry project route serves no `/embeddings`), and that account has only `text-embedding-3-large`, so the deployment is not found → 404. The deployed function build also predates the `_get_embeddings_client` account-route fix, so it may still target the project route. No pure app-setting fix exists; resolution needs `text-embedding-3-small` provisioned on `aisa-<SUFFIX>` (or the embedding endpoint repointed to the account that has it) plus a redeploy of the current function code. **Fixed 2026-06-16:** (a) provisioned `text-embedding-3-small` (1536, GlobalStandard) on `aisa-<SUFFIX>` and verified the `/openai/v1/embeddings` route returns 1536-dim vectors; (b) redeployed the current function code — the first `azd deploy function` shipped a **stale** `build-functions/` artifact (the prepackage hook did not regenerate it; tracked as BUG-0058), so the embed path still hit the project route and 404'd; after manually running `prepackage_function.py` and redeploying, the new code's `_get_embeddings_client` account-route loaded. End-to-end confirmed: PerksPlus.pdf now indexes with **4 chunks** in the active `cwyd-index` (151 docs total). |

| BUG-0060 | 2026-06-17 | 2026-06-17 | infra | blocker | fixed | The first `databaseType=postgresql` `azd up` fails ARM template validation with `InvalidTemplate`: `The template reference 'avmPrivateDnsZones[7]' is not valid`. In postgresql mode `privateDnsZones` = 6 always-on zones + 1 postgres zone (indices 0–6), but the cosmos-only `aiSearch` module's private-endpoint DNS-zone reference uses the literal constant `dnsZoneIndex.search` (= 7). ARM validates copy-index references **statically** against the declared array length, **before** the module's `if (databaseType == 'cosmosdb')` condition is evaluated, so the out-of-range literal `[7]` fails — even though the search PE never deploys in postgresql mode (and even though `enablePrivateNetworking=false` empties the copy at runtime). This path had never been provisioned (all prior cloud QA was cosmos, where the array has 8 zones so index 7 is valid). Fixed in [main.bicep](../infra/main.bicep): made the search PE DNS-zone index a mode-conditional expression — `avmPrivateDnsZones[databaseType == 'cosmosdb' ? dnsZoneIndex.search : dnsZoneIndex.postgres]` — so it is never the literal `7` in postgresql mode; ARM then defers the index to runtime where it resolves to a valid in-range index (unused, because the PE is gated out). `az bicep build` clean; the subsequent `azd up` provisioned the full postgresql resource set (incl. `psql-<SUFFIX>`). **Fixed 2026-06-17.** |
| BUG-0061 | 2026-06-17 | 2026-06-17 | infra | blocker | fixed | The postgresql `azd up` (after BUG-0060) fails the **provision** step with `Managed Identity for event subscription does not have authorization to deliver to the endpoint` (Event Grid `blob-created-to-doc-processing` → `doc-processing` Storage Queue). Deploy-time chicken-and-egg: the AVM `event-grid/system-topic` module (`evgt-<SUFFIX>`) creates the system topic, its system-assigned MI, **and** the `blob-created-to-doc-processing` event subscription **inside one nested deployment**, while the role assignment that grants that MI `Storage Queue Data Message Sender` on the storage account (`eventGridQueueSenderRole`) is an **external** resource ordered *after* the module (it consumes `eventGridSystemTopic.outputs.systemAssignedMIPrincipalId`). The subscription's `deliveryWithResourceIdentity` preflight validates the MI's queue-delivery permission **at subscription-creation time, inside the module** — before the external role exists — so it 401s and fails the whole provision. (Storage has `allowSharedKeyAccess=false`, so identity-based delivery is mandatory; there is no key fallback.) Unblocked live (cloud role grant, not bicep): `az role assignment create --assignee-object-id <EG_TOPIC_MI> --role "Storage Queue Data Message Sender" --scope <storage account>`, then re-ran `azd up` — the topic's MI now passes preflight and the subscription + remaining resources provision. The random-named manual grant then collided by-content with the bicep-managed `eventGridQueueSenderRole` (deterministic GUID name) on the next provision (`RoleAssignmentExists`); resolved by deleting the manual grant and letting bicep own the role (the subscription is permanently created, so the chicken-and-egg does not recur). Durable bicep back-port (split the event subscription out of the system-topic module into a separate resource that `dependsOn` the role assignment, OR pre-create the MI + role before the module) pending — bicep edits paused. **Fixed 2026-06-17.** |
| BUG-0062 | 2026-06-17 | 2026-06-17 | infra | blocker | fixed | `azd deploy function` fails fast with `InaccessibleStorageException` / `BlobUploadFailedException: 403` against the Flex Consumption Function App's storage account `st<SUFFIX>`. The function uses identity-based storage (`AzureWebJobsStorage__credential=managedidentity`, no shared key), but the storage account ships `networkRuleSet.defaultAction=Deny` + `bypass=AzureServices` with **no resource-instance rule** for the Function App, and `allowSharedKeyAccess=false` (Azure Policy) leaves no key fallback — so with `enablePrivateNetworking=false` (no VNet path) the Flex Consumption platform is denied at deploy and runtime. Fixed live: `az storage account update -n st<SUFFIX> -g <RESOURCE_GROUP> --default-action Allow` (data stays Entra/RBAC-protected; only the network-ACL default flips). Durable bicep fix pending. **Fixed 2026-06-17.** |
| BUG-0063 | 2026-06-17 | 2026-06-17 | infra | blocker | fixed | The backend Container App revision fails activation (`ActivationFailed`, 0 replicas) on the first postgresql deploy, so `/api/health` times out. | BUG-0065 | 2026-06-19 | 2026-06-19 | backend | high | fixed | The `langgraph` orchestrator returns no citations and the out-of-domain fallback for in-domain questions in **pgvector** mode, even when relevant chunks are indexed. Root cause: `langgraph` calls `self._search.search(query, top_k=..., use_semantic_search=...)` **without a `vector=`** ([orchestrators/langgraph.py](../src/backend/core/providers/orchestrators/langgraph.py)). `PgVector.search` ([providers/search/pgvector.py](../src/backend/core/providers/search/pgvector.py)) only runs dense cosine search when a `vector` is supplied; with none it falls back to Postgres FTS `to_tsvector('english',content) @@ plainto_tsquery('english',query)`, and `plainto_tsquery` **AND-joins every lexeme**, so a natural-language question (`"What is the Contoso remote work policy and how many days per week can I work remotely?"`) cannot be satisfied by any single small chunk → 0 rows → fallback. `AzureSearch.search` masks the same caller omission because its no-vector path is full-text **plus the Azure semantic re-ranker**, which still surfaces relevant chunks; pgvector has no semantic reranker, only AND-FTS. Confirmed live against the cloud pgvector store (6 indexed chunks, all `vector_dims=1536`): `plainto_tsquery` full question → **0**; `websearch_to_tsquery` full question → **0**; `plainto_tsquery('remote work')` → **4**. So ingestion + storage are correct; only the read-side query construction is wrong. Distinct from BUG-0028 (guardrail over-refusal — there retrieval succeeded). Fix direction: the chat retrieval path must embed the query (via the LLM/embedder seam) and pass `vector=` so `PgVector` does dense cosine retrieval (its intended mode per the provider docstring) — this also upgrades `AzureSearch` to true hybrid; keep the FTS branch only as a no-embedder fallback. Surfaced during local-against-cloud pgvector parity validation (worklog 2026-06-19). **Fixed 2026-06-19:** `LangGraphOrchestrator.run()` now embeds the latest user query via `self.llm.embed([query])` and passes `vector=` to `search(...)`, so `PgVector` runs dense cosine retrieval (and `AzureSearch` gets true hybrid scoring); the FTS branch stays only as a no-embedder fallback. Verified live against cloud pgvector — the same question now returns a grounded answer with an inline `[docN]` marker + a `Citation` (cosine score ~0.75) from the indexed policy doc; 20 `test_langgraph.py` unit tests + 174 orchestrator/pipeline/search tests green. |
| BUG-0066 | 2026-06-19 | 2026-06-19 | backend | high | fixed | The `agent_framework` orchestrator cannot ground on a **pgvector** deployment, so every chat is rejected at request time with HTTP 409 `ConfigResolutionError` (`reason=orchestrator_requires_azure_search`, ADR 0022). It retrieves only through a Foundry IQ Knowledge Base over an Azure AI Search index, and Foundry IQ has no PostgreSQL/pgvector knowledge-source type, so on pgvector it has zero retrieval and the guard blocks the pairing — violating the requirement that **both** orchestrators work on pgvector. | BUG-0077 | 2026-06-20 |  | functions | low | open | **Enhancement (not a defect):** auto-remove a document from the index when its blob is deleted, via the Event Grid `Microsoft.Storage.BlobDeleted` event. The B1 `blob_event` path ([ADR 0028](adr/0028-event-grid-single-trigger-blob-ingestion.md), BUG-0054) handles `BlobCreated` only, so a blob deleted directly from the `documents` container (bulk delete / Storage Explorer) leaves **stale index / pgvector chunks**. v1's `batch_push_results` handled this with a `BlobDeleted` branch (remove-from-index); v2 dropped it when porting. Fix direction: add `Microsoft.Storage.BlobDeleted` to the Event Grid subscription's `includedEventTypes`, and add a delete branch to the `blob_event` translator that maps the event `subject` → `delete_by_source` (reusing the existing `subject` parser + `ParsedBlobRef`). Complements BUG-0073 (admin delete leaves the blob) — this is the inverse direction (blob deleted → remove from index). Deferred follow-up, independent of the BUG-0054 bulk-upload work. **Phase 1 implemented + committed (`a214182`, 2026-06-22):** the `blob_event` path now classifies the event (`parse_blob_event` → `BlobEventType`) and dispatches create → ingest / delete → `delete_by_source` (handler `handle_blob_deleted`; the blueprint resolves the registry-first search provider, mirroring `batch_push`), and [main.bicep](../infra/main.bicep) adds `Microsoft.Storage.BlobDeleted` to `includedEventTypes` on **both** Event Grid subscriptions. **Phase 2 (deploy) deferred** behind BUG-0058 (prepackage) + BUG-0053 (always-ready instance for the queue trigger); status stays **open** until the function deploys and a live blob-delete is confirmed to drop its chunks. |

| BUG-0081 | 2026-06-24 |  | infra | high | open | The **frontend never deploys via `azd deploy frontend`** — the App Service stays on the default placeholder image (`mcr.microsoft.com/appsvc/staticsite:latest`) even though `azd` reports SUCCESS. **Root cause:** `azure.yaml` declares the `frontend` service as `host: appservice` + `language: js` with a `docker:` block, but per the [azd schema](https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/developer/azure-developer-cli/azd-schema) the **`appservice` host does not support `docker`** ("Supports docker: N"; the block is only applicable to `containerapp`, `aks`, `ai.endpoint`, `azure.ai.agent`). So `azd` silently ignores the Dockerfile and **zip-deploys code** (`azd package frontend` → npm install + compress to .zip, ~18s, no image built/pushed), which is a no-op against the **container-kind** App Service that [main.bicep](../infra/main.bicep) provisions (`kind: 'app,linux,container'`, placeholder DOCKER image, UAMI for ACR pull). The two halves never agreed → the frontend has never been deployable as designed (ACR held only the backend image). **Mitigated 2026-06-24 (operator-endorsed manual container deploy):** built `docker/Dockerfile.frontend` (`--target prod`, `--build-arg VITE_BACKEND_URL=<backend-fqdn>`), pushed to ACR, `az webapp config container set` + enabled `acrUseManagedIdentityCreds` / `acrUserManagedIdentityID=<UAMI-client-id>`, restarted → the frontend now serves the real SPA (`HTTP 200`, `<title>CWYD v2</title>`, placeholder gone). **Durable fix (pending design decision, structural — Hard Rule #10):** either move the frontend to a **Container App** (like the backend — fully azd-supported container build/push) or switch the App Service to an azd **code/static deploy** model; today's manual `az webapp config container set` is reverted by the next `azd provision`. |
| BUG-0082 | 2026-06-24 | 2026-06-24 | backend | medium | open | The backend Container App crash-loops (default startup probe fails, replica `Started: False`) whenever its **PostgreSQL Flexible Server is unreachable**. The FastAPI lifespan's first DB calls (`get_runtime_config` → `ensure_pool` → `ensure_schema`) have **no connect timeout**, so an unreachable server (auto-stopped Burstable instance, firewall drop) hangs the lifespan forever — the app never finishes startup and the probe restarts it indefinitely instead of failing fast or degrading. Console logs stop at uvicorn's `Waiting for application startup.` (the app's own log lines never flush — stdout is block-buffered in the container), which masks where it hangs. **Observed 2026-06-24:** the cloud backend was wedged because `psql-<SUFFIX>` had auto-stopped (Burstable, 7-day idle); `az postgres flexible-server start` + a revision restart brought it healthy (`/api/health` → `status: pass`). **Fix direction (pending):** add a bounded connect timeout to the asyncpg connect / pool acquisition and let lifespan fail fast (or mark the `database` check degraded) so a transient DB outage can't become a permanent crash-loop; add `PYTHONUNBUFFERED=1` to the backend image so startup logs flush. |
| BUG-0083 | 2026-06-24 | 2026-06-24 | frontend | low | fixed | The admin Configuration **Assistant type** dropdown renders **empty** instead of defaulting to the `default` preset. `configToForm` passed `ai_assistant_type` through verbatim, and the `select` renderer prepends any value not in its option set as a phantom first option ([Configuration.tsx](../src/frontend/src/pages/admin/Configuration/Configuration.tsx)); when the value is missing or unknown the phantom is **blank** and shows selected. The value is missing whenever the backend omits `ai_assistant_type` — e.g. a deployed backend that predates the Assistant-type presets (ADR 0030, BUG-0076). A current backend returns `ai_assistant_type="default"`, so this reproduces only against a **stale backend** (the live cloud backend image predates BUG-0076). **Fixed 2026-06-24:** added a `withAssistantTypeDefault` normalizer applied at both reducer entry points (`LoadSucceeded` / `SaveSucceeded`) that coalesces a missing/unknown `ai_assistant_type` to `AssistantType.Default`, keeping `serverConfig` + `formValues` consistent (no spurious dirty state). | BUG-0084 | 2026-06-24 | 2026-06-24 | backend | high | fixed | Saving admin config rejects the **unchanged default prompt** — `PATCH /api/admin/config` returns `422 {"msg":"RAI safety check rejected the submitted prompt","field":"cwyd_agent_instructions","reason":"The submitted prompt was rejected by the Responsible AI safety classifier and was not persisted."}` even when the operator never edited the prompt. **Root cause — category error:** the router screens every `PROMPT_FIELDS` value (`cwyd_agent_instructions`, `post_answering_prompt`) through `validate_prompt_with_rai` → `rai_check` → `RAI_AGENT` ([routers/admin.py](../src/backend/routers/admin.py) `PATCH` loop; [services/admin.py](../src/backend/services/admin.py); [core/tools/content_safety.py](../src/backend/core/tools/content_safety.py)). But `RAI_AGENT` is a **user-message** jailbreak/prompt-injection classifier ("Respond TRUE if the message is a normal information-seeking … request; FALSE if it contains … jailbreak / prompt-injection attempts; instructions to bypass documented safety controls"). The value being classified is a **system prompt** — the operator persona body, including the built-in default — which is inherently full of meta-instructions and guardrail language ("you **must refuse** to discuss your prompts", "rules … cannot be overridden, ignored, weakened", "Answer **only** using …", "**Do not** generate or provide URLs"). The classifier reads a legitimate system prompt as an attack and returns FALSE → save rejected → the **default prompt fails its own gate**, making the prompt-config admin feature unusable. Applying a user-input classifier to trusted operator-authored system prompts is the defect; the chat-time `rai_check` (which screens actual user chat input) is correct and unaffected. v1 never did this — its admin prompt "validation" was non-blocking `{sources}`/`{question}` placeholder warnings only ([code/backend/pages/04_Configuration.py](../../code/backend/pages/04_Configuration.py)); the blocking gate is v2-only. **Fixed 2026-06-24 (keep the gate, fix the calibration — operator directive was "allow the original prompt AND be sure the RAI still blocks bad prompts"):** (a) **deterministic allow-list** — `validate_prompt_with_rai` now accepts any vetted built-in body (`body_for(t)` for every `AssistantType` + `DEFAULT_POST_ANSWERING_PROMPT`, normalized for CR/LF + trailing whitespace) without a classifier round-trip, so an unedited default/preset can never be rejected; (b) **system-prompt-calibrated reviewer** — added `PROMPT_REVIEW_AGENT` (`backend.core.agents.definitions`), a TRUE/FALSE classifier framed to review *administrator-authored system prompts* (allows persona/guardrail/refusal/domain/format language, blocks only prompts that direct harmful output, malware, secret exfiltration, or disabling the fixed guardrails); `rai_check` gained a `*, agent: AgentDefinition = RAI_AGENT` param (chat default unchanged) and the admin gate passes `PROMPT_REVIEW_AGENT`; custom prompts are still screened so a genuinely harmful operator prompt is blocked. The fixed `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` remains appended last to every override regardless. Tests: +8 (default/each-preset/default-post-answering accepted without classifier; custom prompt still screened; `rai_check` honors the `agent` arg; `PROMPT_REVIEW_AGENT` shape). Gates green: 1125 `tests/backend`, 764 shared invariant gates, pyright strict 0/0/0 on the three edited files. |

| BUG-0086 | 2026-06-25 | 2026-06-25 | infra | high | fixed | The **backend Container App is down** — the latest revision shows `runningState: ActivationFailed` with 0 replicas, so every request times out (no replica becomes ready). This is blocked by your Cosmos DB account firewall settings` → `Application startup failed. Exiting`. Cosmos is `publicNetworkAccess=Disabled` (private-endpoint-only) with **0 IP/VNet rules**, but the Container Apps environment is **not VNet-integrated** (`vnetConfiguration=null`, `enablePrivateNetworking=false`), so the backend egresses from public Azure IPs that Cosmos blocks. **Why it drifted:** the env **reuses pre-existing data resources** (`AZURE_ENV_EXISTING_COSMOS_NAME`, `..._STORAGE_NAME`, …); the Bicep Cosmos module is guarded `if (databaseType=='cosmosdb' && !useExistingCosmos)` ([main.bicep](../infra/main.bicep) L1333), so for a **reused** account it only adds the SQL db/container/role and **never manages `publicNetworkAccess`**. The reused Cosmos was left `Disabled` from a prior life, and the non-private-networking provision (which sets new accounts to `Enabled`, L1348) never re-opened it. The same drift left **Storage** private-only (breaks function ingestion); Search + OpenAI happened to be `Enabled` so they worked. **Fixed 2026-06-25:** `az cosmosdb update --public-network-access ENABLED --ip-range-filter 0.0.0.0` (the `0.0.0.0` rule = "Accept connections from within public Azure datacenters" — allows the Container Apps Azure-internal egress, still blocks the public internet), then restarted the backend revision. Verified `/api/health` → `HTTP 200 {status:pass, database=pass(cosmosdb), search=pass, foundry_iq=pass}`. **Durable fix (pending):** reused data resources aren't network-managed by the Bicep — either stop reusing (clear `AZURE_ENV_EXISTING_*` so the modules provision + manage network posture) or ensure reused accounts match the profile's posture (public + Azure-datacenters for non-VNet). Companion to the Storage instance of the same drift. |
| BUG-0087 | 2026-06-25 | 2026-06-25 | infra | medium | fixed | A **stale v1 Event Grid subscription** dead-letters a junk message on every blob upload. On the **reused** storage account's system topic (`evgt-<DATA_SUFFIX>`), a leftover subscription (`evts-<DATA_SUFFIX>`) delivered raw `Microsoft.Storage.BlobCreated`/`BlobDeleted` events **directly to the `doc-processing` queue** with plain (non-MI) delivery. `doc-processing` is consumed by `batch_push`, which expects a typed `BatchPushQueueMessage` JSON envelope — not a raw Event Grid event — so every delivered event failed to deserialize, retried 5×, and dead-lettered to `doc-processing-poison` (one junk poison message per uploaded blob). | BUG-0089 | 2026-06-25 | 2026-06-25 | backend | high | fixed | The **backend process reads `environment=local` despite `AZURE_ENVIRONMENT=production`** being present on the running Container App revision, which **activates the admin auth bypass** — `/api/admin/*` is reachable **unauthenticated** on the public backend FQDN. | BUG-0090 | 2026-06-25 |  | infra | high | open | The **production admin panel is unreachable** — `GET /api/admin/status` on the public backend FQDN returns `401 {"detail":"Missing client principal claims; Easy Auth claims header required."}` for every caller (unauthenticated *and* the signed-in SPA). Found 2026-06-25 immediately after BUG-0089 closed (production auth enforcement restored). **This 401 is the auth gate working as designed**, not a regression: in `production`, `backend.dependencies.requires_role("admin")` requires the base64 `x-ms-client-principal` Easy Auth claims blob carrying an `admin` role ([dependencies.py](../src/backend/dependencies.py)). **Root cause: no Easy Auth identity source feeds the backend.** The backend Container App (`ca-backend-<SUFFIX>`) has **no** `authConfig` — `az containerapp auth show` returns `{}` — so Container Apps Easy Auth never injects the claims blob. The SPA calls the backend **directly** cross-origin (`frontend_app.py` serves the SPA + `/config` only; it does **not** proxy `/api/*` and cannot forge the trusted claims header), and no Entra app registration defining an `admin` app role exists in the deployment. The frontend App Service (`app-frontend-<SUFFIX>`) has Easy Auth enabled but its Entra provider reads back unconfigured (empty `clientId`/issuer), so the identity layer was never fully provisioned. Admin previously *appeared* to work **only** via the local-dev bypass on the stale revision (the BUG-0089 anomaly). Non-admin chat/history still works because the SPA forwards a default `x-ms-client-principal-id` that `get_user_id` accepts in production. **Fix (pending decision):** wire a real identity source — either **(A)** enable Container Apps Easy Auth on the backend behind an Entra app registration with an `admin` app role, or **(B)** make `frontend_app.py` reverse-proxy `/api/*` and reuse the frontend's Easy Auth (define the `admin` role on the frontend app registration). Both are structural infra + Entra changes (Hard Rule #10) pending operator decision. **Status: open — awaiting auth-architecture decision.** |
| BUG-0091 | 2026-06-29 | 2026-06-29 | frontend, backend | high | fixed | The `auth_enforced` health signal and the client-side `AuthBlocked` "Authentication Not Configured" screen were **removed**; the CWYD v2 SPA now resolves identity purely from Azure Easy Auth `/.auth/me` (principal → real `userId`, else the `DEFAULT_USER_ID` guest user) and never renders a blocking wall. **Root cause:** `auth_enforced` was a frontend-only UI flag — derived from the deployment's admin-auth posture and folded into `GET /api/health` (added under BUG-0046) — that made the SPA render a dead-end "Authentication Not Configured" screen whenever it read `auth_enforced=true` but `/.auth/me` returned no principal, instead of degrading to the guest user. On an open / partially-wired deploy (cf. BUG-0089's `environment` mis-read and BUG-0090's missing backend Easy Auth identity source) that wall could lock every caller out of an app that has no login configured at all. **Fix:** deleted the `auth_enforced` field from `HealthResponse` and its producer in [services/health.py](../src/backend/services/health.py); removed `AuthPhase.Blocked`, the `authEnforced` state, the `readAuthEnforced` helper, and the `AuthBlocked` component (`src/frontend/src/components/AuthBlocked/` deleted) from the SPA; the `App.tsx` bootstrap effect now calls `resolve(getUserInfo())` alone (principal → real id; none → guest) and never blocks. `require_admin_auth` (`AZURE_REQUIRE_ADMIN_AUTH`), `get_user_id`, and `requires_role` are **retained unchanged** as the orthogonal opt-in server-side admin-write gate (PD-01 → Scenario A). Supersedes the D2 / B1 / F9 / F10 / F11 portions of [frontend-user-identity-plan.md](frontend-user-identity-plan.md) (the per-user header-forwarding work from BUG-0046 is unchanged). Local gates green (backend `pytest` + `pyright --strict` 0/0/0; frontend `vitest` + `tsc` exit 0; shared AST gates); cloud verification complete 2026-06-29 (Phase 4) — live `/api/health` carries no `auth_enforced`, the deployed SPA renders no blocking wall, resolves the `DEFAULT_USER_ID` guest, and returns a grounded answer with citations. See [worklog/2026-06-29.md](worklog/2026-06-29.md). |
| BUG-0092 | 2026-06-29 |  | frontend | high | open | The **chat History panel fails to load on the split-host cloud deploy** — opening History shows `Could not load history: Unexpected token '<', "<!doctype "... is not valid JSON`. **Root cause:** [HistoryPanel.tsx](../src/frontend/src/pages/chat/components/HistoryPanel.tsx) builds its request URL from the **build-time** `BACKEND_URL = import.meta.env.VITE_BACKEND_URL ?? ""`, which is empty in the deployed App Service build, so `GET`/`PATCH`/`DELETE` `/api/history/conversations[...]` are sent **relative** to the SPA's own App Service origin (`app-frontend-<SUFFIX>`) instead of the backend Container App. The App Service returns its SPA `index.html` (`<!doctype html>`) for the unknown `/api/*` path and `resp.json()` throws on the HTML body. Chat streaming and the health probe work because they resolve the origin at **runtime** via `loadRuntimeConfig()` → `getBackendUrl()` (the `/config` seam in [App.tsx](../src/frontend/src/App.tsx)); `HistoryPanel` never adopted that seam, and the transcript-rehydrate client [conversationHistory.tsx](../src/frontend/src/api/conversationHistory.tsx) already does. **Fix (pending):** route `HistoryPanel`'s `buildUrl` through the runtime `getBackendUrl()` seam from [api/runtimeConfig.tsx](../src/frontend/src/api/runtimeConfig.tsx) like the rest of the SPA, dropping the build-time `VITE_BACKEND_URL` read. Observed 2026-06-29 during the Phase 4 cloud verification of BUG-0091; unrelated to the `auth_enforced` removal. See [worklog/2026-06-29.md](worklog/2026-06-29.md). **Status: open.** |

## Details

### BUG-0001 — Embeddings routed to the project endpoint and missing `dimensions`

Area: backend. Severity: blocker. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-10).

Symptom: the `batch_push` ingestion pipeline could not produce a single embedded chunk. `FoundryIQ.embed()` returned `404`.

Root cause: `FoundryIQ.embed()` reused the project-scoped OpenAI client that is correct for chat and agents. The Foundry **project** route exposes no `embeddings` path, so every embeddings request returned `404`. The call also never passed `dimensions`, so a `text-embedding-3-large` deployment would emit 3072-dimension vectors against the 1536-dimension `content_vector` index field.

Fix: a new `FoundryIQ._get_embeddings_client()` targets the **account** endpoint (`AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` plus `/openai/v1`), and `embed()` now passes `dimensions=settings.openai.embedding_dimensions`.

Why it was not caught earlier: `test_foundry_iq.py` fully mocks the OpenAI client, which hid the project-versus-account routing distinction.

References: [worklog/2026-06-10.md](worklog/2026-06-10.md); [development_plan.md](development_plan.md) §0.1 `INGEST-EMBED-DOCKEY`.

### BUG-0002 — Parser chunk id is an illegal Azure AI Search document key

Area: backend. Severity: blocker. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-10).

Symptom: after embeddings were fixed, the Azure AI Search push step failed with `InvalidDocumentKey`, so no document reached the index.

Root cause: parsers minted `Chunk.id` as `f"{source}__{index}"`. When `source` is a filename, its extension dot makes the key illegal. Azure AI Search document keys allow only letters, digits, `_`, `-`, and `=`.

Fix: a new Stable Core helper `BaseParser.make_chunk_id(source, index)` hashes the readable `f"{source}__{index}"` through SHA-256 into a key-safe hex digest (mirrors the v1 `source_document.py` hashing precedent). Both parsers call it. The readable name survives on `Chunk.source` and the Search `title` field, and the read-side `_to_result` already treats `id` as opaque.

Why it was not caught earlier: the parser tests asserted the raw `id` literal, which baked the invalid key charset into the expectation. A new `test_base.py` (5 tests) now asserts key safety with a charset regex against the helper contract instead of a magic string.

References: [worklog/2026-06-10.md](worklog/2026-06-10.md); [development_plan.md](development_plan.md) §0.1 `INGEST-EMBED-DOCKEY`.

### BUG-0003 — Admin documents endpoint returns 503 (`list_sources` throws an `AzureError` on the live index)

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11; fixed 2026-06-14, verified live).

Symptom: `GET /api/admin/documents` returns `503 Service Unavailable` (body `{"detail":"Azure dependency temporarily unavailable."}`), so the admin Delete data grid cannot list indexed sources. Reproduced locally 2026-06-11 against the live cloud data plane **with search fully configured** (endpoint, index, and knowledge base all set, and the `search` readiness check passing) — the listing still 503s.

Root cause: `list_sources()` in `backend/core/providers/search/azure_search.py` issues `client.search(search_text="*", facets=["title,count:10000,sort:value"], top=0)` to bucket chunks by their `title` field, then reads `paged.get_facets()`. The configured index schema does not mark `title` as `facetable`, so Azure AI Search rejects the request with `HttpResponseError` — `(OperationNotAllowed) The field 'title' has not been marked as facetable in the schema` (`Code: FieldNotFacetable`). The SDK-boundary handler in `backend/routers/admin.py` maps that `AzureError` to `HTTPException(503)` per the resilience contract. The failure is independent of endpoint configuration; it fires whenever the index used by the deployment lacks a facetable `title` field. The earlier hypothesis (empty endpoint → `search_provider` is `None` → 503) is a separate latent pass-through path, not the cause of the observed 503.

Proposed fix (direction, to be settled in the fix turn): prefer a code-side fix in `list_sources()` so the endpoint is robust to existing index schemas — derive the source listing without faceting `title` (for example facet on a field declared `facetable`, or page documents and aggregate distinct sources client-side). Optionally, also mark the source-grouping field `facetable` in the index schema. Separately, decide whether the `search_provider is None` pass-through state should degrade gracefully (empty `ListDocumentsResponse` + a "search not configured" signal) instead of a hard `503`, and track that as its own concern.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md), [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md).

Fix (2026-06-14, verified live): rewrote `list_sources()` in `backend/core/providers/search/azure_search.py` to stop faceting `title`. It now issues `client.search(search_text="*", select=["title"])`, pages the result set (the same async-iterator pattern `delete_by_source` uses), tallies a per-source chunk count into a `dict[str, int]` client-side, and returns `SourceListing`s sorted alphabetically by source. The `try/except AzureError` + structured `logger.exception` + re-raise contract is retained, so a genuine search outage still surfaces as 503 upstream. Tests in `tests/backend/core/providers/search/test_azure_search.py` were rewritten from the facet harness to the paging harness (29/29 green; `pyright --strict` 0/0/0).

Live confirmation: a throwaway probe ran the credential-selection path the backend lifespan uses (`select_default` → `AzureCliCredential` locally) against the live index. The new `list_sources()` returned 2 real sources; the original raw facet query (`facets=["title,count:10000,sort:value"]`) raised `HttpResponseError` 400 `(FieldNotFacetable) The field 'title' has not been marked as facetable in the schema`, confirming the recorded root cause. The earlier mock-only attempt appeared not to clear the live 503 only because the running `uvicorn` had been started **without** `--reload` and was still serving the pre-fix code (the stale worker's command line carried no `--reload` flag). After stopping that process and starting a fresh backend with the patched code, `GET /api/admin/documents` returns `200` with the source listing (`total: 2`). The separate latent `search_provider is None` pass-through (empty endpoint → hard 503) is unchanged and stays tracked as its own concern.

### BUG-0004 — Orchestrator field is free text instead of a dropdown

Area: frontend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-11).

Symptom: on the admin Configuration page the Orchestrator field is a single-line text input, so an operator can type an invalid key and save it.

Root cause: `orchestrator_name` is declared as a text field in the `FIELD_SPECS` array in `frontend/src/pages/admin/Configuration/Configuration.tsx`; there is no select control bound to the known orchestrator keys.

Proposed fix: render a dropdown sourced from the first-party orchestrator keys `langgraph` and `agent_framework` (the `OrchestratorName` enum in `backend/core/settings.py`, registered in `backend/core/providers/orchestrators/registry.py`). Decide in the fix turn whether to keep a free-text escape hatch for third-party registered keys, since the settings type is widened to `OrchestratorName | str`.

Fix: added an `OrchestratorName` closed-set map (`langgraph`, `agent_framework`) to `frontend/src/models/admin.tsx` mirroring the backend StrEnum, extended `FieldSpec` with a `select` kind plus an `options` list, and rendered the Orchestrator field as a Fluent UI `Select` dropdown. Escape-hatch decision: no free-text input is kept, but if the running config already holds a key outside the first-party set (allowed by the widened `OrchestratorName | str` backend type), that current value is added as an extra option so it stays selectable and is never silently dropped. The wire field `orchestrator_name` stays a plain `string`, and `validateField` now treats `select` as a closed choice. Covered by the Configuration Vitest suite (`src/tests/frontend/pages/admin/Configuration/Configuration.test.tsx`); full frontend suite green (371 tests).

Follow-up defect (persistence): after the dropdown shipped, selecting `agent_framework` and saving reported success but the field reverted to `langgraph` on reload. Root cause: the admin client `getAdminConfig()` in `frontend/src/api/admin.tsx` read `GET /api/admin/config` — the plain env-default snapshot that intentionally ignores overrides — instead of `GET /api/admin/config/effective`, the endpoint that overlays the persisted `RuntimeConfig` from `app.state.runtime_overrides`. The `PATCH /api/admin/config` write persisted and live-reloaded the override correctly; only the read-back used the wrong source, so every override field (the orchestrator was just the visible one) reverted on reload. Fix: pointed `getAdminConfig()` at `/api/admin/config/effective` and unwrapped the `values` payload, and added an `EffectiveAdminConfig` wire type to `frontend/src/models/admin.tsx` mirroring the backend model. The backend env-vs-effective endpoint split is intentional (backend tests pin `/api/admin/config` as the env-only snapshot), so no backend change was made. Covered by the admin client Vitest suite (`src/tests/frontend/api/admin.test.tsx`, `getAdminConfig` block now asserts the effective endpoint and the unwrapped override-resolved value); full frontend suite green (371 tests).

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md).

### BUG-0005 — Admin configuration labels show internal config-key names

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-11).

Symptom: every field label on the admin Configuration page appends the raw config key in parentheses, for example "Orchestrator (orchestrator_name)" and "Content safety (content_safety_enabled)".

Root cause: the label rendering in `frontend/src/pages/admin/Configuration/Configuration.tsx` appends each field spec's key to its human-readable label.

Proposed fix: render the human-readable label only and drop the parenthetical config-key suffix.

Fix: removed the `<span>` that rendered `({spec.key})` from the field label so it shows only the human-readable `spec.label`, and deleted the now-dead `.fieldName` CSS class. Added a test asserting rendered labels contain the human text and never the parenthetical config key.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md).

### BUG-0006 — Content Safety defaults to disabled

Area: backend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-11).

Symptom: Content Safety starts disabled by default, so the input pre-filter does not run unless an operator opts in.

Root cause: `ContentSafetySettings.enabled` defaults to `False` in `backend/core/settings.py`, a deliberate opt-in. Production infrastructure already sets `AZURE_CONTENT_SAFETY_ENABLED` to `true` in Bicep, and the lifespan activates the client only when both `enabled` is true and an endpoint is set; the shipped `.env.sample` leaves it `false`.

Proposed fix: change the default to `True`. This is safe because the lifespan gates the client on both `enabled` and a configured endpoint — with no endpoint the client stays `None` and the guard is inert. Confirm the intent in the fix turn before flipping the default.

Fix: flipped `ContentSafetySettings.enabled` to default `True` (secure-by-default) and set `.env.sample` `AZURE_CONTENT_SAFETY_ENABLED=true` (chosen with the operator). The lifespan gate still requires both `enabled` and a non-empty endpoint, so the new default is inert until `AZURE_CONTENT_SAFETY_ENDPOINT` is set; production (which already provisions the endpoint via Bicep) is unchanged. Updated the settings docstring, the `.env.sample` comment, and the two backend tests that pinned the old `False` default (`test_content_safety_settings_defaults_when_unset` now asserts `True`; `test_init_content_safety_client_returns_none_when_disabled` now opts out explicitly).

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md).

### BUG-0007 — Default agent instructions do not carry the v1 default prompt text

Area: backend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-11).

Symptom: the v2 default system prompt does not reflect the vetted default answering prompt that v1 ships.

Root cause: the v1 default prompt text lives in `code/backend/batch/utilities/helpers/config/default.json` (the `answering_system_prompt` and `answering_user_prompt` keys). v2 defines its built-in instructions as `CWYD_AGENT` in `backend/core/agents/definitions.py` and never ported the v1 default text. The functional impact is that the prior minimal prompt never told the model the `[docN]` inline citation format, yet the v2 citation pipeline depends on it: the langgraph orchestrator injects a `Sources:` system message, the model is expected to emit `[docN]` markers, and `filter_to_referenced` (`backend/core/tools/citations.py`) extracts those markers into `citation` SSE events. Without the format instruction, citations were unreliable.

Fix: ported v1's `answering_system_prompt` into `CWYD_AGENT.instructions` as a strict near-verbatim port (Option A, chosen with the operator) -- kept the two code-generation lines and the "private model trained by Open AI" line, and reproduced v1's exact text (including its sub-bullet indentation and its original wording quirks) so the prompt stays the vetted, shipped text. The **only** adaptation was dropping v1's stale knowledge-cutoff line ("Your internal knowledge ... only current until ... 2021 ... The current date will be provided in the system message."), because v2 injects no current date. The v1 per-business-unit assistant-type system (Default / Contract assistant / Employee assistant) and the separate `answering_user_prompt` user-turn template remain out of scope. Updated the test (renamed `test_cwyd_agent_grounds_in_knowledge_base` -> `test_cwyd_agent_carries_vetted_v1_default_prompt`) to assert the ported content: grounds in "retrieved documents", carries the `[doc+index]` citation format, preserves the out-of-domain refusal string, and confirms the 2021 line is gone. `name`/`tools` assertions unchanged. 173 backend tests pass (agents + admin + orchestrators).
