References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md).

### BUG-0008 — Separate Prompt editor page should fold into Configuration

Area: frontend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-11).

Symptom: v2 exposes a dedicated Prompt editor page, whereas v1 edits all prompts inline on a single Configuration page.

Root cause: the prompt-editor route was added during the `#35d` admin merge. `frontend/src/pages/admin/PromptEditor/PromptEditor.tsx` is wired through `frontend/src/models/sections.tsx` (the `AdminPrompt` section and its `/admin/prompt` route), `frontend/src/App.tsx` (the route element), `frontend/src/pages/admin/AdminLayout.tsx`, and the header nav — built as v1 parity, but v1 has no separate editor.

Fix: adopted the v1 structure — `cwyd_agent_instructions` is now a multi-line `kind: "text"` field with `allowEmpty: true` at the top of `FIELD_SPECS` on the Configuration page, rendered through the existing `<Textarea>` branch exactly like `post_answering_prompt`. It is added to `RAI_GUARDED_FIELDS`, so a 422 RAI rejection surfaces inline on the field row. v1 has no per-field "Reset to default" button; clearing the textarea and saving sends an empty string, which `_resolve_definition` (`backend/core/providers/agents/base.py`) already treats identically to `null` (both fall back to the built-in `CWYD_AGENT` default), so reset-to-default is preserved without extra `null` plumbing. Removed the standalone page and all its wiring: deleted `frontend/src/pages/admin/PromptEditor/` (page + CSS) and `tests/frontend/pages/admin/PromptEditor/`, dropped the `AdminPrompt` member + its `SectionPath` entry from `sections.tsx`, removed the `admin-subnav-prompt` nav item from `AdminLayout.tsx`, and removed the `PromptEditor` import + `/admin/prompt` route from `App.tsx`. The folded coverage lives in `tests/frontend/pages/admin/Configuration/Configuration.test.tsx` (textarea render, empty-allowed, PATCH, inline RAI rejection + clear). The wire models already declared the field across `AdminConfig` / `RuntimeConfig` / `AdminConfigPatch`, so no model or backend change was needed.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md).

### BUG-0009 — Log level field is free text instead of a dropdown

Area: frontend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-11).

Symptom: on the admin Configuration page the Log level field is a single-line text input, so an operator can type an arbitrary string and save it.

Root cause: `log_level` is declared with `kind: "text"` in the `FIELD_SPECS` array in `frontend/src/pages/admin/Configuration/Configuration.tsx`, so it renders through the text `<Input>` branch. The field hint even enumerates the closed set (`DEBUG`, `INFO`, `WARNING`, `ERROR`), but no select control is bound to it — the page imports only `Button`, `Input`, `Switch`, and `Textarea` from `@fluentui/react-components`.

Fix: rendered `log_level` as a dropdown over the closed set, reusing the same `kind: "select"` machinery as the orchestrator field (BUG-0004). Added a `LogLevel` closed-set const (`Debug`/`Info`/`Warning`/`Error` → `DEBUG`/`INFO`/`WARNING`/`ERROR`) to `frontend/src/models/admin.tsx`, mirroring the existing `OrchestratorName` `as const` + literal-union pattern; the wire field stays a plain `string` because the backend stores `log_level` as a free-form logging level name (`settings.observability.log_level: str = "INFO"`, no backend enum). Switched the `log_level` `FieldSpec` to `kind: "select"` with `options: [LogLevel.Debug, LogLevel.Info, LogLevel.Warning, LogLevel.Error]` and imported `LogLevel`. No change was needed to the select render branch, `selectOptions` derivation, `validateField` (select branch already present), `computePatch` (already sends `log_level` as a string), or `configToForm`. The pre-existing "empty text fields" validation test used `log_level` as its example non-empty text field; since `log_level` is now a select (and after BUG-0008 no `kind: "text"` field is non-`allowEmpty`), that test was retargeted to assert the select-cleared path (`must be selected`). Added two tests: a dropdown-render assertion (`SELECT` tag, options `["DEBUG","INFO","WARNING","ERROR"]`, value `INFO`) and a PATCH assertion (`patchAdminConfig` called with `{ log_level: "DEBUG" }`). Frontend suite green at 370 tests (31 files).

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md); related BUG-0004.

### BUG-0010 — Numeric config fields should validate numeric entry

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-11).

Symptom (as reported): numeric configuration values should have frontend validation that enforces a numeric entry.

Resolution: confirmed already-implemented and closed with a regression test; no production change was needed. The admin Configuration page is the only numeric-entry surface in the entire v2 frontend (a workspace search for `type="number"` / numeric input returns a single hit, in `frontend/src/pages/admin/Configuration/Configuration.tsx`). There the numeric fields (`openai_temperature`, `openai_max_tokens`, `search_top_k`) render through the `kind === "number"` branch as `<Input type="number">` with `step`, `min`, and `max`; `handleNumberChange` coerces an empty or non-parseable entry to `NaN`; `validateField` returns "must be a number" for a `NaN` or non-number value and enforces the min/max bounds; the error renders inline as `config-field-error-<key>` and `anyFieldInvalid` disables Save. The existing Vitest suite already covered the max-bound path (`openai_temperature` = `5` → "2 or less" + Save disabled) and the numeric PATCH delta, but had no test for the literal symptom (a non-numeric entry). Added one regression test — emptying `openai_max_tokens` surfaces "must be a number" and disables Save — pinning the enforce-numeric-entry behavior the bug asked for. Frontend suite green at 371 tests (31 files).

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md).

### BUG-0011 — Authored prompt could supersede the system guardrail prompt

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-11).

Symptom: an authored agent prompt could override the system's master ("uber") guardrail prompt — the authored text fully replaced the built-in safety, out-of-domain, and citation rules instead of being anchored to a fixed guardrail.

Root cause: `backend/core/providers/agents/base.py::_resolve_definition` applied the configured `cwyd_agent_instructions` with `definition.model_copy(update={"instructions": text})`, so the authored text fully **replaced** the `CWYD_AGENT` system instructions. Only `RAI_AGENT` and future safety surfaces were override-shielded (`if definition.name != CWYD_AGENT.name: return definition`), so an authored `CWYD_AGENT` prompt could supersede the intended system instructions.

Fix: extracted the non-negotiable safety / out-of-domain / citation rules into a single `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` constant in `backend/core/agents/definitions.py` and added `compose_cwyd_instructions(body)`, which appends the guardrail once, after `body`, so the fixed rules have last-word precedence (strongest position for resisting an override appearing in the body). Both the built-in default (`CWYD_AGENT.instructions = compose_cwyd_instructions(CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY)`) and the operator override path (`_resolve_definition` now returns `compose_cwyd_instructions(text)`) route through the same guardrail, so an authored prompt customizes the persona ahead of the guardrail but cannot supersede the fixed rules. To keep the prompt centralized and free of duplication, `CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY` was deduped against the guardrail (Tidy): every rule the guardrail owns (safety, the out-of-domain refusal message, the `[doc+index]` citation mechanics, the no-URLs rule, refuse-to-discuss-prompts, greetings-without-docs) was removed from the body, which now keeps only the unique persona / capabilities / formatting guidance and the in/out-of-domain decision methodology, deferring to the guardrail "below" for the rules it owns. Each rule therefore appears exactly once — no duplication or triplication. Regression coverage: `tests/backend/core/agents/test_definitions.py` (guardrail content + guardrail appended exactly once + default is guardrail-suffixed + each owned rule stated once) and `tests/backend/core/providers/agents/test_base.py` (a hostile override still resolves to instructions carrying the guardrail once, appended last).

Notes on the originally-recorded second facet: (a) RAI validation of the authored `cwyd_agent_instructions` on save was found to be **already in place** — `cwyd_agent_instructions` is in both the backend `PROMPT_FIELDS` (`backend/models/admin.py`) and the frontend `RAI_GUARDED_FIELDS`, so the PATCH handler RAI-screens it before persisting (wired when the prompt editor was folded into Configuration). The original root-cause note was stale on this point. (b) Whether end-user chat input should also be RAI-classified (in addition to the existing `ContentSafetyGuard` screen in `backend/app.py`) is a separate, larger design decision — it adds a Foundry round-trip to every chat turn — so it is intentionally **out of scope** here and is not bundled into this fix.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md); related BUG-0006, BUG-0007.

### BUG-0012 — Robot avatar and Thinking panel are not aligned

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11; fixed 2026-06-11; refined 2026-06-11; operator-confirmed live 2026-06-14).

Symptom: in the chat transcript the assistant robot avatar icon and the Thinking (reasoning) panel do not line up.

Root cause: in `frontend/src/pages/chat/components/MessageList.module.css` the reasoning `<details>` panel (`.reasoning`) carried `margin: 0 0 0 36px`, indenting it into the bubble column (28px avatar + 8px gap = 36px gutter). The assistant avatar (`Bot20Regular`, inside `.row`) and the `<CitationPanel>` `<section>` rendered below it (`.section`, `margin-left: 0`) both sit at the list-item left edge, so the Thinking panel was the odd one out — offset right from the avatar and from the citation panel. (The originally recorded hypothesis was inverted: the panel was already offset to the bubble column, not starting at the list-item edge, so the original "align with the bubble column" proposal would have been a no-op.)

Fix: set `.reasoning { margin: 0 }` so the panel's left edge is flush with the list-item edge, lining up with the avatar and with the citation panel below it. CSS-only — no JSX change; `.row`, the reasoning `<details>`, and `<CitationPanel>` were already direct `<li>` children, so zeroing the offset gives all three a shared left origin. Added a structural regression test (`renders the reasoning panel and citation panel as list-item siblings of the message row`) asserting both decorations render as direct children of the message `<li>`. Vitest runs with `css: false`, so the margin value itself is not observable in jsdom; the test pins the DOM sibling contract the alignment depends on (re-nesting the panel inside `.row` would fail it).

Refinement (2026-06-11): the left-edge fix gave the three elements a shared left origin but kept the avatar on its own line above the Thinking panel — the avatar lives in `.row`, while the reasoning `<details>` rendered as a sibling `<li>` child below it. The operator asked for the avatar to sit on the *same horizontal line* as the Thinking panel. For an assistant message the reasoning `<details>`, the answer bubble, and the `<CitationPanel>` now stack in a vertical `.content` column rendered *inside* `.row` beside the avatar, so the avatar lines up with the column's first item (the Thinking panel while streaming, else the answer); `flex: 1 1 auto; min-width: 0` moved off the assistant `.bubble` onto `.content`. The user-message branch is unchanged. The regression test was retargeted from the sibling contract to the same-row contract — `renders the reasoning panel and citation panel inside the same row as the avatar` asserts both panels share the `.row` that holds the avatar and are no longer direct `<li>` children.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md).

### BUG-0013 — Thinking/reasoning feed never shows

Area: backend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-14).

Symptom: the Thinking/reasoning feed is never visible in the chat UI.

Root cause: the frontend reasoning panel in `frontend/src/pages/chat/components/MessageList.tsx` renders only while `m.streaming === true` or when `m.reasoning` has content, and its body is `m.reasoning.join("")`. The SSE handling in the chat input flow appends `reasoning` frames to `m.reasoning`, so the frontend is wired correctly — but the backend orchestrator emits no `reasoning`-channel SSE frames at runtime (the default `langgraph` orchestrator does not surface o-series reasoning), so `m.reasoning` stays empty and the panel collapses to nothing once streaming ends.

Proposed fix (direction): emit `reasoning`-channel `OrchestratorEvent`s from the orchestrator when a reasoning summary is available, so the existing frontend panel renders. Confirm in the fix turn which orchestrator(s) should surface reasoning and the source of the reasoning text.

Update (2026-06-14): the related BUG-0027 fix now emits an upfront `reasoning` frame ("Searching the knowledge base…") in the shared `run_chat` pipeline before the orchestrator runs, so the panel is no longer always empty — it shows that one canned narration during the retrieval wait. But no **substantive** model reasoning content is ever emitted: neither orchestrator surfaces an o-series reasoning summary or step-by-step thinking, so the panel shows only the canned narration, not the actual thinking process. The operator confirmed exactly this today while verifying BUG-0012 (alignment fixed; thinking-process *content* still missing). This bug remains the home for surfacing real reasoning content.

Confirmed root cause (2026-06-14, code read): the reasoning machinery is fully built end-to-end and correct — `FoundryIQ.reason()` uses the Responses API with `reasoning={"effort": "medium", "summary": "auto"}` and emits `reasoning`-channel events for `response.reasoning_summary_text.delta`; the `langgraph` orchestrator passes reasoning events through verbatim; the `agent_framework` orchestrator maps `text_reasoning` content blocks to `reasoning` events; the FE panel renders them. The reason no substantive content appears is that **the answer model never produces a reasoning summary on either live path**: (1) `langgraph` — `LangGraphOrchestrator.run()` calls `self.llm.complete()`, whose router delegates to `reason()` only when the chosen deployment equals `settings.openai.reasoning_deployment`; the answer always uses `gpt_deployment` (gpt-5.1), so `complete()` always routes to `chat()` (Chat Completions), which emits only `answer`. The `reason()` path (Responses API, summary deltas) is wired but never invoked for answering — the reasoning deployment is used only for KB query-planning. (2) `agent_framework` (the live default in cosmosdb mode) — `CWYD_AGENT` runs on `gpt_deployment` via the server-side Responses run, but the agent definition sets no reasoning effort/summary knob, so the run emits no `text_reasoning` summary blocks. Surfacing real reasoning is therefore a design decision (which path, and whether to change the answer model/API), not a mechanical one-method fix — pending operator direction.

Fix (2026-06-14): the answer deployment's reasoning capability is auto-detected — `BaseLLMProvider.supports_reasoning(deployment)` runs a cached one-shot Responses-API probe (a `reasoning` request against the chat deployment, classified by the 400 the Responses API returns for non-reasoning models) and both orchestrators consult it before answering. When the deployment supports reasoning: (1) `langgraph` — `FoundryIQ.complete()` routes to `reason()` (Responses API, `reasoning={"effort":"medium","summary":"auto"}`), which now builds its `input` via the new `_to_responses_input` helper that emits explicitly `message`-typed items (`{"type":"message","role":…,"content":…}`); the bare `{role,content}` dicts it sent before were rejected by the Responses API with `400 … param=input[N] … invalid_value` (empty `type`). (2) `agent_framework` — `run()` sets the Responses `reasoning` option on the agent run and, in reasoning mode, omits the `temperature`/`max_tokens` sampling knobs (see BUG-0035). Both paths emit substantive model reasoning on the existing `reasoning` SSE channel, which the FE panel already renders; the canned KB-search narration (BUG-0027) still leads during the retrieval wait. An earlier interim fix used an opt-in `AZURE_OPENAI_REASONING_SUMMARY` env flag (default off); it was removed the same day because it defaulted off and hid a capability the shipped `gpt-5.1` answer model has — auto-detection always lights up reasoning when the model supports it, with no operator action. Verified live against the deployment with a parametrized `tests/integration` test that forces each orchestrator past the persisted cosmos `langgraph` override: both `langgraph` and `agent_framework` stream non-empty, non-canned reasoning content (the live run also caught BUG-0035, the `agent_framework` temperature 400).

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md), [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md); related BUG-0026, BUG-0027, BUG-0035.

### BUG-0014 — Assistant response markdown is not converted to HTML

Area: frontend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (2026-06-14, found 2026-06-11).

Symptom: assistant answers display as raw markdown (literal `**bold**`, list markers, headings, fenced code, tables) instead of rendered HTML.

Root cause: `frontend/src/pages/chat/components/answerTokens.tsx` (`renderAnswerTokens`) only tokenizes `[docN]` citation markers and otherwise pushes raw text slices as plain strings; it performs no markdown-to-HTML conversion, and the v2 frontend has no markdown renderer dependency. v1 renders answers through `react-markdown` (`code/frontend/src/components/Answer/Answer.tsx`).

Resolution (2026-06-14): added `frontend/src/pages/chat/components/MarkdownContent.tsx` — a reusable `{ content, className }` renderer wrapping `react-markdown` + `remark-gfm` (GFM tables/strikethrough) with a link override (`target=_blank` + `rel=noreferrer`) and **no** `rehype-raw`, so embedded raw HTML is escaped rather than mounted (XSS-safe). `MessageList` now renders both the assistant answer and the reasoning-panel body through `MarkdownContent` (the reasoning body still flows through `formatReasoning` first); user messages stay plain text. Scope decision (operator-approved Option A): the answer renders as pure markdown, so inline `[docN]` markers now appear as literal text — the clickable-citation behavior previously wired via `renderAnswerTokens` is intentionally deferred to BUG-0016 (which reworks inline references into v1-style superscript links). `renderAnswerTokens` and its tests are retained for that rework, and the panel stays manually expandable in the interim. Covered by `MarkdownContent.test.tsx` (9 cases incl. the raw-`<script>`-not-mounted XSS guard) and the updated `MessageList` answer-rendering tests; full FE suite 402/402, both FE workspaces typecheck clean.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md); [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md); related BUG-0016.

### BUG-0015 — Citation/reference block should look like v1

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: the reference block shown under an assistant answer does not match the v1 appearance.

Root cause: the v2 reference block is rendered by `frontend/src/pages/chat/components/CitationPanel/CitationPanel.tsx` with its own styling, which differs from the v1 citation presentation (`code/frontend/src/components/Answer/Answer.tsx` plus `Answer.module.css` `.citationContainer` and `.citation`).

Resolution (2026-06-15, operator-approved scope — reference-block restyle only; the v1 right-side citation detail column is out of scope): reworked `CitationPanel` into the v1 reference block — a collapsible toggle labeled `N references` / `1 reference` (singular at one) with a chevron (`ChevronRight16Regular` / `ChevronDown16Regular`), collapsed by default, over a numbered citation list. Each item shows a circular brand-colored number chip plus the citation title (falling back to `Citation N` when the title is empty); the score badge was dropped. Items still expand individually to a snippet and an XSS-safe `Open source` link (`target=_blank` + `rel=noopener noreferrer`). The inner list is mounted-but-`hidden` while collapsed (not conditionally unmounted), and a focused citation auto-opens the toggle and expands the matching item. `MessageList` now computes `parseAnswer(m.content, m.citations)` once and passes the renumbered referenced-citation subset to `CitationPanel` (falling back to `m.citations` when the answer has no markers), so the chip numbers stay coherent with the BUG-0016 answer superscripts and only cited sources appear. Covered by the rewritten `CitationPanel.test.tsx` (17 cases) and a new `MessageList` coherence test (out-of-order `[doc2] [doc1]` → chips numbered to match the renumbered superscripts); full FE suite 420/420, both FE workspaces typecheck clean.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md); [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md); related BUG-0014, BUG-0016.

### BUG-0016 — Inline references should render like v1

Area: frontend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: inline citation markers inside the answer render as literal `[docN]` text; v1 shows them as compact superscript citation links.

Root cause: the answer body rendered the wire string as-is through `MarkdownContent`, so the `[docN]` markers the model emits stayed as literal bracket text. (The earlier `answerTokens.tsx` renderer had shown each marker as `<button>{raw}</button>` — still the literal bracket text — before BUG-0014 routed the answer through the markdown panel.)

Resolution: added `frontend/src/pages/chat/components/parseAnswer.tsx`, a pure transform that rewrites each in-bounds `[docN]` marker into a `^K^` superscript token, deduplicating repeated sources and renumbering them `1..K` in first-appearance order, collapsing consecutive duplicates, and leaving out-of-bounds markers verbatim. `MarkdownContent` gained an opt-in `enableSupersub` prop that adds `remark-supersub` to the remark pipeline (no `rehype-raw`, so rendering stays XSS-safe), turning `^K^` into `<sup>` nodes. `MessageList` routes the assistant answer body through `parseAnswer(...).markdownText` with `enableSupersub`; the superscripts are visual-only (v1-exact — the reference block in BUG-0015 is the click target). `CitationPanel` still consumes the unmodified `m.citations`; user messages and citation-less assistant answers keep `[docN]` verbatim. Covered by `parseAnswer.test.tsx` (13 cases) and two new `MarkdownContent.test.tsx` supersub cases; full FE suite 417/417, both FE workspaces typecheck clean. The now-unused `renderAnswerTokens` / `answerTokens.tsx` (+ test) are retained pending a separate removal decision.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md); [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md); related BUG-0014, BUG-0015.

### BUG-0017 — New conversation is not saved to history

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: when a user starts a conversation by sending a message, the conversation does not appear in the left-hand chat history column.

Root cause: `POST /api/conversation` in `backend/routers/conversation.py` runs the orchestrator and streams the answer but performs no chat-history writes. History persistence is entirely client-driven through the separate `/api/history/*` endpoints — the only create path is the explicit New chat button in `HistoryPanel` (`handleNew` → `POST /api/history/conversations`). So a conversation begun by simply typing a first message is never persisted server-side and never appears in the history list.

Proposed fix (direction): persist the conversation and its turns as part of the conversation flow — either server-side in the conversation router or by having the chat flow create and persist a conversation on the first message. Settle the exact persistence trigger and ownership in the fix turn.

Progress (2026-06-15): Phase 1 (backend persistence) complete and green. `POST /api/conversation` now persists every completed turn server-side via `services.conversation.persist_turn` — the user message, the assistant answer, and the answer's grounding citations (stored in the assistant message's `metadata["citations"]`) — keyed by the Easy Auth principal id, in both buffered and streaming modes. A new thread is titled with the first question; the streaming path returns the resolved id on a terminal `conversation` SSE control frame. Units U1 / U2a / U2b / U3a–U3d landed test-first with an end-to-end live integration test (`test_conversation_persists_citations_to_history_live`, green against the live env). **Stays open**: the user-visible fix needs Phase 2 (frontend) — `ChatContext` conversation-id tracking, parsing the terminal `conversation` frame, load-on-click rehydration in `HistoryPanel`, and the new-chat / hidden-db-name UX (folds BUG-0018 / BUG-0019). BUG-0017 flips to fixed when Phase 1 + 2 both land.

Resolution (2026-06-15): Phase 2 (frontend bridge) is now complete and green, so BUG-0017 is fixed. The frontend half landed test-first: `ChatContext` tracks the `conversationId` (U4); `streamChat` parses the terminal `conversation` SSE control frame and surfaces the resolved id (U5); `MessageInput` sends the tracked id and folds the resolved id back into context on the next turn (U6); selecting a history row fetches the stored conversation detail and rehydrates the full transcript plus persisted citations (U7a / U7b); the New chat button was removed from the history column in favor of the existing header affordance (U9, BUG-0019); and the raw backend db-name display was removed from the history header (U10, BUG-0018). With Phase 1 (backend persistence, validated by the live integration test) and Phase 2 both landed, a conversation begun by simply sending a first message is persisted server-side and appears in the left history column. Follow-on work tracked separately and **not** part of this bug's symptom: Phase 3 (rename validation + RAI screening, U11–U12) and Phase 4 (cloud identity / per-user history isolation, U13–U15).

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md), [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md); related BUG-0018, BUG-0019.

### BUG-0018 — Chat history column shows the backend database name

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: the chat history left column header shows `backend: <db_type>` — the configured chat-history database discriminator.

Root cause: `frontend/src/pages/chat/components/HistoryPanel.tsx` renders `<p data-testid="history-db-type">backend: {status.db_type}</p>` from the `/api/history/status` response in the panel header.

Fix (2026-06-15): removed the `history-db-type` display from the panel header. Since the panel fetched `/api/history/status` solely to surface that discriminator (it never branched on it — Hard Rule #4), the now-orphaned status fetch, the `status` React state, and the `HistoryStatus` interface were removed too; the panel now mounts by loading only `/api/history/conversations`. Test-first: the mount test was updated to assert the panel loads the conversations list *without* calling `/api/history/status`, plus a negative test that `history-db-type` is never rendered.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md), [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md); related BUG-0017.

### BUG-0019 — Remove the New chat section from the history column

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: the chat history left column contains a New chat section that should be removed.

Root cause: `frontend/src/pages/chat/components/HistoryPanel.tsx` renders a New chat button (`data-testid="history-new"`) wired to `handleNew` (`POST /api/history/conversations`). Related New-chat wiring exists outside the panel — the header `HeaderTools` `onNewChat` control and the `newChatNonce` flow in `App.tsx`.

Fix (2026-06-15): removed the `history-new` button and the `handleNew` callback from `HistoryPanel`, along with the now-unused `Add16Regular` icon import. Scope decision: the header New-chat affordance (`HeaderTools` `data-testid="header-new-chat"` → `App.tsx` `newChatNonce` → `<ChatPage key={newChatNonce} />` remount) is the working way to start a fresh chat — it remounts `ChatPage`, re-initializing `ChatContext` to `initialChatState` (empty transcript, `conversationId: null`). Because the bug is scoped to the history left column and removing the header control too would leave no way to start a new chat, the header affordance and `newChatNonce` wiring are intentionally kept. Test-first: the obsolete "creates a new conversation" `HistoryPanel` test was replaced with a negative assertion that the `history-new` button is not rendered.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md); [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md); related BUG-0017.

### BUG-0020 — KB MCP connect is unauthenticated (401 on chat)

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-11).

Symptom: sending a chat message on a Foundry IQ deployment failed with `Message failed ('Failed to enter context manager.', ExceptionGroup('unhandled errors in a TaskGroup', [HTTPStatusError("Client error '401 Unauthorized' for url 'https://srch-<SUFFIX>.search.windows.net/knowledgebases/cwyd-kb/mcp?api-version=2025-11-01-preview'")]))`.

Root cause: the `agent_framework` orchestrator (`backend/core/providers/orchestrators/agent_framework.py`) attached the Search data-plane bearer to the Knowledge Base MCP tool through the SDK's `header_provider` hook only. The Agent Framework SDK applies that hook exclusively inside `MCPStreamableHTTPTool.call_tool()` (it sets a `contextvars.ContextVar` that an httpx request event hook reads). The MCP session-initialize connect handshake runs earlier — when the tool's async context manager is entered (`MCPTool.__aenter__` → `connect()`), before any tool call — so the connect request carried no `Authorization` header. Azure AI Search rejected the unauthenticated connect with `401`, and the SDK re-raised it as `ToolExecutionException("Failed to enter context manager.")`. The `/health/ready` search probe stayed green because it exercises the normal data-plane index credential, a different surface from the KB MCP connect.

Fix: `run()` now constructs an `httpx.AsyncClient` carrying the same bearer as a default `Authorization` header and passes it to `_build_kb_tool(..., http_client=...)`, which forwards it to `MCPStreamableHTTPTool(http_client=...)`. httpx applies default headers to every request, so the connect handshake is authenticated as well as tool calls. The `header_provider` hook is retained (belt-and-suspenders for tool calls; the same bearer merges idempotently). Because the MCP streamable-HTTP transport never closes a caller-supplied client (`mcp.client.streamable_http.streamable_http_client` only manages clients it creates), `run()` owns the client lifecycle and closes it in a `finally` that covers both the streaming path and an agent-construction failure. Cross-checked against the read-only reference architecture, whose one bearer-attached MCP client path sets `headers["Authorization"]` as a default header on the httpx client (`src/backend/v4/common/services/mcp_service.py`), confirming the connection-level default-header approach.

Why it was not caught earlier: this was the first live end-to-end exercise of the agent path against a real Search service; orchestrator unit tests fully fake the FoundryAgent and never enter the MCP tool's context manager, so the connect handshake was never exercised. New tests assert the KB tool is built with a default-`Authorization`-header client and that the client is closed after a normal run and after an agent-construction failure.

References: [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md).

### BUG-0021 — `agent_framework` chat 404s: persistent-assistant vs name-referenced Foundry agent mismatch

Area: backend. Severity: blocker. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-12).

Symptom: every `POST /api/conversation` on the default `agent_framework` orchestrator returns `500` (buffered) / an `error` SSE frame (streaming). Backend log: `ChatClientException: ... 404 - Agent 'cwyd' not found`. The failure surfaces in the chat-completion stream (`agent_framework_openai/_chat_client.py`), i.e. *after* `_prepare_run_context` — so it is downstream of, and distinct from, the BUG-0020 MCP-connect 401 (which is fixed).

Root cause: two different Foundry agent surfaces are crossed.

- Provisioning (`BaseAgentsProvider.get_or_create_agent` → `FoundryAgentsProvider`) calls `azure.ai.agents.aio.AgentsClient.create_agent(...)`, which creates an **Assistants-API persistent agent** identified by an `asst_` id. Confirmed live: the Foundry project holds exactly one agent — an `asst_`-prefixed id with `name='cwyd'` and `model='gpt-5.1'`, i.e. an Assistants-API persistent agent.
- Invocation (`AgentFrameworkOrchestrator` → `agent_framework_foundry.FoundryAgent(agent_name="cwyd", allow_preview=True)`) references the agent through the **Responses API by name** (`get_openai_client(agent_name=...)` / `agent_reference {"name": "cwyd"}`). That name-reference resolves a Foundry *named/prompt* agent resource, not an Assistants-API `asst_` persistent agent, so Foundry returns 404.
- The conversation router compounds the gap: it calls `get_or_create_agent(CWYD_AGENT, db)` but **discards the returned `asst_` id** and passes the friendly `CWYD_AGENT.name` ("cwyd") to the orchestrator.

Contributing context: the project endpoint was recently switched to a different Foundry account/project (per `.env`). In the new project only the persistent-assistant create path has run, so no name-referenceable agent resource exists.

Fix direction (recommended — structural, Hard Rule #10, needs operator consent): align the two halves of the decoupled-hybrid (dev_plan §0.1 `B1-MAF-MISLABEL` / `B-IMPL-AUDIT`) on the **name-referenced Prompt Agent** resource type. Switch `FoundryAgentsProvider`'s create path from `azure.ai.agents.AgentsClient.create_agent` (which mints an Assistants-API `asst_` agent) to the Foundry **Prompt Agent** path (`PromptAgentDefinition` + `create_version` on the projects SDK), so a name(+version)-resolvable `cwyd` agent exists for the orchestrator's `FoundryAgent(agent_name=..., agent_version=...)` invocation. This is exactly the alternative the dev_plan **B-Spike** flagged (`PromptAgentDefinition` + `create_version` vs `AgentsClient.create_agent`) but never switched.

Rejected alternatives: (a) invoke the existing `asst_` agent by id — the OSS `FoundryAgent` exposes no `agent_id` parameter (name + optional version only, for Prompt/Hosted agents) and no `agent_framework` persistent-agent (Azure AI Agent Service threads/runs) client is installed; (b) toggling `allow_preview` does not change the resource type the reference resolves — both code paths reference a Prompt/Hosted agent by name.

Why it was not caught earlier: `test_agent_framework.py` injects a fake agent factory, so the persistent-assistant-vs-name-reference distinction is never exercised against the live Responses API. The "Thinking" panel appears as soon as the SSE stream opens, so a screenshot showing "Thinking" does not prove the agent actually ran.

Resolution (2026-06-12, [ADR 0025](adr/0025-foundry-prompt-agent-ga-pattern.md)): fixed via the Foundry **Prompt Agent GA pattern** — exactly the recommended direction above. `FoundryAgentsProvider.get_or_create_agent` now builds a `PromptAgentDefinition` and calls `AIProjectClient.agents.create_version(agent_name=...)` (the `asst_` `AgentsClient.create_agent` path is removed), persisting and returning the agent **name**; a cold start validates the name with `agents.get` (`ResourceNotFoundError` → recreate) and a concurrent-create `409` re-reads and reuses the existing agent. Invocation no longer uses the by-name `FoundryAgent` Responses path: the orchestrator composes a client-side `agent_framework.Agent` over `FoundryChatClient` through the shared `build_agent` seam and drives it as an async context manager. KB grounding moved server-side (`MCPTool(project_connection_id=...)`), which also retired the BUG-0020 client-side bearer / `httpx` machinery. Both halves now reference one name-addressed Prompt Agent, so the resource-type mismatch cannot recur. Landed across units U1–U8 + U10 (RAI migrated to the same seam in U8); ADR 0025 carries the full decision record and the multi-agent coordinator readiness note.

References: [adr/0025-foundry-prompt-agent-ga-pattern.md](adr/0025-foundry-prompt-agent-ga-pattern.md); [worklog/2026-06-11.md](worklog/2026-06-11.md); [worklog/2026-06-12.md](worklog/2026-06-12.md).

### BUG-0022 — Operator-authored system prompt dropped on the `agent_framework` chat path

Area: backend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-11, fixed 2026-06-12).

Symptom: surfaced by audit during the BUG-0021 fix planning (GAP-2), not a separate live repro — BUG-0021's `404` masked the chat path entirely. On the default `agent_framework` orchestrator, an operator-authored instruction override (the admin `cwyd_agent_instructions` in `RuntimeConfig`) could fail to reach the model: the saved prompt would silently not take effect, while the same override applied correctly on the `langgraph` path.

Root cause: the conversation router threads the effective instructions to every orchestrator uniformly as `system_prompt=effective.cwyd_agent_instructions`. `langgraph` consumes it (injects it as the leading system message). The `agent_framework` orchestrator swallowed `system_prompt` via `**_extras` and invoked the agent **by name** (`FoundryAgent(agent_name="cwyd")`), which resolves the server-side agent's instructions — baked once at create time and cached by identity ([ADR 0008](adr/0008-lazy-foundry-agent-bootstrap.md)). So neither the per-request effective instructions nor a later admin prompt edit propagated to the default path; the operator prompt lever worked only on `langgraph`.

Fix: the GA pattern ([ADR 0025](adr/0025-foundry-prompt-agent-ga-pattern.md), unit U5) makes instruction resolution a per-request provider concern. `FoundryAgentsProvider.build_agent` calls `_resolve_definition(definition)` — which reads the current `RuntimeConfig` override (`overrides.cwyd_agent_instructions`, `CWYD_AGENT` only; `RAI_AGENT` is intentionally not operator-editable so the classifier prompt cannot be weakened) and wraps it via `compose_cwyd_instructions` so the fixed `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` keeps last-word precedence (the BUG-0011 invariant) — then composes the client-side `agent_framework.Agent(instructions=resolved.instructions)`. Because the runtime `Agent` is built with the resolved instructions on every request, the authored prompt now applies on the `agent_framework` path too. The orchestrator still swallows the router's `system_prompt` kwarg by design — instructions are resolved in the provider, not threaded by the orchestrator — so that kwarg is intentionally inert on this path.

References: [adr/0025-foundry-prompt-agent-ga-pattern.md](adr/0025-foundry-prompt-agent-ga-pattern.md); [worklog/2026-06-12.md](worklog/2026-06-12.md).

### BUG-0023 — Knowledge-base seed wires the o-series reasoning model; Foundry IQ rejects it

Area: infra. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-12).

Symptom: `post_provision` (the azd `postprovision` hook) fails when seeding the Foundry IQ knowledge base in `cosmosdb` / AzureSearch mode. The knowledge *source* PUT succeeds, then the knowledge *base* PUT returns `400 Bad Request`: `Unsupported model type in Knowledge Base Model Configuration. ModelName must be either gpt-4o, gpt-4o-mini, gpt-4.1-nano, gpt-4.1-mini, gpt-4.1, gpt-5, gpt-5-mini, gpt-5-nano, gpt-5.1, gpt-5.2, gpt-5.4, gpt-5.4-mini, gpt-5.4-nano, gpt-5.5.` So the knowledge base is never created and the `agent_framework` orchestrator has nothing to ground against.

Root cause: `_ensure_knowledge_base` sourced the knowledge-base query-planning model from the **reasoning** deployment (`AZURE_OPENAI_REASONING_DEPLOYMENT`, an o-series model such as `o4-mini`). The Foundry IQ knowledge-base model configuration only accepts **chat** models from a fixed allow-list (the 400 lists the gpt-4o / gpt-4.1 / gpt-5.x families); o-series reasoning models are not accepted, so the PUT 400s. This affected every deployment, not just one environment — no path through the seed would pass with the reasoning deployment.

Why it was not caught earlier: the unit tests for `_build_knowledge_base_seed` / `_ensure_knowledge_base` used `"gpt-5"` as the model name (a value that happens to be on the allow-list), so they asserted the seed *shape* but never exercised the real reasoning-deployment value. The seed had also never been run end-to-end against a live knowledge-base API on the current project.

Fix: source the knowledge-base query-planning model from the **chat** deployment (`AZURE_OPENAI_GPT_DEPLOYMENT`, e.g. `gpt-5.1`), with an optional `AZURE_OPENAI_GPT_MODEL_NAME` override (the deployment id doubles as the model name when unset, matching how Bicep names the deployment after `gptModelName`). Renamed the `_build_knowledge_base_seed` parameters `reasoning_deployment` / `reasoning_model_name` to `query_planning_deployment` / `query_planning_model_name`, changed the guard + error message to require `AZURE_OPENAI_GPT_DEPLOYMENT`, and updated the comments / docstrings to record that Foundry IQ rejects o-series models for the KB model. Tests now set both the chat and reasoning deployments and assert the knowledge base uses the chat one (regression guard). Verified live: re-running the seed reports `knowledge base 'cwyd-kb' ready`.

References: [worklog/2026-06-12.md](worklog/2026-06-12.md).

### BUG-0024 — Search service identity lacks OpenAI User, so the knowledge-base query-planning model call 401s

Area: infra. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-12).

Symptom: on the `agent_framework` / Foundry IQ path (`cosmosdb` mode), a chat such as "tell me about employee benefits" returns the out-of-domain fallback (`The requested information is not available in the retrieved data...`) with **no `tool`, `reasoning`, or `citation` SSE frames** — even though the chat index contains relevant content (a direct index search for "employee benefits" returns `Benefit_Options.pdf` and `employee_handbook.pdf`). The backend logs no error: the chat request returns `200` and the agent simply produces the grounding refusal.

Root cause: the Foundry IQ knowledge base cannot call its query-planning chat model. Calling the knowledge-base retrieve endpoint directly reproduces the failure server-side: `Could not complete model action. The model endpoint returned status code '401' (Unauthorized). The principal <search-service-MI-principal-id> lacks the required data action Microsoft.CognitiveServices/accounts/OpenAI/deployments/chat/completions/action`. The knowledge-base model configuration has `authIdentity: null`, which means the knowledge base authenticates the model call with the **search service's system-assigned managed identity**. That identity has **no role assignments** on the AI Services account (`az role assignment list --assignee <search-MI> --scope <ai-services-account>` returns `[]`), so the `chat/completions` data action is denied and the model call 401s. The knowledge base then returns no grounded results, and the agent (correctly, given empty grounding) answers with the out-of-domain fallback. This is environment-independent: the v2 Bicep (`infra/main.bicep`) grants `Cognitive Services OpenAI User` (`5e0bd9bd-7b93-4f28-af87-19fc36ad61bd`) and `Azure AI User` to the **UAMI** on the AI Services account, but never grants any inference role to the **search service identity**, so every Foundry IQ deployment hits this once the knowledge base is exercised.

Why it was not caught earlier: this is the first end-to-end exercise of knowledge-base retrieval against a live AI Services account on the current project. The earlier `agent_framework` bugs (`BUG-0020` MCP-connect `401`, `BUG-0021` agent-resource `404`) blocked the path upstream of retrieval, and orchestrator unit tests fake the agent + knowledge base entirely, so the knowledge-base → model auth hop was never exercised. The model 401 happens server-side inside Foundry IQ and is not surfaced as a backend error — the agent receives empty grounding and refuses, which looks like a prompt over-refusal but is not.

Fix direction: grant the search service's system-assigned managed identity the `Cognitive Services OpenAI User` role (`5e0bd9bd-7b93-4f28-af87-19fc36ad61bd`) on the AI Services account — both live (`az role assignment create`) to unblock the running environment, and durably in `infra/main.bicep` (add a role assignment with the search service principal id as assignee on the AI Services account, mirroring the existing UAMI grants) so every `azd up` wires it. The reuse-existing-OpenAI path needs the same grant against the reused account. Alternative (not chosen): set the knowledge-base model `authIdentity` to a user-assigned identity that already holds the role — rejected because the search service has no suitable user-assigned identity attached, so the role grant on the system-assigned identity is the smaller, standard change.

Resolution (2026-06-12): granted the search service system-assigned MI `Cognitive Services OpenAI User` on the AI Services account, both live (to unblock the running environment) and durably in `infra/main.bicep` (`searchOpenAiUserOnFoundry`, with `searchOpenAiUserOnReusedOpenAi` covering the reuse-existing-OpenAI path). Verified live: a direct knowledge-base `/retrieve` now returns grounded `Benefit_Options.pdf` content, so the inner KB → query-planning-model call no longer 401s. Note: this resolves only the *inner* (KB → model) hop; the end-to-end agent chat remains blocked by BUG-0025 — the *outer* agent → KB-MCP-endpoint hop 401s under the project connection identity.

References: [worklog/2026-06-12.md](worklog/2026-06-12.md); related BUG-0020, BUG-0021, BUG-0023, BUG-0025.

### BUG-0025 — Server-side KB MCP call 401s under the project search connection identity

Area: infra. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-12, fixed 2026-06-12).

Symptom: on the `agent_framework` / Foundry IQ path (`cosmosdb` mode), after BUG-0024's search-MI → OpenAI User grant made the knowledge base's *inner* query-planning model call succeed (a direct REST `/retrieve` with an operator token now returns grounded `Benefit_Options.pdf` content), the end-to-end chat through the backend still returns the out-of-domain fallback with **no `tool`, `reasoning`, or `citation` SSE frames** and **no backend error** (`200 OK`). A standalone orchestrator diagnostic that reproduces the production wiring (credential → FoundryIQ llm → Foundry agents provider → cosmosdb client → `agent_framework` orchestrator) with `openai` + `agent_framework` DEBUG logging exposes the real failure in the Responses-API event stream:

```text
McpListTools(server_label='cwyd-kb', tools=[], type='mcp_list_tools', error=None)
ResponseMcpListToolsInProgressEvent(...)
ChatClientException / openai.APIError: Authentication failed when connecting to the MCP server:
  https://srch-<SUFFIX>.search.windows.net:443/knowledgebases/cwyd-kb/mcp:
  Response status code does not indicate success: 401 (Unauthorized). Verify your authentication headers.
```

The Responses API attempts `mcp_list_tools` against the KB MCP endpoint, gets `401`, and the agent ends up with an empty tool list (`tools=[]`) → no grounding → the out-of-domain refusal. In the live backend the orchestrator's `run()` catches only `AzureError`, so this `ChatClientException` / `openai.APIError` does not surface as a clean SSE `error` frame — it manifests as the refusal answer.

Root cause: the KB retrieval tool is attached **server-side**. `AgentFrameworkOrchestrator._build_kb_tool()` returns `MCPTool(server_url=…/knowledgebases/cwyd-kb/mcp, require_approval="never", allowed_tools=["knowledge_base_retrieve"], project_connection_id=<search connection>)`, serialized via `.as_dict()` into the agent's `extra_tools`. The Responses API therefore opens the MCP connection **itself**, under the *project search connection's* identity (`search-srch-<SUFFIX>`, category `CognitiveSearch`, `authType AAD`, no explicit managed-identity binding — the live connection reports `useWorkspaceManagedIdentity: false`, and `ai-project-search-connection.bicep` creates it with bare `authType: 'AAD'`). That identity is not accepted by the search MCP endpoint: the search service runs `aadOrApiKey` auth with `aadAuthFailureMode: http401WithBearerChallenge`, where a *missing/invalid* token returns `401` (authentication) and an *under-privileged* token returns `403` (authorization). The `401` therefore means no valid bearer reaches the endpoint — the runtime is not presenting the project managed identity's token. The **project** MI *does* hold `Search Index Data Reader` on the search service (sufficient per the Foundry RBAC "retrieve from a knowledge base" row, and assigned 7 days earlier so propagation is ruled out), but it is not the identity the server-side MCP path presents.

This is distinct from BUG-0020 and BUG-0024:

- BUG-0020 fixed the **SDK-side** (client-side) MCP connect via the Agent Framework `header_provider` / default-`Authorization` httpx client, minting the bearer from the *backend's* own credential. The GA pattern (ADR 0025, BUG-0021/0022) moved MCP execution **server-side** (`project_connection_id`), so that hook no longer runs — the connect is now authenticated by Foundry under the connection identity, not by our process.
- BUG-0024 was the KB's **inner** call (knowledge base → query-planning model), authenticated by the *search service* MI. BUG-0025 is the **outer** call (agent → KB MCP endpoint), authenticated by the *project connection* identity. BUG-0024's verification used a direct `/retrieve` with an operator token for the outer call, so it exercised only the inner hop and never surfaced this outer-hop `401`.

Why it was not caught earlier: orchestrator unit tests fake the agent + Responses API entirely, so the server-side `mcp_list_tools` connect is never exercised; this is the first end-to-end agent run against the live KB MCP endpoint with the project connection identity, and the failure is swallowed (the agent refuses rather than erroring).

Root cause confirmed against the read-only reference architecture (whose server-side KB MCP grounding works): CWYD points the `MCPTool` at the **wrong category of connection**. The KB MCP tool's `project_connection_id` must reference a dedicated **`RemoteTool` / `ProjectManagedIdentity`** connection that targets the KB MCP URL and pins the token audience — not the general-purpose `CognitiveSearch` / `AAD` connection CWYD reuses. The reference architecture creates one connection per KB at post-deploy via `PUT …/connections/{kb}-mcp?api-version=2025-04-01-preview` with this payload:

```json
{ "properties": {
    "category": "RemoteTool",
    "target": "https://srch-<SUFFIX>.search.windows.net/knowledgebases/<kb>/mcp?api-version=2025-11-01-preview",
    "authType": "ProjectManagedIdentity",
    "useWorkspaceManagedIdentity": true,
    "isSharedToAll": true,
    "audience": "https://search.azure.com",
    "metadata": { "ApiType": "Azure" } } }
```

The explicit `audience: https://search.azure.com` is the linchpin: it makes Agent Service mint a **project-MI** token for the **search** audience and present it to the MCP endpoint. CWYD's `CognitiveSearch` / bare-`AAD` connection (`useWorkspaceManagedIdentity: false`, no `audience`) mints no usable token for the generic server-side MCP path, so the endpoint sees no valid bearer → `401`, `mcp_list_tools` returns `tools=[]`, and the agent refuses. The reference architecture keeps a `CognitiveSearch` connection too, but only as the *base* search connection — and even that sets `useWorkspaceManagedIdentity: true` (`modules/aifp-connections.bicep`); the KB tool uses the separate `RemoteTool` connection. The reference architecture also grants the project MI **both** `Search Index Data Reader` **and** `Search Service Contributor` on the search service (CWYD granted only Reader), and grants the search MI `Cognitive Services OpenAI User` on the AI Services account — identical to CWYD's BUG-0024 grant, which is the part CWYD already matches.

Fix (applied + verified live 2026-06-12, operator-approved): (1) created a `cwyd-kb-mcp` `RemoteTool` / `ProjectManagedIdentity` connection on the project using the reference architecture's payload (`category: RemoteTool`, `authType: ProjectManagedIdentity`, `useWorkspaceManagedIdentity: true`, `isSharedToAll: true`, `audience: https://search.azure.com`, `target` = the `cwyd-kb` MCP URL, `metadata.ApiType: Azure`) — GET-verified all six properties; (2) pointed `AZURE_AI_SEARCH_CONNECTION_NAME` at `cwyd-kb-mcp` (the gitignored `.env`); (3) granted the project MI `Search Service Contributor` on the search service so it now holds **both** `Search Index Data Reader` and `Search Service Contributor` (matching the reference architecture). Verified by re-running the standalone orchestrator diagnostic against the live environment: the Responses-API stream now shows `mcp_call_arguments.delta` (real `knowledge_base_retrieve` queries) followed by `response.mcp_call.completed` (no `error`), and the orchestrator emits two `citation` frames plus a grounded `answer` about Contoso Electronics benefits (Northwind Health Plus / Standard) with `【N:1†source】` citation markers — **no `401`, no `tools=[]`, no out-of-domain fallback**. This confirms the `agent_framework`/Foundry IQ retrieval path now grounds. **End-to-end verified:** a first live `/api/conversation` test still returned the fallback — not a BUG-0025 regression, but because the persisted `RuntimeConfig` pinned `orchestrator_name='langgraph'`, which `resolve_effective_config` overlays *on top of* the env's `CWYD_ORCHESTRATOR_NAME=agent_framework`, so the backend dispatched to `langgraph` (client-side search + strict-prompt over-refusal) and never exercised the fixed path. After flipping the override to `agent_framework` via `PATCH /api/admin/config` (live-reload, no restart), the same query returned a **4608-byte grounded answer** with two `mcp://searchindex/…` `citation` frames and `【6:0†source】` markers about the Northwind Health Plus / Standard plans — so the conversation regression is **fixed end-to-end through the real request path**. The earlier Option B test (granting the account/workspace MI `Search Index Data Reader`) is confirmed **not** the fix — the bare-`AAD` connection with `useWorkspaceManagedIdentity: false` never presents that identity (re-tested `401` ~5 min post-grant) — and that spurious grant is being reverted. Still to do (tracked): make the connection + project-MI `Search Service Contributor` durable in `infra/` (a Bicep `RemoteTool` connection resource — CWYD's KB name `cwyd-kb` is static, unlike the reference architecture's dynamic content-pack KBs, so a seed script is unnecessary). Separately consider broadening the orchestrator's `run()` except so an MCP `ChatClientException` / `openai.APIError` surfaces as a clean SSE `error` frame (tracked separately; Hard Rule #12).

References: [worklog/2026-06-12.md](worklog/2026-06-12.md); related BUG-0020, BUG-0024; [adr/0025-foundry-prompt-agent-ga-pattern.md](adr/0025-foundry-prompt-agent-ga-pattern.md).

### BUG-0026 — agent_framework KB narration keys on `function_call`, but server-side MCP surfaces as `mcp_server_tool_call`

Area: backend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-12).

Symptom: on the `agent_framework` / Foundry IQ path the grounded SSE stream carries only `citation` + `answer` frames — the FE "thinking" panel stays empty even though a knowledge-base retrieval clearly ran (citations are present). The earlier `e65bf826` "Narrate KB search before tool events" change was meant to populate the panel but has no visible effect on the live server-side path.

Root cause: `AgentFrameworkOrchestrator._update_to_events` maps each streamed content block to SSE events. The KB-search reasoning narration (`_KB_SEARCH_NARRATION`) and the `tool` event are emitted only inside the `ctype == "function_call"` branch. After the GA-FULL migration (`8f83ad69`, "Use build_agent seam and server-side KB tool") KB retrieval is attached as a server-side `MCPTool(project_connection_id=…)` and runs inside the Responses API. The `agent_framework_openai` chat client maps that server-side call to a `Content.from_mcp_server_tool_call(...)` block whose `.type` is **`mcp_server_tool_call`** (tool name on `.tool_name`, not `.name`) — not `function_call`. The orchestrator has no branch for that content type, so it falls through: no narration, no tool event. The narration added later (`e65bf826`) inherited the same `function_call`-only condition, so it never fired on the live server-side path. This is the concrete mechanism behind BUG-0013's empty-panel symptom for the `agent_framework` + KB path.

Fix: broaden the `function_call` branch in `_update_to_events` to also handle `mcp_server_tool_call`, resolving the tool name from either `.name` (client-side function tools) or `.tool_name` (server-side MCP). Both paths then drive the same `_KB_SEARCH_NARRATION` reasoning event + `tool` event, so the FE thinking panel populates whenever KB retrieval runs, regardless of which retrieval transport executed.

References: [worklog/2026-06-12.md](worklog/2026-06-12.md); BUG-0013 (umbrella symptom); BUG-0025 (the infra fix that made server-side retrieval actually run, which exposed this). SDK evidence: `agent_framework_openai/_chat_client.py` streaming `response.output_item.added` → `case "mcp_call"` → `Content.from_mcp_server_tool_call(...)`; `agent_framework/_types.py` content-type literal `"mcp_server_tool_call"`.

### BUG-0027 — KB-search narration shows only at the end of the wait, not during it (and not at all on `langgraph`)

Area: backend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-12; U1 shared-pipeline seam + U1b router gating landed test-first; U2 `agent_framework` dedup landed + fixed 2026-06-14).

Symptom: while the assistant is working, the FE "thinking" panel shows only the "Thinking" label and animated dots. The actual reasoning narration ("Searching the knowledge base for relevant sources…") never appears *during* the multi-second wait — on the `agent_framework` / Foundry IQ path it flashes in for an instant at the very end (immediately before the `answer` arrives and the panel collapses), and on the `langgraph` path it never appears at all. The user sees no indication of *what* the model is doing while they wait.

Root cause: BUG-0026 correctly made the narration reach the stream, but it is emitted **too late to function as a during-the-wait indicator**. On the `agent_framework` path the narration + `tool` event are produced inside `_update_to_events` when the `mcp_server_tool_call` content block surfaces — and Foundry IQ runs KB retrieval **server-side**, so that block does not surface until retrieval has already completed. The whole `reasoning → tool → citation → answer` sequence therefore arrives in a tight burst at the end; during the actual multi-second wait no `reasoning` frame has been emitted yet, so `m.reasoning` is empty and the panel renders only dots, then everything floods in and the `answer` immediately collapses the panel. On the `langgraph` path retrieval runs in-code at the top of `run()` and blocks before any event is yielded, so it emits nothing upfront either. The FE reasoning pipeline (streamChat → MessageInput → ChatContext → MessageList) is correctly wired and renders `m.reasoning` in the force-open panel while streaming — the defect is backend **timing + coverage**, not a frontend bug.

Fix: emit the narration **upfront in the shared `run_chat` pipeline** — after the content-safety / RAI guards pass and *before* the orchestrator runs — via a new `retrieval_hint: str | None` parameter carrying the canonical `KB_SEARCH_NARRATION` string. The router passes the hint only when a knowledge source is configured for the active mode. Because the seam is in the orchestrator-agnostic pipeline, every current and future orchestrator inherits the during-the-wait narration with zero per-provider code; an orchestrator that emits its own native reasoning simply streams more frames after it. The now-redundant late per-call narration in `agent_framework._update_to_events` is then removed (the `tool` event stays). `sse_stream` is a true async generator, so the upfront frame reaches the browser as soon as it is yielded — i.e. at the start of the wait. Landed test-first across three units: U1 (the `run_chat` seam + `retrieval_hint` parameter + `KB_SEARCH_NARRATION` constant + 5 pipeline tests), U1b (router gating -- `retrieval_hint = KB_SEARCH_NARRATION if search is not None else None` in `conversation.py`, passed only when a search backend is wired), and U2 (2026-06-14 -- removed the now-redundant late per-call narration block from `agent_framework._update_to_events`, keeping the raw `tool` event; dropped the now-unused `_KB_SEARCH_NARRATION` orchestrator constant). The two former "narrates" orchestrator tests now assert that a KB retrieval `function_call` / `mcp_server_tool_call` yields only the `tool` event with **no** `reasoning` frame, and the upstream during-the-wait narration stays covered by the `run_chat` pipeline tests. Net after U2: the `agent_framework` path no longer double-narrates -- the single during-the-wait `reasoning` frame is emitted upfront by `run_chat`, and the orchestrator streams only its native `tool` / `citation` / `answer` frames afterward.

References: [worklog/2026-06-12.md](worklog/2026-06-12.md); BUG-0026 (made the narration reach the stream — this fixes *when* it is emitted); BUG-0013 (umbrella reasoning-feed symptom). Seam: `run_chat(..., retrieval_hint=...)` in `core/pipelines/chat.py` emits a leading `reasoning` frame; constant `KB_SEARCH_NARRATION` lives there and the router imports it.

### BUG-0028 — `langgraph` over-refuses in-domain queries (strict CWYD guardrail → gpt-5.1 fallback)

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-12; root cause confirmed by live prompt-variant probes; prompt-softening fix landed + live-verified 2026-06-14).

Symptom: with the active orchestrator set to `langgraph`, a normal in-domain question ("tell me about employee benefits") returns the out-of-domain fallback ("The requested information is not available in the retrieved data. Please try another query or topic.") — a single `answer` frame, no `tool` / `reasoning` / `citation` frames, HTTP 200, no backend error. The same deployment and corpus ground correctly on the `agent_framework` path.

Root cause: the `langgraph` orchestrator does raw chat completion — it retrieves with client-side Azure AI Search, injects the results as a `[docN]` "Sources:" system message, and streams the chat model with the shared CWYD system prompt (`compose_cwyd_instructions(CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY)`). That prompt ends with the non-negotiable `CWYD_GUARDRAIL`, whose grounding clause — "if the retrieved documents do not contain enough information to answer the query, or if no documents are retrieved, your only response is [fallback]" — makes `gpt-5.1` read "enough information" ultra-conservatively and refuse relevant-but-broad queries. Retrieval and message structure are ruled out: direct index search returns 5 relevant hits, and a minimal prompt + the same injected sources grounds reliably. `agent_framework` survives the identical prompt because Foundry IQ executes retrieval server-side and presents the KB results as authoritative tool outputs, which the agent runtime is tuned to ground on; the raw chat-completion path obeys the strict prompt literally.

Confirmation (five live guardrail-variant probes, temp 0.0 + default): the strict prompt refuses the benefits query 8/8 (temperature is not the lever); softening the guardrail grounds most in-domain queries (health plans, handbook, "tell me about the company") while all out-of-domain / creative requests still refuse — but the single broad "tell me about employee benefits" overview sits exactly on gpt-5.1's grounding decision boundary for this small corpus (non-deterministic even at temp 0.0), and a naively permissive guardrail regresses the BUG-0011 grounding guarantee (leaks ungrounded creative content such as "write me a poem about dragons"). So there is a genuine tension: permissive enough to ground broad in-domain queries vs. strict enough to refuse ungrounded creative / out-of-domain requests.

Impact by mode: in `cosmosdb` mode the intended path is `agent_framework` (Foundry IQ), which grounds correctly end-to-end, so `langgraph` is a legacy / fallback path there. In `postgresql` mode `langgraph` is the only supported orchestrator (no pgvector knowledge source for Foundry IQ — ADR 0021 / 0022), so this over-refusal blocks answering entirely for every postgres deployment. This is the "Phase 3 (prompt softening)" work already tracked in the worklog.

Secondary finding (separate code defect): `LLMProvider.complete()` calls `self.chat(messages, deployment=...)` without threading `temperature` / `max_tokens`, so the configured `openai_temperature` (0.0) and `openai_max_tokens` are ignored on the `langgraph` path — the model runs at its default temperature, contributing to the boundary non-determinism. Threading them was attempted as a follow-on unit but **reverted**: passing `max_tokens` made every `langgraph` chat 500 on `gpt-5.1`, which rejects `max_tokens` in favor of `max_completion_tokens` (tracked as BUG-0029). The threading is deferred behind that fix.

Fix (landed 2026-06-14, with operator consent per Hard Rule #10 — edits the non-negotiable, BUG-0011-protected shared CWYD safety prompt): softened the `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` grounding clause and replaced the `CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY` strict v1 in/out-of-domain section ("read sentence by sentence", "only when … enough information", "think twice", "you cannot decide") with a relevance-based "## On answering from the retrieved documents:" section. The new guardrail directive is positive and relevance-anchored — *"When the retrieved documents contain information relevant to the user's question, you **must** answer using that information and cite each claim. Do not refuse just because the documents are brief, fragmentary, or do not cover every detail … Only when none of the retrieved documents are relevant … your only response is [fallback]"* — and explicitly bans ungrounded creative content (*"Never produce creative content (such as stories, poems, jokes, or song lyrics) unless the retrieved documents contain it"*) so the BUG-0011 grounding guarantee is preserved. The exact fixed fallback string, the `[doc+index]` citation format, the no-URLs rule, and the `compose_cwyd_instructions` guardrail-wrapping (BUG-0011 invariant) are all unchanged. Landed test-first: four new invariant assertions in `test_definitions.py` (relevance-based grounding directive present, strict "enough information" wording absent, creative-content ban present, strict v1 body drag dropped) plus the existing fallback/citation/wrapping assertions stay green (16/16). Live-verified on `langgraph` + `gpt-5.1` + `cwyd-index`: "tell me about employee benefits" grounded 3/3 (the prior on-the-boundary query), "what health plans are available?" grounded, "what is the capital of France?" and "write me a poem about dragons" both returned the fixed fallback. Both orchestrators share the prompt, so `agent_framework` inherits the softer grounding while keeping the same safety ban.

References: [worklog/2026-06-12.md](worklog/2026-06-12.md) (the "Conversation regression" + operator-decision sections, "Phase 3 prompt softening"); [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md) (the realized fix + BUG-0029 discovery); BUG-0011 (the guardrail wrapping invariant the fix preserves); BUG-0029 (the `max_tokens` → `max_completion_tokens` defect that deferred the secondary temperature threading); ADR 0021 / ADR 0022 (the db_type ↔ orchestrator coupling that locks postgres mode to `langgraph`).

### BUG-0029 — `FoundryIQ.chat()` sends `max_tokens`, rejected by `gpt-5.1` (`max_completion_tokens` required)

Area: backend. Severity: medium. Status: open (found 2026-06-14 while attempting the BUG-0028 secondary temperature/`max_tokens` threading).

Symptom: threading the configured `openai_max_tokens` through `BaseLLMProvider.complete()` into `FoundryIQ.chat()` made every `langgraph` conversation return `500 Internal Server Error`. Backend log: `RuntimeError: Error code: 400 - {'error': {'message': "Unsupported parameter: 'max_tokens' is not supported with this model. Use 'max_completion_tokens' instead.", 'type': 'invalid_request_error', 'param': 'max_tokens', 'code': 'unsupported_parameter'}}`.

Root cause: `FoundryIQ.chat()` / `chat_stream()` forward the sampling cap as the legacy Chat Completions `max_tokens` parameter. Current Azure OpenAI chat models (`gpt-5.1`, gpt-5 family, o-series) removed `max_tokens` in favor of `max_completion_tokens`; sending `max_tokens` is a hard `400`. The defect is **latent** in the shipped code because `complete()` (the only `langgraph` chat entry point) does not pass `max_tokens`, so the parameter is never populated on that path — it only fires when a caller explicitly threads `max_tokens` (as the BUG-0028 secondary fix did). That threading was reverted, so the live tree is back to green.

Fix (separate unit, not yet landed): in `FoundryIQ.chat()` and `chat_stream()` send `max_completion_tokens` instead of `max_tokens` (the forward-compatible name accepted by current chat models). Update `test_chat_passes_temperature_and_max_tokens` accordingly. Then re-attempt the BUG-0028 secondary improvement (thread `settings.openai.temperature` / `max_tokens` through `complete()`), but first confirm `gpt-5.1` accepts a custom `temperature` — gpt-5 reasoning models constrain `temperature` to the default, so the chat path may need to omit it for those deployments.

References: BUG-0028 (the deferred secondary temperature threading that surfaced this); [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md).

### BUG-0030 — citation shape diverges per orchestrator (`agent_framework` native `【N:M†source】` + raw `mcp://` id vs `langgraph` `[docN]` + filename)

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-14 by side-by-side comparison of the two orchestrators answering "tell me about employee benefits"; fixed 2026-06-15 via fallback (b) — app-side by-key citation enrichment + a null-url mapping fix).

Symptom: the same question against the same corpus produces two different citation shapes depending on the active orchestrator.

* `langgraph` answer: inline `[doc1]` markers; **Sources** block lists `Benefit_Options.pdf` (the friendly filename).
* `agent_framework` answer: inline `【6:0†source】` markers (OpenAI Responses native annotation format); **Sources** block lists `mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>` (the raw search-index document key, no filename, with an `[Open source](mcp://…)` link that is not user-meaningful).

Root cause: the two paths ground and cite through entirely different mechanisms, even though they share the same system instructions.

* `langgraph` ([langgraph.py](../../src/backend/core/providers/orchestrators/langgraph.py)) retrieves client-side via `BaseSearch.search`, injects the hits as a numbered `Sources:\n[doc1]: <content>` system message (`format_sources_block`), and the shared `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` instructs the model to cite with `[docN]`. After the answer streams, `filter_to_referenced` maps each referenced `[docN]` marker to a `Citation(id="[doc1]", title=<src.title>=Benefit_Options.pdf, url=<src.url>)`. The `[docN]` contract is fully honored, and the title is the friendly filename the search provider returns.
* `agent_framework` ([agent_framework.py](../../src/backend/core/providers/orchestrators/agent_framework.py)) grounds via the server-side Foundry IQ Knowledge Base MCP tool. The Responses model performs retrieval through that tool and emits its **own native** citation annotations — inline `【N:M†source】` markers plus `Content.annotations` (`type == "citation"`) whose `file_id` / `url` is the raw search-index document key (`mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>`), not the filename. `citations_from_annotations` ([citations.py](../../src/backend/core/tools/citations.py)) sets `id = file_id or url or title`, so the raw key flows straight through; the `[docN]` rule in the shared prompt is effectively overridden by the KB tool's annotation contract and never produces `[docN]` markers on this path.

So the system **instructions** are identical (`compose_cwyd_instructions(...)` for both — confirmed: `langgraph` threads `system_prompt=effective.cwyd_agent_instructions`; `agent_framework` applies the same via `build_agent` → `_resolve_definition`), but the **effective citation behavior** diverges because grounding is in-prompt (`[docN]`) for one and server-side-tool (native annotations + document keys) for the other. This is a backend defect, distinct from the FE-rendering bugs BUG-0014 (markdown→HTML), BUG-0015 (block styling), and BUG-0016 (`[docN]` superscript) — all three assume a `[docN]` marker is already present, which is exactly what the `agent_framework` path fails to produce.

Fix direction (not yet landed; needs operator direction): normalize the `agent_framework` output to the v1 citation shape so both orchestrators emit one `Citation` shape and one inline-marker convention. That means, on the `agent_framework` path: (a) rewrite the inline native `【N:M†source】` markers in the answer text to sequential `[docN]` markers; (b) build the parallel `Citation` list with `id="[docN]"` and a friendly `title` resolved from the annotation `title` (or a KB-metadata lookup keyed by the document key) instead of passing the raw `mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>` through. Open question for the fix: confirm what the Foundry IQ KB annotation actually carries for `title` / display name (it may already include the filename), which decides whether a metadata lookup is needed or the title is already present and just dropped today.

References: BUG-0026 (the related `mcp_server_tool_call` content-shape difference on the same `agent_framework` path); BUG-0016 (the FE `[docN]` superscript rendering that depends on this backend normalization); BUG-0011 (the shared-prompt guardrail wrapping that both paths preserve **for the default prompt only** — see BUG-0031 for the override-case gap); [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md).

**Update 2026-06-14 (live integration-lane capture):** this does **not** reproduce on the current live `agent_framework` deployment. A real `POST /api/conversation` ("What health plans are available?") returned inline `[doc1]` markers in the answer text and a structured `Citation(id="[doc1]", title="Benefit_Options.pdf", snippet=<doc text>)` — the normalized v1 shape on both the inline-marker and `Citation` fronts. This answers the open question above: the Foundry IQ KB annotation now carries `file_id="[doc1]"` **and** a friendly filename `title`, so `citations_from_annotations` (`id = file_id or url or title`) passes the normalized `[doc1]` + filename shape straight through with no code change. The new integration lane asserts this as a live regression guard (`tests/integration/test_conversation_live.py::test_in_domain_citation_ids_use_normalized_docn_shape`): if Foundry IQ / the SDK regress to native `【N:M†source】` markers or raw `mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>` ids, that test fails. No code fix landed — the normalization is Foundry-IQ-side and may be KB-config-dependent — so the table-row status stays **open** pending operator confirmation to close. (A separate minor wire defect surfaced in the same capture: `Citation.url` serialized as the string `"None"` — see BUG-0033.)

**Update 2026-06-14 (second live capture — SUPERSEDES the note above):** the divergence **does** reproduce. A fresh A0 capture (same query, throwaway integration-lane probe forcing the `agent_framework` orchestrator) returned the **un-normalized** shape on both fronts: the answer text literally contains native `【6:1†source】` / `【6:0†source】` markers, and `citations_from_annotations` returned `id == title == url == mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>`, `snippet == ""`, `score == null`. The two captures disagree because the friendly `[doc1]` + filename output is **Foundry-IQ-KB-config-dependent**; the live KB now emits the native shape, so a code-side normalizer is required (the earlier "no code change" conclusion was an artifact of a transient KB config). The integration guard `test_in_domain_citation_ids_use_normalized_docn_shape` correctly fails against this deployment — it is catching the real regression.

Three findings shape the fix:

* **Mapping is offset-anchored, not `N:M`.** Each annotation carries `annotated_regions = [{type: "text_span", start_index, end_index}]` — the exact character span of one native marker in the answer text (verified: first span `78..90` lands on the first 12-char `【6:1†source】`, offsets align with the buffered answer 1:1). `citations_from_annotations` already groups annotations by source id in first-occurrence order and aggregates every span under `Citation.metadata["annotated_regions"]`. The `N:M` inside the marker is misleading — `N` is constant and `M` is the KB's internal source index, **inverted** from citation order here (`M=1`→Citation[0], `M=0`→Citation[1]). The normalizer maps by the **citation grouping order** (Citation[0]→`[doc1]`, Citation[1]→`[doc2]`) and rewrites each citation's spans to its `[docN]`.
* **Friendly title + snippet are NOT in the annotation.** The full `raw_representation` is `{type: "url_citation", start_index, end_index, title: "mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>", url: "mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>"}`; `additional_properties` is only `{annotation_index: <n>}`. No filename, no chunk text anywhere. So title/snippet recovery cannot read annotation fields — it needs either a Foundry IQ KB citation-field-mapping change (infra) or a secondary Azure Search lookup keyed by the document key (code), or it accepts a degraded `[docN]` id with no friendly title/snippet. This fork is surfaced to the operator and gates the right-panel snippet, **not** the marker normalization.
* **The normalizer is independent of that fork.** Rewriting `【N:M†source】` → `[docN]` and renumbering citation ids to `[docN]` is fully determined by `annotated_regions` + grouping order, so it lands first as a pure unit; title/snippet recovery follows once the fork is decided.

Fix landing: a pure `normalize_kb_citations(answer, citations)` in [citations.py](../../src/backend/core/tools/citations.py) — rewrite each `annotated_regions` span to the citation's 1-based `[docN]`, renumber ids to `[docN]`, strip any residual native marker — then wire it into `agent_framework.run` after `citations_from_annotations`.
