Status stays **open** until the normalizer + wire-in land and the live guard passes.

**Update 2026-06-14 (option (a) seed change — KB citation source-data fields):** the marker normalizer (`normalize_kb_citations`) has landed and the live guard passes on the marker/id front. For the remaining title/snippet recovery fork the operator chose **(a) KB citation-field-mapping config** (over the app-side secondary lookup (b) or the degraded `[docN]`-only (c)), because a Foundry-IQ-side mapping keeps recovery out of every orchestrator's code (Hard Rule #20). Implemented in the `post_provision` knowledge-source seed: `_build_knowledge_base_seed` now sets `searchIndexParameters.sourceDataFields = [{"name": "title"}, {"name": "url"}, {"name": "content"}]` (Azure AI Search KB REST `2025-11-01-preview`, "request additional fields for referenced source data"), so the KB returns the friendly filename (`title`), document `url`, and chunk `content` snippet as citation source data instead of only the raw `mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>`. Module constant `KNOWLEDGE_SOURCE_SOURCE_DATA_FIELDS`; test `test_build_knowledge_base_seed_shape` updated (18/18). **Live verification still required before close:** a re-seed (`azd hooks run postprovision` / `python -m scripts.post_provision`) + a fresh A0 capture must confirm the Responses model's `url_citation` annotation now carries a friendly `title` / snippet. If the annotation `title` still shows `mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>` after the re-seed (the knob may only enrich the tool's source-data payload, not the emitted annotation), a follow-up code unit in `citations_from_annotations` reads the source-data fields, or falls back to (b)/(c). Status stays **open** until the live capture confirms friendly title/snippet on the served `Citation`.

**Live verification 2026-06-14 (re-seed + A0 capture) — option (a) is INSUFFICIENT.** Re-seeded the live KB (`python -m scripts.post_provision` → `knowledge base 'cwyd-kb' ready`), then captured a fresh `agent_framework` A0 run. The answer marker/id parity holds (inline `[doc1]`, no native `【N:M†source】` leak), but the served `Citation` still carries `title` = `url` = the raw `mcp://searchindex/<doc-key>` with an empty `snippet`. The `sourceDataFields` knob enriches the KB tool's *referenced source data* but does **not** surface on the Responses `url_citation` annotation `citations_from_annotations` reads. The seed change stays in (correct KB config) but does not close this bug. **Fallback (b) now proven viable:** a read-only `get_document(key=<doc-key>)` against the chat index resolved both captured doc-keys to real documents (`id` == the `<doc-key>` hash, `title` == the sample filename, `content` == the chunk snippet), so a secondary Search lookup by doc-key is deterministic. Decision pending operator: implement (b) (app-side enrichment after `citations_from_annotations`, honoring Hard Rule #20 R2) or accept (c) degraded `[docN]`-only. Status stays **open**.

**Fixed 2026-06-15 (fallback (b) implemented + live-confirmed).** The operator chose **(b)** — an app-side secondary Azure AI Search lookup keyed by the KB document id — over the degraded `[docN]`-only (c). Landed as three test-first units, all honoring Hard Rule #20 R2 (citation shaping stays in [citations.py](../../src/backend/core/tools/citations.py), provider-free):

* **`enrich_kb_citations(citations, fetch_document)`** — for each citation whose `mcp://searchindex/<key>` id (read from `metadata["source_id"]`) resolves, backfills `title`/`snippet`/`url` from the fetched document; preserves `id`/`score`/`metadata` (including the original `source_id`). `fetch_document` is an **injected** `Callable[[str], Awaitable[SearchResult | None]]`, so `citations.py` imports no Search provider — the single response-format point.
* **`BaseSearch.get_document_by_key(key)`** with an `AzureSearch` override (`client.get_document(key=…, selected_fields=["id","content","title","url"])`): `ResourceNotFoundError` → `None` (soft miss), other `AzureError` → log + re-raise (Hard Rule #14); a by-key fetch carries no relevance `score`.
* **Wire-in** in `agent_framework.run` after `normalize_kb_citations`: best-effort `await enrich_kb_citations(citations, self._search.get_document_by_key)`, guarded by `try/except AzureError` → `logger.warning` + degrade to the raw-id citation (never drops it). The orchestrator gained a keyword-only `search: BaseSearch | None`, threaded by the router from the active Search provider.
* **Null-url fix** in `AzureSearch._to_result`: `url=str(doc.get("url", ""))` produced the string `"None"` for a present-but-`null` `url` field (the `""` default only fires when the key is *absent*), which the enrichment newly exercised. Changed to `url=str(doc.get("url") or "")`. This is a **second** `str(None)`→`"None"` site, distinct from BUG-0033's `citations_from_annotations` boundary fix, and also cleans the `langgraph` retrieval path for url-less documents.

Live A0 capture (real `agent_framework` deployment, same query) now returns the normalized v1 shape end-to-end: inline `[doc1]`, `Citation(id="[doc1]", title="Benefit_Options.pdf", snippet=<chunk text>, url="")`, no native `【N:M†source】` markers, `metadata["source_id"]` retaining the raw `mcp://searchindex/<key>` for traceability. See [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md).

### BUG-0031 — Authored-prompt guardrail wrapping applied only on `agent_framework`, not `langgraph`

Area: backend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-14 while tracing whether the two orchestrators share instruction-building code, in response to the parity question behind BUG-0030; fixed 2026-06-14).

Observed: instruction composition is two parallel code paths, not one shared seam. They converge only when no operator override is set.

* Default (no `cwyd_agent_instructions` override): both paths resolve to `CWYD_AGENT.instructions` = `compose_cwyd_instructions(CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY)` — identical, guardrail-wrapped text. No divergence.
* With an operator override: the paths diverge.
  * `agent_framework`: `build_agent` → `_resolve_definition` ([base.py](../../src/backend/core/providers/agents/base.py)) calls `definition.model_copy(update={"instructions": compose_cwyd_instructions(text)})`, so the authored text is bookended by the fixed `CWYD_GUARDRAIL`.
  * `langgraph`: the router threads `system_prompt=effective.cwyd_agent_instructions` and `LangGraphOrchestrator.run` ([langgraph.py](../../src/backend/core/providers/orchestrators/langgraph.py)) injects it verbatim as a `ChatRole.SYSTEM` message — no `compose_cwyd_instructions` call anywhere on this path.

Root cause: the stored override is raw (un-wrapped). The PATCH handler ([admin.py](../../src/backend/routers/admin.py)) screens the prompt through the RAI gate (`PROMPT_FIELDS`) but stores `payload[field]` un-wrapped; `resolve_effective_config` ([services/admin.py](../../src/backend/services/admin.py)) overlays that raw value onto `effective.cwyd_agent_instructions`. The guardrail wrap exists only at agent_framework read-time (`_resolve_definition`) and in the default constant — there is no shared composition step, so anything that consumes `effective.cwyd_agent_instructions` directly (langgraph) gets the un-wrapped persona. (That the override is stored raw is confirmed by the fact that `_resolve_definition` wraps at read-time; if storage were already wrapped, agent_framework would double-wrap.)

Impact / reachability: only reachable when an operator saves a custom `cwyd_agent_instructions` override AND the active orchestrator is `langgraph` (the sole path in `postgresql` / pgvector mode, and a selectable option in `azure_search` mode). The malicious-prompt vector that motivated BUG-0011 is NOT reintroduced — the RAI gate still rejects unsafe authored prompts at write time. What is lost on `langgraph` is the non-safety guardrail behavior the authored persona is supposed to be bookended by: the out-of-domain refusal directive, the `[docN]` citation instruction, and the fixed fallback string. With a custom persona the langgraph orchestrator effectively runs persona-only, diverging from agent_framework. This also means BUG-0030's note that "both paths preserve" the BUG-0011 wrapping is accurate only for the default prompt.

Fix (landed 2026-06-14): instruction composition is now a single shared seam both consumers call — `resolve_cwyd_instructions(override_text: str | None) -> str` in [definitions.py](../../src/backend/core/agents/definitions.py). It returns `compose_cwyd_instructions(override_text)` when the override is non-blank and `compose_cwyd_instructions(CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY)` (= `CWYD_AGENT.instructions`) when it is `None` / blank, so a blank-clear falls back to the wrapped default. Both consumers route the **raw** stored override through this one seam, each wrapping it exactly once: `resolve_effective_config` ([services/admin.py](../../src/backend/services/admin.py)) re-resolves `values["cwyd_agent_instructions"]` through the seam after the overlay loop (this is the value `langgraph` injects as its SYSTEM message), and `_resolve_definition` ([base.py](../../src/backend/core/providers/agents/base.py)) calls the same seam instead of an inline `compose_cwyd_instructions`. There is no double-wrap because each consumer wraps the raw override (`overrides.cwyd_agent_instructions`), never the already-wrapped effective value. The three previous composition references (default constant + `_resolve_definition` + the absent langgraph wrap) collapse to one definition. Tests: `test_definitions.py` pins the seam's None/blank/override behavior and that `resolve_cwyd_instructions(None) == CWYD_AGENT.instructions`; `test_services_admin.py` asserts the effective override is guardrail-wrapped (count == 1, body leads) and a blank override falls back to the default; `test_base.py` asserts the agent_framework path equals `resolve_cwyd_instructions(override)`; `test_conversation.py` asserts the router forwards a guardrail-wrapped `system_prompt` (the langgraph-boundary regression). Full v2 suite green (2247 passed, 1 skipped); `pyright --strict` clean on the three touched source files. Implemented as Option (a) from the original fix direction (wrap in `resolve_effective_config`) but keeping `_resolve_definition`'s wrap routed through the same seam rather than dropping it, so both paths share one composition function.

References: BUG-0011 (the original guardrail-wrapping fix this completes for the langgraph path); BUG-0030 (the citation-mechanism divergence found in the same parity investigation — same shared-seam fix family); BUG-0022 (the prior agent_framework override-handling fix); [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md).

### BUG-0032 — Admin prompt-override round-trip can double-wrap the guardrail

Area: backend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-14 during the BUG-0031 shared-seam fix; fixed 2026-06-19).

Observed: the effective CWYD instructions can carry the fixed `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` block twice when an operator saves a custom prompt that was seeded from the admin GET.

Mechanism:

1. `GET /api/admin/config` ([admin.py](../../src/backend/routers/admin.py)) returns `cwyd_agent_instructions = CWYD_AGENT.instructions`, which is the **wrapped** default — `compose_cwyd_instructions(CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY)` = body + `CWYD_GUARDRAIL`.
2. If the FE admin editor pre-populates the field from that GET, the operator is editing text that already contains the guardrail.
3. On `PATCH /api/admin/config` the RAI gate screens the prompt (passes) and stores it raw — the stored override now contains the guardrail.
4. At runtime the shared `resolve_cwyd_instructions` seam (BUG-0031) wraps the raw override via `compose_cwyd_instructions`, appending `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` a second time. The effective instructions contain two guardrail blocks.

Impact / reachability: only when an operator saves a custom `cwyd_agent_instructions` that includes the guardrail text (the common path if the editor seeds from the wrapped default). Not a safety regression — the guardrail is duplicated, never dropped, and the RAI write-gate still screens authored prompts — so severity is low. The cost is a bloated system prompt (the non-negotiable rules repeated) and a confusing authoring experience (the operator sees and must scroll past the fixed guardrail). Before BUG-0031 the duplication occurred only on `agent_framework` (`_resolve_definition` wrapped) while `langgraph` injected the operator's copy verbatim; after BUG-0031 both paths wrap, making the double-wrap consistent across orchestrators.

Fix (landed 2026-06-19): make the persona **body** the unit of storage and editing. Both admin read endpoints now expose the editable body instead of the wrapped runtime prompt — `GET /api/admin/config` ([config_endpoint](../../src/backend/routers/admin.py)) and the env baseline of `GET /api/admin/config/effective` ([config_effective_endpoint](../../src/backend/routers/admin.py)) return `CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY`, not `CWYD_AGENT.instructions`. The `/config/effective` override case already surfaced the raw authored override (itself a body), so it was correct. The runtime seam `resolve_effective_config` ([admin.py](../../src/backend/services/admin.py)) is **unchanged** — it still appends `CWYD_GUARDRAIL` exactly once via `resolve_cwyd_instructions` when building the effective prompt. So the editor never shows or round-trips the guardrail, the operator edits only the body, and the guardrail is applied once at runtime where it belongs. The `cwyd_agent_instructions` field on `AdminConfig` stays a single field whose value differs by surface by design (editable body on the admin reads, wrapped effective prompt on the runtime resolve); the divergence is documented in the two endpoint comments. `CWYD_AGENT` became unused in `admin.py` and its import was swapped to `CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY`. The alternative (strip a leading/trailing guardrail before re-wrapping) was rejected as brittle string surgery.

Verification: three existing contract tests updated to expect `CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY` (`test_config_surfaces_cwyd_agent_instructions_default`, `test_config_effective_returns_env_defaults_when_no_overrides`, `test_config_effective_overlays_cwyd_agent_instructions_override` — the last keeps the override-case assertion against the raw operator string); one new regression `test_config_effective_default_persona_excludes_guardrail` asserts the guardrail is absent from the editable default on both GET surfaces; the no-override env baseline tests assert `CWYD_GUARDRAIL not in instructions`. Admin router + service suites 133 passed; full backend suite 1070 passed / 0 failed. (Unrelated pre-existing tracked failure `ROUTERS-NON-ROUTE-CONTENT-DEBT` on `_DI_PARSER_PROBE_KEY` in the router-purity gate is from the BUG-0034 fix, not this change — confirmed by diff.)


References: BUG-0031 (the shared composition seam that made the double-wrap consistent and surfaced this round-trip); BUG-0011 (the original guardrail-wrapping invariant); [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md).

### BUG-0033 — `Citation.url` serializes as the string `"None"` on the `agent_framework` path

Area: backend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-14 via the live integration lane while capturing the BUG-0030 citation shape; fixed 2026-06-14).

Symptom: a live `POST /api/conversation` capture returned a citation whose `url` was the literal string `"None"` rather than `null` / `""`: `{"id": "[doc1]", "title": "Benefit_Options.pdf", "url": "None", ...}`. The Foundry IQ KB annotation carried no usable link, yet a `"None"` placeholder reached the wire, which the FE could render as a broken `None` link.

Root cause: `citations_from_annotations` ([citations.py](../../src/backend/core/tools/citations.py)) read each annotation field verbatim (`url = ann.get("url", "")`) and built the `Citation` from those raw values. When the KB source has no URL, the SDK surfaces the field as a Python `None` — or, once stringified upstream, the literal text `"None"` — and that value flowed straight into `Citation.url`. The same un-coerced read also fed the identity fallback `id = file_id or url or title`, so a `"None"` `file_id` could have become the citation id.

Fix (landed 2026-06-14): a single boundary helper `_clean_annotation_field(value: object) -> str` coerces both a Python `None` and the literal string `"None"` to `""`. The annotation adapter routes its four user-visible string reads — `file_id`, `url`, `title`, `snippet` — through it before assembling the `Citation`, so the placeholder is treated as absent: it never reaches `Citation.url`, and a `"None"` `file_id` / `url` / `title` no longer becomes an id (the fallback skips empties and the annotation is dropped when no real identity remains). The `langgraph` path is unaffected — it builds citations from `SearchResult` fields, not annotations.

Verification: `tests/backend/core/tools/test_citations.py` adds coverage for a `"None"`-string url → `""`, a Python `None` url → `""`, a `"None"` `file_id` falling back to the url for the id (and omitted from metadata), and an annotation whose every identity field is `"None"` being dropped. Full file green (22 passed); `pyright --strict` clean on `citations.py`; the shared AST gates pass (926).

References: BUG-0030 (the citation-shape parity investigation that surfaced this in the same live capture); BUG-0016 / BUG-0015 (the FE citation rendering that consumes this `Citation` shape); [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md).

### BUG-0034 — Uploaded document reports success but never appears in the documents list

Area: functions. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-14, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: an operator uploads a document through the admin Add-data UI; the request returns `200` with an `UploadResponse` (the UI shows success), but the document never appears in the admin documents list (the Delete-data grid), so it cannot be managed or — by implication — used for grounding.

Root cause (diagnosed 2026-06-16): the upload endpoint (`POST /api/admin/documents` → `backend.services.ingestion.upload_document`) is a two-step "store blob + enqueue" operation — it writes the blob and enqueues a `BatchPushQueueMessage`, then returns `200`; indexing happens asynchronously in the Functions `batch_push` queue trigger (download → parse → embed → push to Azure AI Search). The break is in the **parse** step for PDFs: `DocumentIntelligenceParser` builds its client endpoint from `settings.foundry.services_endpoint` (`AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT`, prefix `AZURE_AI_`). When that setting is empty, `_get_client` computes `endpoint = f"{''.rstrip('/')}/"` → `"/"`, a URL with no `https` scheme; the Azure SDK's `BearerTokenCredentialPolicy` then refuses to attach the managed-identity token and raises `azure.core.exceptions.ServiceRequestError: Bearer token authentication is not permitted for non-TLS protected (non-https) URLs` before any request leaves the process. `batch_push` therefore throws on every PDF, the message is retried and dead-lettered, and the doc never reaches the index — but the upload + enqueue already returned `200`, so the UI reports success. `list_sources` reads distinct `title` values from the index, so an unindexed doc never lists.

Diagnostic trace (2026-06-16): (1) wiring confirmed identical between backend-enqueue and Functions-trigger (queue name, storage account, container all match; identity-based auth, not Azurite). (2) Queue state: main queue empty, **poison queue held 22 messages** (14 `.pdf` + 8 extension-less, all dated 2026-06-10) with valid envelopes (`filename` / `container_name` / `ingestion_job_id` present) — so the failure is downstream of message validation, in parse/embed/push. (3) Running the exact `functions.batch_push.blueprint._execute` seam in-process against `Benefit_Options.pdf` reproduced the failure: `ServiceRequestError` in `DocumentIntelligenceParser.parse` → `begin_analyze_document`, because `services_endpoint` resolved to `""` (the `v2/.env` the script loads is missing `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT`). (4) Re-running the same seam with the Functions host's `local.settings.json` values loaded (which **do** carry an `https` `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT`) **succeeded — 4 chunks pushed** — and `Benefit_Options.pdf` then appeared in `GET /api/admin/documents`. So the code + host config are now correct; the 22 poison messages are stale failures from before the endpoint was added to the host config on/after 2026-06-10.

Classification: primarily a **configuration gap** (empty `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT`) compounded by a **code-hardening gap** — an empty/non-HTTPS endpoint fails with a cryptic SDK auth error and silently poisons every PDF while the UI shows success, with no fail-fast validation and no surfacing of the ingestion failure to the operator.

Fix plan (separate units, test-first): (a) **fail-fast guard** — validate `services_endpoint` is non-empty and `https`-schemed at `DocumentIntelligenceParser` construction (or in `FoundrySettings`), raising a clear, actionable error instead of the opaque SDK "non-TLS" message; this is the real code fix and prevents silent PDF-poisoning. (b) **`v2/.env` backfill** — add `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` (the backend's synchronous `ingest_url` path and the ingestion scripts read `.env` and still break without it; only the Functions host's `local.settings.json` was repaired). (c) **operational cleanup** — redrive the 22 poison messages (or `POST /api/admin/documents/reprocess`) now that config is correct. (d) **upload-boundary fail-fast** — surface the misconfig as an honest error at the HTTP boundary: `POST /api/admin/documents` returns `503` (not a green `200`) when a Document-Intelligence-routed file (PDF / DOCX) is uploaded while `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` is unset or non-HTTPS, so the operator is told the deployment cannot index the file instead of seeing a false success.

Fix progress: **all units (a)–(d) landed 2026-06-16.** (a) `DocumentIntelligenceParser._get_client` now raises an actionable `ValueError` naming `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` when `services_endpoint` is empty or not `https`-schemed, before constructing the SDK client (after the injected-client seam, so client-injecting tests are unaffected); five new tests in `v2/tests/functions/core/parsers/test_document_intelligence_parser.py` (empty, three non-HTTPS forms, injected-seam bypass), `pyright --strict` `0/0/0`. (b) the tracked template `v2/.env.sample` was missing `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` entirely (the source of the gap — every `v2/.env` copied from it inherited the omission); added the documented key to the sample and backfilled the real value into the gitignored `v2/.env` from the azd env store, so backend `AppSettings.foundry.services_endpoint` now resolves to an `https` URL. (d) the upload endpoint (`upload_document_endpoint` in [admin.py](../../src/backend/routers/admin.py)) now fails fast with `503` when a Document-Intelligence-routed file is uploaded while `services_endpoint` is empty/non-HTTPS — a registry-identity probe (`registry.get(ext) is registry.get("pdf")`) scopes the guard to DI-routed extensions so non-DI uploads (txt / md / html) are never over-blocked; two new tests in `v2/tests/backend/test_admin.py` (DI file + blank endpoint → `503`; txt + blank endpoint → `200`), full admin suite 111 passed, `pyright` `0/0/0`. This converts the BUG-0034 false-`200` into an honest error at the boundary the operator sees. A **second, local-dev contributing factor** surfaced during the (c) drain: the Functions host's gitignored `local.settings.json` had drifted to queue `doc-processing-local` while the azd store + backend `v2/.env` use the canonical `doc-processing`, so the local host listened on a different queue than the backend enqueues to and never consumed the messages — not a shipped defect (azd wires both tiers from one env), fixed by aligning the local value, restarting the host on the canonical queue, and draining it: all 6 backend-enqueued messages processed successfully (DI parse → embed → push, 22–27 s each) and the documents list grew from 2 to 5 distinct sources (`PerksPlus.pdf`, `role_library.pdf`, and the Woodgrove cyber-risk policy newly indexed), with the canonical queue returning to empty. A non-destructive peek confirmed every PDF the poison referenced was already indexed and that 8 of the 22 canonical-poison messages were base64 Event Grid blob-event envelopes that `batch_push` cannot process; redriving would therefore re-index present docs and re-poison the envelopes, so (operator-confirmed) both poison queues were cleared instead (22→0 and 10→0). All four ingestion queues are now empty and the pipeline indexes uploads end-to-end. **Fixed 2026-06-16.** See [bug-0034-diagnosis.md](bug-0034-diagnosis.md) for the full narrative.

Adjacent observations (not part of this defect): the in-process `_execute` run logged `aiohttp` "Unclosed client session / Unclosed connector" warnings — the DI client / embedder is not closed on the `batch_push` path (low-severity resource leak, candidate for a separate bug). Separately, the locally-running Functions host (restarted after an overnight DNS/credential crash) was not draining the main queue during the trace (a queued message sat undrained) — a local-dev-session listener artifact cleared by a clean host restart, not a code defect.

References: BUG-0003 (the same `list_sources` documents list — healthy after its facet→paging fix; this defect is upstream of it, in ingestion); [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md), [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md).

### BUG-0035 — `agent_framework` sends unsupported `temperature` to the reasoning model (400)

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-14, fixed 2026-06-14).

Symptom: on the BUG-0013 reasoning path (the answer deployment auto-detected as reasoning-capable), forcing the `agent_framework` orchestrator live fails the agent run with `400 - Unsupported parameter: 'temperature' is not supported with this model.`, so the conversation stream emits an `error` frame instead of reasoning + answer.

Root cause: `AgentFrameworkOrchestrator.run()` built `ChatOptions(temperature=…, max_tokens=…)` for every run and passed it to `agent.run(...)`. When the run also requests a Responses-API `reasoning` option, the gpt-5 / o-series answer deployment (`gpt-5.1`) switches to reasoning-model semantics and rejects the `temperature` sampling parameter. The `langgraph` reasoning path never hit this because its `reason()` sends neither `temperature` nor `max_tokens`. The whole `agent_framework` reasoning path was never exercised live before because the deployment runs `langgraph` via a persisted cosmos orchestrator override (`resolve_effective_config` overlays it on the `agent_framework` env default), so only the new both-orchestrator integration test — which sets `app.state.runtime_overrides = RuntimeConfig(orchestrator_name="agent_framework")` after lifespan boot — drove the path and surfaced the 400.

Fix: branch `run()` on the auto-detected reasoning capability (`llm.supports_reasoning()`) — in reasoning mode build a bare `ChatOptions()` and set only the `reasoning` option (omit `temperature`/`max_tokens`), symmetric with the `langgraph` `reason()` path; in non-reasoning mode keep `ChatOptions(temperature, max_tokens)` unchanged. The non-reasoning `agent_framework` path is unaffected — it sends `temperature=0.0` and was live-verified grounding an answer under BUG-0025, so this is strictly a reasoning-mode combination defect, not a broader temperature problem.

Verification: the parametrized `tests/integration/test_conversation_live.py::test_reasoning_feed_streams_substantive_model_reasoning[agent_framework]` now passes live (substantive reasoning streams, no 400); the `langgraph` parameter also passes. Unit coverage: `test_run_requests_reasoning_summary_when_model_supports_it` asserts the `reasoning` option is present and `temperature`/`max_tokens` are absent; `test_run_omits_reasoning_option_when_model_lacks_reasoning` and the default-sampling tests assert the non-reasoning path is unchanged.

References: [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md); related BUG-0013 (the reasoning feed this unblocks), BUG-0025 (prior `agent_framework` non-reasoning live verification), BUG-0029 (the sibling `max_tokens`→`max_completion_tokens` chat-path parameter defect).

### BUG-0036 — canned KB-search narration persists alongside real model reasoning

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-14, fixed 2026-06-14).

Symptom: once BUG-0013 made the answer model stream substantive reasoning, the thinking panel showed the canned "Searching the knowledge base for relevant sources…" sentence *and* the real reasoning together — the placeholder line was never replaced when genuine reasoning began.

Root cause: the during-the-wait narration (added in BUG-0027, emitted upfront by the shared `run_chat` pipeline on the `reasoning` channel) and the orchestrator's own native reasoning frames are both `reasoning`-channel `OrchestratorEvent`s. The FE `append_reasoning` reducer pushed every `reasoning` frame into a single `reasoning[]` list, and `MessageList` joined the whole list, so the placeholder and the model reasoning concatenated. SSE is append-only, so the already-displayed narration could not be removed without FE state support.

Fix: mark the transient narration so the client can drop it. (1) Backend — `run_chat` emits the `retrieval_hint` frame with `metadata={"placeholder": True}`; `format_sse` already forwards `metadata` for every channel, so it reaches the FE as `ev.metadata.placeholder === true`. (2) FE model — `ChatMessage` gains a `reasoningPlaceholder?: string` slot, held apart from `reasoning[]`. (3) FE reducer — a new `set_reasoning_placeholder` action sets (never appends) the placeholder. (4) FE handler — `MessageInput` routes a `reasoning` frame with `metadata.placeholder === true` to `set_reasoning_placeholder`, all other `reasoning` frames to `append_reasoning`. (5) FE renderer — `MessageList` shows the panel when streaming, or when `reasoning` is non-empty, or when a non-empty placeholder exists, and renders `reasoning.join("")` when non-empty else `reasoningPlaceholder` — so the first real reasoning frame supersedes the placeholder, and a non-reasoning model keeps the placeholder as the sole content (no regression).

Verification: `tests/backend/core/pipelines/test_chat.py` asserts the narration frame carries `metadata == {"placeholder": True}` and the orchestrator's native reasoning frame does not (18/18). FE Vitest: `ChatContext.test.tsx` (placeholder set without touching `reasoning`, replace-not-append), `MessageInput.test.tsx` (placeholder frame → `reasoningPlaceholder`, subsequent real frame → `reasoning[]`), `MessageList.test.tsx` (placeholder shown when no reasoning yet; real reasoning drops the placeholder) — 87/87 across the three suites. `tsc --noEmit` clean on the frontend source + test workspaces; `pyright` 0/0/0 on `chat.py`.

References: [worklog/2026-06-14.md](worklog/2026-06-14.md); related BUG-0013 (the reasoning content this polishes), BUG-0027 (the upfront narration whose lifecycle this completes).

### BUG-0037 — finished answer missing the "AI-generated content may be incorrect" disclaimer

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-15, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: a finished assistant answer renders the answer body and then the reference block with nothing between them; v1 shows a small muted "AI-generated content may be incorrect" disclaimer in the answer footer.

Root cause: `MessageList` never rendered a disclaimer element; the assistant content column stacked only the answer `MarkdownContent` and the `CitationPanel`.

Fix: `MessageList` now renders a static `<p>` (`AI-generated content may be incorrect`, `data-testid="answer-disclaimer-<id>"`) between the answer body and the `CitationPanel`, gated on `m.streaming !== true && m.content.length > 0` so it appears only under a finished, non-empty answer — not while streaming, not on user messages, not on empty error-only messages. The `.disclaimer` style is small and muted (`fontSizeBase200` / `colorNeutralForeground3`) to mirror the v1 answer footer.

Verification: `MessageList.test.tsx` — disclaimer present under a finished assistant answer; absent on a user message; absent while streaming; absent on an empty error-only message (33/33).

References: [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md).

### BUG-0038 — extra blank line between reasoning sections in the thinking panel

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-15, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: the thinking/reasoning panel renders consecutive reasoning sections separated by a blank line (an extra paragraph break), making the panel taller and looser than intended.

Root cause: `formatReasoning` (reasoningText.tsx) replaces each model bold section title (`SECTION_TITLE`) with a `"\n\n"` paragraph break and then collapses `\n{3,}` to `\n\n`. Rendered through the markdown panel, each `\n\n` becomes a separate `<p>`, so sequential reasoning bodies show a blank line between them.

Fix: changed the section-title replacement to a single `"\n"` line break and the run-collapse to `\n{2,}` → `"\n"`, so adjacent reasoning bodies render on consecutive lines within one `<p>` (a soft break shown via the panel's `white-space: pre-wrap`) with no empty paragraph between them. Updated `reasoningText.test.tsx` (multi-section expectations now `\n`) and the `MessageList.test.tsx` reasoning assertion (one `<p>` with a softbreak instead of two paragraphs).

References: [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md).

### BUG-0039 — references do not open a source-detail column on click

Area: frontend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-15, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: in v1, references render as bordered, clickable chips (a number box + the document filename); clicking a chip opens a right-side column showing the document title, a link to open the document, and the reference text (with markdown handled). In v2, the `CitationPanel` renders a "N references" toggle over a numbered list whose items expand inline to a snippet + an "Open source" link — there is no right-side detail column, and the chat layout has no place for one.

Root cause: the v2 `CitationPanel` was scoped (BUG-0015) to the reference-block restyle only; the right-side citation detail column was explicitly deferred as a separate structural change. There is no `activeCitation` state, no `CitationDetailPanel` component, and `ChatPage` is a two-column grid.

Fix (multi-unit): added `activeCitation` + `ShowCitation` / `CloseCitation` to chat state (models/chat.tsx, ChatContext.tsx); added a pure `formatCitationLabel` middle-truncation helper; restyled the references as clickable v1-style chips (number box + truncated filename) that dispatch `ShowCitation` (CitationPanel.tsx + .module.css; MessageList.tsx wires `onSelectCitation`); added a `CitationDetailPanel` that renders the active citation's title, an open-document link, and the markdown-rendered reference text (XSS-safe `MarkdownContent`, no rehype-raw), with a dismiss control dispatching `CloseCitation`; and added a third push-content grid column to `ChatPage` driven by an inner `ChatShell` component that reads `activeCitation` and toggles `data-citation-open` (chat `.main` is `1fr`, so it narrows when the column opens). Structural sign-off for the third column obtained from the operator (push-content column, v1 parity).

References: [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md).

### BUG-0040 — reference toggle does not collapse the chip list

Area: frontend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-15, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: the "N references" toggle under an answer never hides the reference chips. The list stays visible whether the toggle reads as expanded or collapsed, so the collapse affordance appears broken and the references always show.

Root cause: `CitationPanel.tsx` correctly sets the `hidden` attribute on the chip-list container (`hidden={!expanded}`), but `CitationPanel.module.css` styles that container with `.chipList { display: flex }`. An explicit `display` declaration overrides the user-agent `[hidden] { display: none }` rule (lowest possible priority), so the element stays laid out even when `hidden` is present. The existing `CitationPanel.test.tsx` asserts only the `hidden` attribute (set correctly), and jsdom does not apply CSS-module styles, so the visual regression was invisible to the test.

Planned fix: add a `.chipList[hidden] { display: none }` rule so the `hidden` attribute actually hides the container. Verified live (CSS-only change; jsdom cannot assert computed layout).

Fix: added a `.chipList[hidden] { display: none }` rule so the `hidden` attribute actually hides the container. Verified live (CSS-only change; jsdom cannot assert computed layout).

References: [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md).

### BUG-0041 — reference chips render side by side instead of stacked

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-15, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: the expanded references render as chips laid out side by side on the same line, wrapping to the next line only when they run out of horizontal room. v1 lists each reference on its own line (a vertical stack).

Root cause: `CitationPanel.module.css` styles the chip container as a wrapping row (`.chipList { display: flex; flex-wrap: wrap }`); v1's reference list is a column.

Fix: changed `.chipList` to a column layout (`flex-direction: column`, `align-items: flex-start`) and let each chip size to its content, so references stack one per line. Verified live.

References: [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md).

### BUG-0042 — expanded reference has no link to open the document

Area: frontend (with a backend dependency). Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-15, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: opening a reference in the citation detail column shows the title and the reference text but no "Open document" link, so there is no way to view the underlying file (for example a sample PDF).

Root cause: the v2 ingestion pipeline intentionally omits a `url` field from the search index — `SearchDocument` writes only `id`, `content`, `title`, and `content_vector`, and the blob filename survives only in `title` (`title = chunk.source`). The index `url` column is therefore never populated, so `SearchResult.url` and in turn `Citation.url` are always the empty string, and `CitationDetailPanel` gates the open-document link on a non-empty `url`. The backend also exposes no file-serving endpoint (routers: health, conversation, history, speech, admin), so even a recovered filename had nowhere to resolve. v1 served documents through a Flask `/api/files/<filename>` proxy that streamed the blob from the documents container with path-traversal and content-type guards.

Fix (multi-unit): recover the filename from `Citation.title`; add a backend `GET /api/files/{filename}` route that streams the blob from the documents container via the existing storage helpers, sets the content type from the filename and `Content-Disposition: inline` (so the browser renders the PDF or native format in a new tab), and rejects path traversal / double-encoding; register the router on the app; and render an absolute `${VITE_BACKEND_URL}/api/files/<filename>` open-document link in `CitationDetailPanel` (the cloud frontend is a static-only app on a separate origin, so the new-tab navigation needs the absolute backend URL). Verified with backend pytest + a live probe (`200`, `Content-Type: application/pdf`, `Content-Disposition: inline`, 544 KB body) plus browser confirmation of the toggle-collapse, vertical-stack, and open-document-in-new-tab behaviors.

References: [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md).

### BUG-0043 — raw KB citation markers leak into the reasoning panel

Area: backend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-15, fixed 2026-06-19).

Symptom: the reasoning/thinking panel renders raw native citation markers of the form `【message_idx:search_idx†source_name】` (for example `【6:1†source】`) inline in the reasoning text. These full-width-bracket markers are an internal citation encoding, not human-readable content, so they appear as garbage in the panel and need to be removed.

Root cause: the `agent_framework` orchestrator grounds through the server-side Foundry IQ Knowledge Base, whose model emits native `【N:M†source】` markers. Those markers are normalized away from the **answer** string by `normalize_kb_citations` (which rewrites attributed markers to the shared `[docN]` shape and strips any residual marker via `_KB_MARKER_RE`), but that normalization runs only over the answer. In `_update_to_events`, `text_reasoning` content blocks are forwarded **verbatim** to the `reasoning` channel with no marker stripping. When a reasoning-capable model (gpt-5 / o-series) produces a reasoning summary that references KB sources, it emits the same `【N:M†source】` markers inline in that summary, and they reach the frontend reasoning panel unmodified. The panel has no `[docN]` citation rendering, so the markers show as raw text. The `langgraph` path is unaffected (it emits `[docN]` markers, not native ones, and its reasoning summaries carry no KB markers).

Fix (landed 2026-06-19): added a `strip_kb_markers(text) -> str` helper to [tools/citations.py](../../src/backend/core/tools/citations.py) that removes every `_KB_MARKER_RE` match and collapses the doubled horizontal whitespace the removal leaves behind (`[ \t]{2,}` → single space), preserving newlines so a multi-line reasoning summary keeps its structure. `_update_to_events` ([agent_framework.py](../../src/backend/core/providers/orchestrators/agent_framework.py)) now wraps the `text_reasoning` text in `strip_kb_markers` before emitting the `reasoning` event, so the answer-side `normalize_kb_citations` keeps sole ownership of rewriting markers to `[docN]` while the reasoning channel only drops them. The `langgraph` path is untouched (it emits `[docN]`, not native markers). The helper is exported via `__all__`.

Verification: four `strip_kb_markers` unit tests in `tests/backend/core/tools/test_citations.py` (removes-and-collapses, multiple markers, preserves newlines, no-op without markers) + one orchestrator test `test_run_strips_native_kb_markers_from_reasoning_events` asserting a reasoning frame containing `【6:1†source】` is emitted clean and no native marker leaks onto any channel. Citations + agent_framework suites 82 passed; full backend suite 1075 passed / 0 failed; changed files 0 type/lint errors. (The unrelated pre-existing `ROUTERS-NON-ROUTE-CONTENT-DEBT` shared-gate red on `_DI_PARSER_PROBE_KEY` in `admin.py` is from the BUG-0034 fix, not this change.)

References: [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md).

### BUG-0044 — stale conversation-route test asserts narration metadata `{}` (source emits `{"placeholder": True}`)

Area: backend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-15 while wiring conversation persistence for BUG-0017).

Symptom: `tests/backend/test_conversation.py::test_sse_emits_leading_retrieval_narration_when_search_wired` fails at `HEAD`: `{'content': '…', 'metadata': {'placeholder': True}} != {'content': '…', 'metadata': {}}`. The failure was latent because the conversation-route suite was not re-run between the source change and the BUG-0017 wiring.

Root cause: BUG-0036 added `metadata={"placeholder": True}` to the leading retrieval-narration `reasoning` event that `run_chat` emits (so the frontend can replace the transient placeholder bubble once real reasoning streams). The narration test's expected frame was never updated to match — it still asserts `metadata: {}`. The source is correct (the placeholder marker is required by BUG-0036's FE replace-not-append behavior); the test expectation is stale.

Fix: updated the expected metadata in `test_sse_emits_leading_retrieval_narration_when_search_wired` to `{"placeholder": True}` so the test matches the shipped `run_chat` behavior; added a one-line comment noting the placeholder is the BUG-0036 frontend-replacement marker. No source change. Full conversation-route + services suites and the four shared AST gates pass (509 passed, 1 skipped).

References: [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md); related BUG-0036 (the source change that introduced the placeholder metadata), BUG-0017 (the persistence wiring whose suite run unmasked the stale assertion).

### BUG-0045 — chat page still has a double scroll after the L1 height-chain fix

Area: frontend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-15, fixed 2026-06-19 by the operator).

Symptom: on the v2 chat page the whole page scrolls in addition to the inner message-list scroll (a "double scroll"). When the page scrolls, the app header slides off the top of the viewport and the message composer lifts off the bottom, exposing empty whitespace below it. The operator reports this is still present after the L1 fix and a hard reload.

Root cause (under investigation): the L1 fix targeted the shell height chain — it gave the Fluent provider wrapper a height (`.appFluentRoot { height: 100% }` on the `FluentThemeBridge` provider), changed CoralShell `.column` from `height: 100vh` to `height: 100%`, and added `min-height: 0` to ChatPage `.main` — on the hypothesis that `100vh` (which includes the strip under a horizontal scrollbar) combined with X-overflow from wide markdown tables was producing vertical page overflow. After the fix, agent Playwright measurements reported `document.scrollingElement.scrollHeight - clientHeight === 0` (no page overflow) across an empty chat, 2000px of injected content, a real four-message conversation, and a viewport sweep (1360×600 → 1280×1024) — only the inner `.scroll` region scrolled. Despite those measurements the operator still observes the double scroll in their own browser, so the reproducing condition is not captured by the automation environment. Candidates not yet ruled out: a specific browser/OS scrollbar mode or zoom level, a particular conversation/content state, or a layout path the headless viewport does not exercise. The original height-chain hypothesis is therefore incomplete.

Status: fixed 2026-06-19. The operator took ownership of the fix (per the original triage) and confirms the double scroll is gone — only the inner `.scroll` message-list region scrolls now; the app header stays pinned to the top and the composer to the bottom, with no page-level overflow. The L1 height-chain edits remain in place (they are independently correct and pass their `FluentThemeBridge` vitest) and are documented in the worklog's L1 and live-verification sections. Closed on operator confirmation.

References: [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md).

### BUG-0046 — frontend never resolves the user or forwards an identity header

Area: frontend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-15, fixed 2026-06-15).

Symptom: chat history is not isolated per user. The v2 SPA never resolves the signed-in user, keeps no user-id state, and forwards no `x-ms-client-principal-id` header on any of its four `fetch` clients (`streamChat`, `conversationHistory`, `admin`, `speech`). There is no detection of whether login is enforced, no error screen when login is enforced but no user is present, and no default-user fallback when login is not enforced.

Root cause: the backend is already user-scoped — the history and conversation routes consume `UserIdDep` (which reads `x-ms-client-principal-id`), and the Cosmos DB / PostgreSQL providers key every read and write on `user_id`, so a non-owned conversation already resolves to `404` on get / delete / rename. But the frontend was never wired to supply that identity. With the separate-origin topology (the SPA reaches the backend at an absolute `VITE_BACKEND_URL`), the Easy Auth header that the platform injects on the frontend origin does not travel to the cross-origin backend call, so without manual forwarding the backend sees no principal: in `production` mode `get_user_id` returns `401` on every history / conversation call, and in `local` mode every caller collapses into the single `local-dev` partition. Net: per-user isolation is non-functional even though the server-side enforcement is correct. Latent in local single-user development; surfaces in a cloud multi-user deployment.

Fix direction: port the v1 `getUserInfo()` flow and the reference architecture's header-forward pattern. On load, read an `auth_enforced` signal (folded into `GET /api/health`) and call `/.auth/me`; when login is enforced, resolve the real user from the `objectidentifier` claim and block with an error screen if it is absent; when login is not enforced, use the all-zeros default user `00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000`. Inject `x-ms-client-principal-id` on every API call via a single `userIdHeaders()` helper spread into each `fetch`. Add the backend `auth_enforced` signal and a light principal-id well-formedness check in `get_user_id`. The full unit checklist lives in [frontend-user-identity-plan.md](frontend-user-identity-plan.md).

Security: a browser-forwarded `x-ms-client-principal-id` is not a trust boundary — it is acceptable for chat-history partitioning only. Admin RBAC (`requires_role("admin")`) stays anchored on the backend's own server-injected Easy Auth claims (`x-ms-client-principal`); the browser must not forward the claims blob to satisfy a role check, and "valid" for a forwarded id means well-formed, not authentic. (The BUG-0046 id-forwarding change later regressed the admin local-dev bypass — see BUG-0047.)

Verification finding (2026-06-15): the original fix enumerated **four** `fetch` clients (`streamChat`, `conversationHistory`, `admin`, `speech`) and spread `userIdHeaders()` into each, but a live browser request-header capture showed `GET /api/history/conversations` still going out with **no** `x-ms-client-principal-id` while `GET /api/admin/status` carried the default id correctly. Root cause of the miss: `HistoryPanel.tsx` is a **fifth** request seam — it does not use any `api/*.tsx` client; it has its own inline `fetchJson` helper that built headers from scratch (`Content-Type` only), so the panel's list / rename / delete calls bypassed the shared identity seam. This is the primary history surface, so the core requirement ("the chat history call must be a query by the user id" / "delete must belong to the same user") was unmet from the browser even though the per-client unit tests passed. Fixed by spreading `userIdHeaders()` into `HistoryPanel`'s `fetchJson` (smallest change — no refactor to route the panel through a shared client). Re-verified live: `/api/history/conversations` now carries the default id. Regression guard added in `HistoryPanel.test.tsx` (the fetch harness now captures the forwarded principal and asserts it rides the list, rename, and delete calls). Caught only because the verification step captured **real** browser request headers rather than trusting the mocked per-client suites — the mocks asserted the clients that were wired, not the seam that was missed.

References: [worklog/2026-06-15.md](worklog/2026-06-15.md), [frontend-user-identity-plan.md](frontend-user-identity-plan.md).

### BUG-0047 — admin panel 401s in local dev (claims-absent bypass regression)

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-16, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: every `/api/admin/*` request (`GET /api/admin/status`, `/config`, `/documents`, …) returns `401 {"detail":"Missing client principal claims; Easy Auth claims header required."}` in local development, so the admin UI cannot load. Observed at `http://localhost:5273/api/admin/status` → `401`.

Root cause: a regression introduced by the BUG-0046 identity-forwarding fix. The SPA's single modular header seam, `userIdHeaders()` in `api/auth.tsx`, now spreads `x-ms-client-principal-id` (the resolved user, or the all-zeros default `00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000` when auth is not enforced) onto **every** API call — including all admin calls. The backend admin gate `requires_role("admin")._checker` (in `dependencies.py`) has a local-dev bypass that returned the synthetic `local-dev` admin **only when both** Easy Auth headers were absent (`if not principal_id and not claims_raw`). Because the id header is now always present, that condition is never true locally, so the gate falls through to the next branch (`if not claims_raw` → `401`). The bypass guard was written against the pre-BUG-0046 world where the SPA sent no headers at all.

Why the frontend is NOT the fix: the missing header is the `x-ms-client-principal` **claims** blob, which carries the role claims the gate evaluates. That blob must stay server-injected by Easy Auth and must never be forged or forwarded by the browser — a browser-supplied claims blob would let any caller assert the admin role. The frontend's modular seam already forwards everything it legitimately can (the partition id); supplying the claims blob from the SPA is the documented anti-pattern (see the BUG-0046 Security note). The correct, modular fix is the single backend conditional, which fixes all admin endpoints simultaneously.

Fix: the local-dev bypass now keys on the **absence of the claims blob** (the sole authority for the role check), not on both headers being absent. When `x-ms-client-principal` is absent: in `local` the gate returns `local-dev` (the admin panel is exercisable end-to-end without forging claims, regardless of whether the forgeable id header rode along); in any non-local environment it raises `401` and fails closed (the id header alone can never satisfy a role gate). Authenticated callers (claims present) are unchanged — decode, check the role, `403` on absence. Regression test `test_requires_role_falls_back_to_local_dev_when_id_present_no_claims_in_local` locks the id-present + claims-absent + `local` → `local-dev` path; the existing production no-claims `401` test continues to guard the fail-closed boundary.

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md).

### BUG-0048 — admin document delete 503s (`title` not filterable in the index)

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-16, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: `DELETE /api/admin/documents/{source}` returns `503 {"detail":"Azure dependency temporarily unavailable."}` for every delete. Observed deleting `Benefit_Options.pdf` from the admin documents list (`DELETE http://localhost:5273/api/admin/documents/Benefit_Options.pdf` → `503`).

Root cause: `AzureSearch.delete_by_source` resolved the chunk ids to delete by issuing a server-side OData filter — `client.search(search_text="*", filter="title eq '<source>'", select=["id"])` — but the deployed index schema (`scripts/post_provision.py` `_build_chat_index`) defines `title` as a `SearchableField`, which is **searchable but not filterable**. Azure Search therefore rejects the query with `azure.core.exceptions.HttpResponseError: Invalid expression: 'title' is not a filterable field. Only filterable fields can be used in filter expressions. Parameter name: $filter`. That `AzureError` propagates to the app-level handler in `backend.app`, which sanitises every `AzureError` to `503 "Azure dependency temporarily unavailable."` (Hard Rule #14, no SDK detail leaked). The sibling `list_sources` method in the same provider already documents and works around the identical fragility for the *facetable* attribute (it avoids faceting on `title` and pages client-side), so filtering was the one path that still assumed an index capability the schema does not grant.

Why it is not a name-vs-id problem: a wrong identifier returns `404` (the `deleted == 0` branch), not `503`. The delete already removes **by id** — it collects the chunk `id`s and calls `client.delete_documents(documents=[{"id": ...}])`. Only the *id-discovery* step failed. The admin documents list surfaces *sources* (filenames / URLs), not per-chunk ids, and one logical document is N chunks each with its own search-doc `id`, so the `DELETE /…/{source}` contract is correct; the frontend has no per-chunk id to send.

Fix: resolve source → ids client-side, mirroring `list_sources`. `delete_by_source` now pages every chunk (`client.search(search_text="*", select=["id", "title"])`, auto-paging, no `top` cap, no server-side `$filter`), keeps the `id`s whose `title` exactly equals the requested source, then deletes them in ≤1000-id batches as before. Because the user-supplied filename is no longer interpolated into an OData expression, the OData-injection seam that the previous `title eq '<source>'` filter opened is closed by construction (matching is plain Python equality). No index-schema change, no reindex, no frontend change; works against the already-deployed index. Tests updated to assert the client-side contract (no `filter` kwarg; `select == ["id", "title"]`; non-matching titles are not deleted; a mixed-source scan deletes only exact-title matches).

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md).

### BUG-0049 — DOCX (and Office / HTML) uploads index nothing (`pages[].lines` empty)

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-16, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: uploading a `.docx` file appears to succeed (upload + enqueue + `batch_push` all report success), but the document never appears in the search index and cannot be queried. No error surfaces to the operator — the file silently fails to index.

Root cause: `DocumentIntelligenceParser.parse` ([azure/functions/core/parsers/document_intelligence_parser.py](../src/functions/core/parsers/document_intelligence_parser.py)) builds chunks exclusively from `result.pages[*].lines[*].content`. Azure Document Intelligence's `prebuilt-layout` model handles paginated formats (PDF, images) by returning `pages[*].lines`, but it treats Microsoft Office (DOCX/PPTX/XLSX) and HTML inputs as **"pageless"**: it returns the extracted text in `result.paragraphs` (and the flat `result.content`) and leaves `pages[*].lines` empty. Confirmed against the live service: a sample DOCX returned `len(pages)=1`, per-page `len(lines)=[0]`, `len(paragraphs)=848`, `len(result.content)=29335`, while a sample PDF returned `len(pages)=4`, per-page `len(lines)=[4,6,34,25]`. So the page loop produces **zero** chunks for DOCX; the handler `batch_push_handler` then logs its zero-chunk info line and returns `[]` without ever embedding or indexing, and the upload boundary already returned `200` — hence the silent false success.

Why one chunk per `result.content` is the wrong fix: the `batch_push` handler embeds each `Chunk.content` directly — there is no downstream re-chunker (v2 removed the chunker primitive; parsers own chunking per format). A single 29 KB chunk would push the embedding deployment toward its token ceiling and produce one undifferentiated vector with poor retrieval granularity. The codebase already has the right precedent: `TextParser` chunks plain text **one chunk per paragraph**, and Document Intelligence already returns the DOCX text pre-split into 848 semantic `paragraphs`.

Fix: add a paragraph fallback. After the existing page pass, when it produced **zero** chunks, emit one chunk per `result.paragraphs` entry (stripping empties, keeping `index` dense for stable `make_chunk_id`s) — the same semantic unit `TextParser` uses. The fallback fires only when the page pass yielded nothing, so paginated formats (PDF, images) keep their one-chunk-per-page shape and never double-emit (a PDF returns both `pages[].lines` and `paragraphs`, but its page chunks suppress the fallback). No new chunker abstraction, no infra / model / frontend change; works against the already-deployed index. Verified live: the sample DOCX now produces 848 paragraph chunks and indexes end-to-end.

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md).

### BUG-0050 — Admin button missing in the deployed app (relative admin URLs hit the SPA catch-all)

Area: frontend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-16, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: in the deployed app the **Admin** button never appears in the chat header, and probing the admin-availability endpoint returns `200` with an HTML body instead of JSON. Chat works normally.

Root cause: the admin REST client ([admin.tsx](../src/frontend/src/api/admin.tsx)) is the **only** frontend fetch client that issues **relative** `/api/admin/*` URLs. Every sibling client prepends `VITE_BACKEND_URL`: `streamChat.tsx`, `conversationHistory.tsx`, `HistoryPanel.tsx`, the `App.tsx` health probe, and `documentHref.tsx`. The deployed topology is split-host — the frontend is an App Service container and the backend is a separate Container App on a different origin — and `VITE_BACKEND_URL` (baked into the bundle at build time) is what every client uses to cross to the backend. Because the admin client omitted that base, a relative `/api/admin/status` resolved against the **frontend** origin, and the frontend's SPA server ([frontend_app.py](../src/frontend/frontend_app.py)) has a catch-all `@app.get("/{full_path:path}")` that returns `index.html` for any path that is not an on-disk file. So the admin probe received `index.html` (HTTP `200`, `Content-Type: text/html`); `getAdminStatus()` then called `response.json()`, which threw on the HTML body; the `App.tsx` availability effect caught the throw and set `adminAvailable=false`; and the `Header` renders the Admin button only when `adminAvailable===true`. Confirmed live: `GET <frontend-host>/api/admin/status` returned `200` `<!doctype html>…`, while `GET <backend-host>/api/admin/status` returned `200` `{"orchestrator_name":…}` for the same path, with or without an identity header (this deployment has `auth_enforced:false`, so the admin gate does not block the status read). Local dev was unaffected because Vite proxies relative `/api` to the backend.

Why this is not an auth or backend bug: the backend admin status endpoint already returns `200` JSON in this deployment regardless of the `x-ms-client-principal` header, so once the request reaches the backend origin the button resolves. The only defect is client-side URL construction.

Fix: add the same `backendUrl()` (reads `VITE_BACKEND_URL` at call time, empty when unset) + `apiUrl(path)` (joins the base with the API path, trailing slash trimmed) seam the sibling clients already use, and prepend `apiUrl(...)` to all 8 admin fetch sites (`getAdminStatus`, `addDocumentUrl`, `uploadDocument`, `reprocessAll`, `listDocuments`, `deleteDocument`, `getAdminConfig`, `patchAdminConfig`; `resetAdminConfig` delegates to `patchAdminConfig`). When `VITE_BACKEND_URL` is unset the base is empty, so the relative-URL behavior (and the existing unit assertions) are unchanged; when set, admin calls target the backend origin like every other client. A new unit test asserts `getAdminStatus` prepends the base when the env var is set. No backend / infra / auth change. The deployed frontend image must be rebuilt (the base is baked at build time) and the App Service container repointed for QA to receive the fix.

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md).

### BUG-0051 — Admin document upload 503s (backend container missing storage env vars)

Area: infra. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-16, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: uploading a document from the (now-visible, post-BUG-0050) admin UI returns `503 {"detail":"Document storage is not configured for this deployment."}`. The same gate fronts URL ingestion, reprocess-all, and the file-download route.

Root cause: the backend admin endpoints ([admin.py](../src/backend/routers/admin.py)) gate document upload / URL ingest / reprocess on `settings.storage.documents_container` **and** `settings.storage.doc_processing_queue` being non-empty, and `GET /api/files/{filename}` ([files.py](../src/backend/services/files.py)) needs the documents container; `StorageSettings` ([settings.py](../src/backend/core/settings.py), `env_prefix="AZURE_"`) defaults every storage field to `""`. The `backendContainerApp` module in [main.bicep](../infra/main.bicep) never wired the storage env vars into its container `env` array — `AZURE_STORAGE_ACCOUNT_NAME` / `AZURE_DOCUMENTS_CONTAINER` / `AZURE_DOC_PROCESSING_QUEUE` were set **only** on the function app block (and emitted as stack outputs), so the deployed backend resolved all three to empty and the gate tripped on every upload. Confirmed live: the backend Container App's container `env` listed none of the three storage vars.

Why this is not an RBAC bug: the shared user-assigned managed identity already holds Storage Blob Data Owner, Storage Blob Data Contributor, Storage Queue Data Contributor, and Storage Queue Data Message Sender on the storage account (the function app performs ingestion blob + queue I/O under the same identity). Once the env vars are present, the backend writes and enqueues with no permission change.

Fix: add the same three storage env entries the function app uses (`AZURE_STORAGE_ACCOUNT_NAME` = `effectiveStorageName`, `AZURE_DOCUMENTS_CONTAINER` = `documentsContainerName`, `AZURE_DOC_PROCESSING_QUEUE` = `docProcessingQueueName`) to the `backendContainerApp` container `env` array. The blob and queue endpoints are derived from the account name by `resolve_storage_endpoints` ([storage_endpoints.py](../src/functions/core/storage_endpoints.py)) — it builds `https://<account>.blob.core.windows.net` and swaps `.blob.` → `.queue.` — so no explicit `AZURE_STORAGE_BLOB_ENDPOINT` var is required (matching the function app, which also omits it). `bicep build` passes with no new errors.

Deploy: a live hotfix `az containerapp update --set-env-vars AZURE_STORAGE_ACCOUNT_NAME=<account> AZURE_DOCUMENTS_CONTAINER=documents AZURE_DOC_PROCESSING_QUEUE=doc-processing` added the three vars to the deployed backend (additive, reversible) to unblock QA immediately; the new revision came up Healthy and an end-to-end `.txt` upload returned `200` `{"blob_path":"documents/…","ingestion_job_id":"…","queued":true}`, proving the config gate, blob write, and queue enqueue all succeed under the UAMI. The smoke-test blob was deleted afterward. The bicep edit makes the wiring durable across re-provision.

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md).

### BUG-0052 — Deployed parsing 503 (backend + function missing AI Services endpoint; UAMI lacks DI role)

Area: infra. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-16, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: with the admin UI working and storage wired (post-BUG-0051), uploading a PDF/DOCX to `POST /api/admin/documents` on the deployed backend returns `503 {"detail":"Document parsing is not configured for this deployment."}`.

Root cause: two deployment gaps. (1) The BUG-0034 unit-(d) upload guard ([admin.py](../src/backend/routers/admin.py)) refuses a Document-Intelligence-routed file when `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` is empty or non-HTTPS — and the deployed **backend** Container App and the **function** app were both missing that env var (the same class of bicep gap as BUG-0051: the var was emitted only as a stack output, never wired into either runtime's `env` array). (2) Even past the guard, the shared UAMI lacked **Cognitive Services User** on the AI Services account, so `DocumentIntelligenceParser` ([document_intelligence_parser.py](../src/functions/core/parsers/document_intelligence_parser.py)) could not authenticate to Document Intelligence (`begin_analyze_document`) under managed identity.

Fix (live): added `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT=https://aisa-<SUFFIX>.cognitiveservices.azure.com/` to both the backend Container App (`az containerapp update --set-env-vars`) and the function app (`az functionapp config appsettings set`), and granted the UAMI **Cognitive Services User** scoped to the AI Services account (`az role assignment create`). After the backend revision cycled, a PerksPlus.pdf upload returned `200 {…,"queued":true,"ingestion_job_id":"…"}` — the guard passes and the file enqueues. End-to-end parse verification is blocked downstream by BUG-0053 (the queued message is never consumed, so the DI parse under the new role has not yet executed in the deployed environment).

Durable follow-up: both the env var (backend + function `env`) and the RBAC role assignment should be added to `main.bicep` so the wiring survives re-provision — noted as follow-up, not applied this turn (further bicep edits paused by the operator).

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md).

### BUG-0053 — batch_push queue trigger never fires on Flex Consumption (scale-from-zero, identity-based queue connection)

Area: functions. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-16, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: documents uploaded through the admin UI enqueue successfully (`queued:true`) but never parse, embed, or index — they never appear in `GET /api/admin/documents`. The `doc-processing` queue holds the messages indefinitely at `dequeueCount=0` (never dequeued); PerksPlus.pdf sat unprocessed for over an hour.

Root cause (diagnosed): the function app (`func-<SUFFIX>`, Flex Consumption, Linux/Python 3.11) uses **per-function (target-based) scaling** — each non-HTTP trigger gets its own scale group. The `batch_push` queue trigger runs only in the `function:batch_push` group, which the platform **scale controller** must wake from zero based on queue depth. The HTTP-served instances (health/admin, woken by direct HTTP) do **not** run `batch_push`. The scale controller is not waking the `function:batch_push` group for the identity-based (`AzureWebJobsStorage__credential=managedidentity`) Storage Queue connection, so nothing ever polls `doc-processing`.

Everything else is provably correct: the trigger metadata is registered (`bindings:[{type:queueTrigger, queueName:%AZURE_DOC_PROCESSING_QUEUE%, connection:AzureWebJobsStorage}], isDisabled:null`); the queue name resolves to `doc-processing` (where the messages are); RBAC is sufficient (the UAMI holds **Storage Queue Data Contributor**, which ⊃ the doc-required Storage Queue Data Reader + Storage Queue Data Message Processor); the app has **only** the user-assigned identity and `AzureWebJobsStorage__clientId` matches it; storage networking is fully open (`publicNetworkAccess=Enabled`, `defaultAction=Allow`, no private endpoints, no VNet integration); and the Flex scale config is healthy (`maximumInstanceCount=40`, target-based defaults, identity-based deployment storage via the UAMI). Decisively, the function **works when an instance is warm** — right after a deploy a warm `batch_push` instance processed messages — so the binding, auth, and code are all correct; the failure is purely scale-from-zero.

No-cost levers tried, none of which woke the group (the queue stayed at 7 messages, `dq=0`, after all four): (a) added explicit `AzureWebJobsStorage__blobServiceUri` / `__queueServiceUri` / `__tableServiceUri` — the documented way for the scale controller to resolve identity-based endpoints, since the `__accountName` shorthand is host-runtime-only; (b) forced a full `az functionapp stop` + `start` cycle (plain `az functionapp restart` never cycled the running instances); (c) `syncfunctiontriggers` to force the platform to re-read triggers + scale config; (d) enabled a **system-assigned identity** on the app (alongside the UAMI) and granted it **Storage Queue Data Contributor** + **Storage Blob Data Owner** scoped to the storage account — on the theory the scale controller might poll under the system-assigned identity — then cycled + re-synced. The queue still did not drain ~15 min after the grant.

Definitive evidence (from `FunctionAppLogs` in the `log-<SUFFIX>` Log Analytics workspace, which — unlike App Insights, BUG-0055 — *is* populated via the app's `allLogs` diagnostic setting): every host start logs `batch_push` with a `Microsoft.Azure.WebJobs.Script.Description.FunctionGroupListenerDecorator+NoOpListener`. The `NoOpListener` **is** Flex Consumption's per-function-scaling mechanism — on instances **not** allocated to the `function:batch_push` scale group (the HTTP/health instances woken by direct HTTP), the real queue listener is deliberately replaced by a no-op that never polls. Across the entire 24h window **no** instance ever started the real `batch_push` listener, which proves the scale controller never allocated a `function:batch_push` instance and the queue poll never happens from zero. This matches the Flex Consumption troubleshooting doc's "trigger registration succeeded but the listener didn't enable" failure class exactly.

Telemetry path: App Insights is empty (BUG-0055), but the host *does* emit platform logs to the `log-<SUFFIX>` Log Analytics workspace (≈500 `Information` rows / 24h) via its `allLogs` diagnostic setting — that path supplied the `NoOpListener` evidence above. The scale controller's own decision trace (why it computes desired=0 for the identity-based queue) is **not** in `FunctionAppLogs`; it would require the App Insights scale-controller traces, which are missing.

Resolution: no-cost levers were exhausted (the speculative system-assigned-identity route (d) was tried and failed; runtime scale monitoring is Premium + VNet only, N/A to this non-VNet Flex app). The only no-regression fix is `alwaysReady = {function:batch_push: 1}` — one always-warm instance runs the real listener instead of the `NoOpListener` and polls the queue. The operator approved the small always-on cost, applied live (cloud variable, not bicep): `az functionapp scale config always-ready set -g <RESOURCE_GROUP> -n func-<SUFFIX> --settings function:batch_push=1`. The always-ready instance immediately ran the real listener and drained `doc-processing` (verified 7→0, then 3→0 on a fresh upload). The identity-based / no-secret design is preserved (switching `AzureWebJobsStorage` to a connection string was rejected). Durable back-port: add `alwaysReady` to the function app's bicep `functionAppConfig.scaleAndConcurrency` (follow-up; bicep edits paused). Note: with the listener fixed, ingestion still failed at message validation — a **separate** base64-encoding defect tracked as **BUG-0056**.

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md).

### BUG-0054 — Event Grid blob-created events poison the doc-processing queue (schema mismatch)

Area: infra. Severity: medium. Status: open — fix implemented + proven locally; cloud deploy of the `blob_event` translator **deferred** (found 2026-06-16, fix designed + locally validated 2026-06-20).

Symptom: the `doc-processing-poison` queue holds 10 base64 `Microsoft.Storage.BlobCreated` Event Grid envelopes (inserted 13:46–13:48).

Root cause: a stray/legacy Event Grid subscription on the storage account delivers blob-created events into `doc-processing`, but `batch_push` expects CWYD ingestion envelopes (`{container, blob_filename, ingestion_job_id, …}`), not the Event Grid `Microsoft.Storage.BlobCreated` schema. The events fail validation, retry, and land in poison. This is noise/poison accumulation — the events are **distinct** messages from the CWYD envelopes, so it does **not** block ingestion — but it pollutes the poison queue and indicates a stray Event Grid → queue wiring that should be removed or pointed at a handler that understands the blob-event schema. The same 8-envelope artifact was noted under BUG-0034's poison cleanup.

Fix design ([ADR 0028](adr/0028-event-grid-single-trigger-blob-ingestion.md)): a `blob_event` queue-trigger blueprint (`src/functions/blob_event/`) translates the raw Event Grid `BlobCreated` envelope into the CWYD `doc-processing` message, so the schema mismatch can never poison `doc-processing`. The Event Grid subscription is repointed off `doc-processing` onto a dedicated `blob-events` queue (with `blob-events-poison`) that only `blob_event` drains. A new `StorageSettings.ingestion_trigger` setting (`direct_enqueue` | `event_grid`; env `AZURE_INGESTION_TRIGGER`; bicep param `ingestionTrigger`; default `direct_enqueue`) lets the backend stop double-enqueuing once Event Grid owns ingestion — under `event_grid` the admin upload stores the blob and lets Event Grid drive the pipeline; under `direct_enqueue` (default) the backend enqueues to `doc-processing` as before.

Locally validated end-to-end (2026-06-20): with the local Functions host running `blob_event` against cloud storage, a blob dropped into the `documents` container flowed Event Grid → `blob-events` → `blob_event` → `doc-processing` → `batch_push` → pgvector, and the document appeared in `GET /api/admin/documents`. Test artifacts (blob, index entry, poison) cleaned up afterward.

Cloud deploy **deferred** (operator decision, 2026-06-20): `azd deploy function` uploaded the package but exceeded azd's 20-minute wait (Flex Consumption remote-build slowness — same env friction class as BUG-0058 / BUG-0062). The cloud Function App still serves the prior five functions (`add_url`, `batch_push`, `batch_start`, `health`, `search_skill`); `blob_event` is **not** registered, and a forced `syncfunctiontriggers` confirmed nothing new is deployed (the running package predates the change). Separately, `blob_event` is a queue trigger, so in Flex it carries the same **BUG-0053** scale-from-zero risk `batch_push` had — cloud `blob_event` reliability is coupled to that always-ready config. Both reasons make the cloud cutover larger than a code change, so it was parked.

Live state left coherent: the backend stays on `direct_enqueue` (`AZURE_ENV_INGESTION_TRIGGER` is unset → the default), so admin uploads keep working via the direct enqueue path. The env flag was deliberately **not** flipped to `event_grid` (that would remove the backend enqueue while no cloud `blob_event` drains `blob-events`, breaking cloud ingestion). The Event Grid subscription points at `blob-events` (matching the committed `infra/main.bicep`); those events only drain while the local Functions host is running. A prepackage gap surfaced during this work (the staged artifact omitted `blob_event`) and was fixed under BUG-0078 with a guard test.

To resume: deploy `blob_event` to the cloud Function App (retry `azd deploy function --timeout 2400`, or diagnose the Flex remote-build hang), add an `alwaysReady` instance for `function:blob_event` per BUG-0053, then `azd env set AZURE_ENV_INGESTION_TRIGGER event_grid` + `azd provision` to flip off the backend double-enqueue, and re-validate end-to-end in the cloud.

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md), [worklog/2026-06-20.md](worklog/2026-06-20.md); [ADR 0028](adr/0028-event-grid-single-trigger-blob-ingestion.md); related BUG-0053 (scale-from-zero), BUG-0058 (stale deploy artifact), BUG-0078 (prepackage allow-list), BUG-0077 (BlobDeleted follow-up).

### BUG-0055 — Application Insights receives zero telemetry from the function + backend

Area: infra. Severity: medium. Status: open (found 2026-06-16).

Symptom: `appi-<SUFFIX>` has never received any telemetry. A union query over `requests` / `traces` / `exceptions` / `dependencies` / `customMetrics` summarizing `count` / `min(timestamp)` / `max(timestamp)` returned `[0, null, null]` — total 0, no earliest, no latest.

Root cause (narrowed): the function's `APPLICATIONINSIGHTS_CONNECTION_STRING` was verified to **match** the `appi-<SUFFIX>` resource exactly (same ingestion endpoint + instrumentation key), so it is **not** a connection-string mismatch.
