Separately, the host **does** emit platform logs to the `log-<SUFFIX>` Log Analytics workspace via its `allLogs` diagnostic setting (≈500 `Information` rows / 24h in `FunctionAppLogs`), so telemetry generation works and the gap is specifically the **App Insights ingestion path** — the SDK/OTel application telemetry (`requests` / `traces` / `dependencies`) is not being exported, while the platform resource-log path is. Narrowed cause: the OTel → App Insights exporter is not initialized/exporting in either runtime (the `FunctionAppLogs` resource-log path is unaffected because it is wired by the diagnostic setting, not the SDK). Still independently a defect (no application-level observability); the `FunctionAppLogs` path is a working substitute for host-log diagnosis in the meantime (it supplied the BUG-0053 `NoOpListener` evidence).

Backend half — root cause confirmed + fixed (2026-06-23): the backend ACA container is a plain container with no host-level App Insights agent, so its Python lifespan (`backend/app.py`) only emits telemetry when it calls `configure_azure_monitor(connection_string=...)`, and that connection string comes from `ObservabilitySettings.app_insights_connection_string`. `ObservabilitySettings` sets `env_prefix="AZURE_"`, so the field reads **`AZURE_APP_INSIGHTS_CONNECTION_STRING`** (a deliberate decision — CU-002b/CU-007, enforced by two `test_app_lifespan.py` tests that intentionally ignore the standard name). But [main.bicep](../infra/main.bicep) wired the backend container with the **standard** `APPLICATIONINSIGHTS_CONNECTION_STRING` (the name the Function host needs), so the typed setting stayed empty and `configure_azure_monitor` never fired in the cloud — zero backend telemetry. Local dev worked only because `v2/.env` uses the `AZURE_`-prefixed name. Fix (operator chose the Bicep path over reversing the code decision): rename the **backend** container's env var to `AZURE_APP_INSIGHTS_CONNECTION_STRING` (the Function App keeps `APPLICATIONINSIGHTS_CONNECTION_STRING`, which its host reads natively); the `test_appinsights_connection_string_bound_to_workload` drift-guard is now parametrized per workload, and [ADR 0018](adr/0018-monitoring-default-on-and-appi-rbac.md) carries Amendment 1. Durable in Bicep — takes effect on the next `azd provision`; not yet cloud-verified (deploy blocked by the platform Flex build outage, see worklog 2026-06-23).

Function half — worker OTel wired (2026-06-23): added `configure_telemetry()` in `src/functions/core/telemetry.py`, called once at module load from `function_app.py` (kept out of the host entry module so it stays a thin blueprint-registration surface with no logic), which reads the host-provided `APPLICATIONINSIGHTS_CONNECTION_STRING` and calls `configure_azure_monitor(connection_string=...)` so the Python worker's application telemetry (logs / traces / dependencies) exports to App Insights; absent (local dev / monitoring off) it no-ops. Two `tests/functions/core/test_telemetry.py` tests cover the configured + no-op paths. Note: host-level `requests` (invocation) telemetry is emitted by the Functions **host**, not the worker — if those stay absent after a deploy, enabling host OpenTelemetry (`host.json` `telemetryMode`) is a separate follow-up. Both halves are now code/config-complete but **not yet cloud-verified** (deploy blocked by the Flex build outage); keep open until App Insights shows backend + function telemetry post-deploy.

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md), [worklog/2026-06-23.md](worklog/2026-06-23.md); [ADR 0018](adr/0018-monitoring-default-on-and-appi-rbac.md).

### BUG-0056 — CWYD ingestion envelopes poison in the cloud (queue messageEncoding base64 mismatch)

Area: functions. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-16, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: with BUG-0053's always-ready listener now draining `doc-processing`, a fresh PerksPlus.pdf admin upload still does **not** index — the document never appears in `GET /api/admin/documents`. The upload returns `200 {…,"queued":true,"ingestion_job_id":"…"}` and three messages appear on `doc-processing`, but the listener dequeues them and all three **poison** (poison depth +3). `FunctionAppLogs` shows `Executed Functions.batch_push (Failed, Duration=5–29ms)` with `batch_push queue message validation failed` — the failure is immediate (single-digit ms), before any blob download / parse / embed, i.e. at message validation, not in the pipeline.

Decoding the three newest poison bodies (each base64) shows the real shape: two are duplicate Event Grid `BlobCreated` envelopes (BUG-0054 noise) and **one is the genuine CWYD envelope** carrying the exact upload `ingestion_job_id` — `{"container_name":"documents","filename":"PerksPlus.pdf","ingestion_job_id":"…","force_reindex":false}`. That envelope **exactly matches** the current `BatchPushQueueMessage` contract (`container_name`, `filename`, `ingestion_job_id`, `force_reindex`; `frozen=True, extra="forbid"`), and the deployed package is from the same day with the only-ever contract — so this is **not** a schema/field-name skew.

Root cause: a **queue-message base64-encoding mismatch** between producer and consumer. The backend producer (`backend/services/ingestion.py` → `functions/batch_start/queue_writer.enqueue_push_message`) builds its `QueueClient` (`functions/core/storage_clients.py`) with **no `message_encode_policy`**, so the modern `azure-storage-queue` SDK uses `NoEncodePolicy` and sends the body as **raw JSON** (the `queue_writer.py` docstring's claim that the SDK base64-encodes by default is factually wrong). The Azure Functions queue trigger only accepts raw bodies when `extensions.queues.messageEncoding=none`; that setting exists **only** in `functions/local.settings.json` (so local dev works — confirmed by BUG-0034's successful local drain) and was **never** propagated to `host.json` or the cloud function app settings. The cloud Flex host therefore falls back to the Storage-Queue extension default `messageEncoding=base64`, cannot decode the raw-JSON body, and poisons every message after 5 retries. This reconciles all evidence: the host **base64-encodes on the way to the poison queue**, which is why every peeked poison body is base64 that decodes to a clean JSON envelope; Event Grid events poison for an independent reason (BUG-0054 schema mismatch) under either encoding.

Confirmed absent in the cloud: `az functionapp config appsettings list` returned no `messageEncoding` / `JobHost__extensions__queues` override (only `AzureWebJobsStorage__queueServiceUri`).

Fix (applied live, cloud variable — not bicep, not code): `az functionapp config appsettings set -g <RESOURCE_GROUP> -n func-<SUFFIX> --settings "AzureFunctionsJobHost__extensions__queues__messageEncoding=none"` (verified stored value `none`), then a forced restart so the `JobHost` setting loads at host startup. This matches the producer's raw-JSON output and the local configuration. Durable back-port: add the same host setting to `host.json` (`extensions.queues.messageEncoding`) or the bicep function app settings so every deploy carries it (follow-up; bicep edits paused).

Resolution (confirmed 2026-06-16): the host loaded the setting (startup `QueuesOptions { … MessageEncoding: None }`) and the poison body for the post-fix upload is **raw JSON** (no longer base64), proving the host now reads/writes raw. The post-fix CWYD envelope passes validation, acquires its managed-identity token, downloads the blob (HTTP 206, full 115 KB), and parses the PDF — so the encoding defect is resolved. The document still does not index because embedding then fails with a 404; that downstream failure is a separate defect tracked as **BUG-0057**.

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md).

### BUG-0057 — cloud ingestion embedding call returns 404 (embedding-deployment / endpoint mismatch)

Area: functions. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-16, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: after BUG-0056's `messageEncoding=none` fix, a fresh PerksPlus.pdf upload's CWYD envelope is now accepted by the queue trigger, but the document still does **not** index. `FunctionAppLogs` shows the envelope passes validation, acquires a managed-identity token, and downloads the blob (`Response status: 206 … Content-Length: 115310`, the full file), then fails with `batch_push queue handler failed` at ERROR level — retried 5 times ~7 s apart (01:16:58 → 01:17:26 UTC) before poisoning. The traceback bottoms out at `handler.py` `embedding_results = await embedder.embed(chunks)` → `embedders/azure_openai.py` `provider.embed(...)` → `llm/foundry_iq.py` `oai.embeddings.create(...)` → `openai.NotFoundError: Error code: 404`. So the failure is **after** blob download + PDF parse, at the embedding step (not validation, not storage).

Root cause: an embedding-deployment / endpoint mismatch across the two OpenAI-capable accounts in this environment. The search index `content_vector` field is **1536-dim**, which matches `text-embedding-3-small` (the value of `AZURE_OPENAI_EMBEDDING_DEPLOYMENT`) — `text-embedding-3-large` is 3072-dim — so the configured *model* is correct for the index. But the two accounts host different embedding deployments: `oai-<DATA_SUFFIX>` (`AZURE_OPENAI_ENDPOINT`) has **`text-embedding-3-small`** (the configured one); `aisa-<SUFFIX>` (`AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT`) has only **`text-embedding-3-large`**. The Foundry IQ provider routes embeddings to the **AI Services account** (`_get_embeddings_client` overrides `base_url` to `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` + `/openai/v1`, because the Foundry *project* route serves no `/embeddings`), so it asks `aisa-<SUFFIX>` for `text-embedding-3-small`, which is not there → 404. The **deployed** function build is also older than the local tree (deployed `foundry_iq.py` has `embeddings.create` at line 365 vs local 449 and lacks `_get_embeddings_client`), so it likely still routes embeddings to the Foundry project route, which 404s on `/embeddings` regardless of deployment name. No integrated vectorizer is configured on the index, so the function must compute embeddings itself — this path is unavoidable.

Why no pure cloud-variable fix exists: the embeddings `base_url` is derived from `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` (local code) or the fixed Foundry project route (deployed code), never from `AZURE_OPENAI_ENDPOINT` where `text-embedding-3-small` lives. Repointing `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` at the classic OpenAI account would also redirect other AI Services calls (e.g. Document Intelligence parsing), so it is not a safe lever.

Candidate fixes (operator decision required — all exceed the cloud-variable scope): (1) provision `text-embedding-3-small` (1536, GlobalStandard) on `aisa-<SUFFIX>` so the code's account-route finds it, **and** redeploy the current function code so embeddings use `_get_embeddings_client`'s account route rather than the project route — cleanest, aligns model + index + endpoint; (2) redeploy current code and route embeddings to `oai-<DATA_SUFFIX>` (where `text-embedding-3-small` already lives) via a code change that reads `AZURE_OPENAI_ENDPOINT` for embeddings (reusing `AZURE_AI_SERVICES_ENDPOINT` for that is unsafe); (3) standardize on `text-embedding-3-large` (already on `aisa-<SUFFIX>`) with `dimensions=1536` and re-embed everything — most disruptive (mixes vector spaces with the existing 1536-dim 3-small docs), not recommended.

Durable back-port: the bicep should deploy the embedding model on the **same** account the embedding code targets, and the function code should be redeployed so it carries the account-route embeddings client (bicep + redeploy paused per operator).

Resolution (confirmed 2026-06-16, fix path 1): (a) provisioned `text-embedding-3-small` (model version 1, 1536-dim, GlobalStandard, capacity 100) on `aisa-<SUFFIX>` — the AI Services account the embed path targets via `_get_embeddings_client` — and verified `POST https://aisa-<SUFFIX>.cognitiveservices.azure.com/openai/v1/embeddings` returns a 1536-dim vector for `text-embedding-3-small`. (b) Redeployed the current function code so `embed` uses `_get_embeddings_client` (account route `…cognitiveservices.azure.com/openai/v1`) instead of the legacy project route. The first `azd deploy function` shipped a stale `build-functions/` artifact (dated 06-06; the prepackage hook did not run — see BUG-0058), so logs still showed `POST https://aisa-<SUFFIX>.services.ai.azure.com/api/projects/proj-<SUFFIX>/openai/v1/embeddings → 404` and a traceback at the old `foundry_iq.py` line 365. After manually running `uv run python scripts/prepackage_function.py` (which regenerated `build-functions/` from current `src/`, putting `embed` → `_get_embeddings_client` at line 446) and redeploying, a fresh PerksPlus.pdf upload processed cleanly: validation → managed-identity token → blob download → PDF parse → embed → push. End-to-end verified — the backend `admin/documents` endpoint lists PerksPlus.pdf with **4 chunks**, and a direct query of the active `cwyd-index` (151 docs) returns 4 `title='PerksPlus.pdf'` chunks. (Note: `index-cwydcdbv23ane6` is a legacy v1 index with blob-URL `source` values; the active v2 index is `cwyd-index`, keyed on `title`/`url`/`content_vector`.)

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md).

### BUG-0058 — `azd deploy function` ships a stale build-functions artifact (prepackage hook skipped)

Area: functions. Severity: medium. Status: open (found 2026-06-16).

Symptom: while fixing BUG-0057, two consecutive `azd deploy function` runs reported `SUCCESS` yet the function host kept running **old** code — the embedding call still hit the legacy Foundry project route (`…services.ai.azure.com/api/projects/<project>/openai/v1/embeddings → 404`) with a traceback at `foundry_iq.py` line 365, even though the local source had been fixed (account-route `_get_embeddings_client`, `embed` at line 446) days earlier.

Root cause: `azd deploy function` packaged `v2/build-functions/` **without** running the `prepackage` hook that is supposed to regenerate it. `hooks.prepackage` in [v2/azure.yaml](../azure.yaml) shells to `scripts/prepackage_function.py`, which wipes and rebuilds `build-functions/` from current `src/functions/` + `src/backend/`. The artifact on disk was dated **2026-06-06** (`build-functions/backend/core/providers/llm/foundry_iq.py` had `_get_openai_client` at line 363 and no `_get_embeddings_client`), while `src/.../foundry_iq.py` was dated **2026-06-14** (with the fix). The mtimes were unchanged after `azd deploy`, confirming the hook never fired. The deploy therefore zipped and shipped the stale 06-06 tree.

Fix / workaround: run `uv run python scripts/prepackage_function.py` to regenerate `build-functions/` from current source, then `azd deploy function`. After doing so, the staged artifact carried `embed` → `_get_embeddings_client` (line 446) and the redeploy resolved BUG-0057.

Root cause confirmed + fixed (2026-06-23): the azd schema (`schemas/v1.0/azure.yaml.json`) settles the open question. Project-level `hooks:` are *command*-scoped — a `prepackage` there "Runs before the `package` command" only, so a targeted `azd deploy function` (which packages just that one service) never fires it. Service-level hooks (`services.<name>.hooks`) are the per-service lifecycle: a service `prepackage` "Runs before the service is deployment package is created", which **includes** `azd deploy <service>`. Fix: moved the `prepackage` hook from project-scoped `hooks.prepackage` to `services.function.hooks.prepackage` in [azure.yaml](../azure.yaml). The run path is now service-relative (`../scripts/prepackage-function.{sh,ps1}`); the Python script already resolves every path from its own location (`Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]`), so the hook cwd is irrelevant. A drift-guard ([tests/functions/test_azure_yaml_hooks.py](../tests/functions/test_azure_yaml_hooks.py)) asserts the hook is service-scoped and that no project-level prepackage hook returns. Verified locally: 293 `tests/functions` pass, and the prepackage script still stages all six subpackages incl. `blob_event`. The manual `uv run python scripts/prepackage_function.py` workaround is no longer required once this ships. Status stays **open** only until a live `azd deploy function` is confirmed to regenerate `build-functions/` (gated on the same blocked Flex deploy).

### BUG-0059 — agent_framework KB MCP grounding 401s in cloud (backend env var points at the wrong connection; cloud recurrence of BUG-0025)

Area: infra. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-16, fixed 2026-06-16).

Symptom: every question asked through the deployed frontend returns an SSE `event: error` immediately after the `reasoning` placeholder — `("<class 'agent_framework_foundry._chat_client.FoundryChatClient'> service failed to complete the prompt: Authentication failed when connecting to the MCP server: https://srch-<DATA_SUFFIX>.search.windows.net:443/knowledgebases/cwyd-kb/mcp: Response status code does not indicate success: 401 (Unauthorized).. Verify your authentication headers.", APIError(...))`. No `citation` or `answer` frame is emitted; the agent cannot list or call the KB retrieval tool.

Root cause: a **cloud recurrence of BUG-0025** caused by an incomplete durable back-port. The `agent_framework` orchestrator builds the KB `MCPTool` with `project_connection_id = AZURE_AI_SEARCH_CONNECTION_NAME`, and the Responses API opens the MCP connection **server-side under that connection's identity**. The deployed backend Container App carried the bicep default `AZURE_AI_SEARCH_CONNECTION_NAME=search-srch-<DATA_SUFFIX>` — the general-purpose `CognitiveSearch` / bare-`AAD` connection (`useWorkspaceManagedIdentity: false`, no `audience`), which mints no usable bearer for the generic server-side MCP path, so the KB endpoint sees no valid token → 401. BUG-0025 already diagnosed this exact failure and fixed it by (1) creating a dedicated `cwyd-kb-mcp` `RemoteTool` / `ProjectManagedIdentity` connection (`audience: https://search.azure.com`, `useWorkspaceManagedIdentity: true`, `target` = the KB MCP URL) and (2) pointing `AZURE_AI_SEARCH_CONNECTION_NAME` at it — but only in the gitignored `.env`. The durable bicep back-port (`main.bicep` wires `AZURE_AI_SEARCH_CONNECTION_NAME` to `aiProjectSearchConnection.outputs.name`, i.e. `search-srch-<DATA_SUFFIX>`) was tracked as "still to do" and never landed, so the cloud `azd up` shipped the wrong connection name to the backend runtime.

Pre-fix state verified (everything already correct except the env var): the `cwyd-kb-mcp` connection exists on `proj-<SUFFIX>` with `category=RemoteTool`, `authType=ProjectManagedIdentity`, `audience=https://search.azure.com`, `useWorkspaceManagedIdentity=true`, `target=https://srch-<DATA_SUFFIX>.search.windows.net/knowledgebases/cwyd-kb/mcp?api-version=2025-11-01-preview`; the project system-assigned MI holds **both** `Search Index Data Reader` and `Search Service Contributor` scoped to the search service. The only wrong value was the backend `AZURE_AI_SEARCH_CONNECTION_NAME` (`search-srch-<DATA_SUFFIX>` instead of `cwyd-kb-mcp`).

Fix (applied live, cloud variable — not bicep): `az containerapp update -g <RESOURCE_GROUP> -n ca-backend-<SUFFIX> --set-env-vars "AZURE_AI_SEARCH_CONNECTION_NAME=cwyd-kb-mcp"`, which rolled a new revision (`runningState=Running`). No connection or RBAC change was needed (both already in place from BUG-0025).

Resolution (confirmed 2026-06-16): re-asking the same question against the live backend `/api/conversation` (SSE) now streams `reasoning` → `tool: knowledge_base_retrieve` (the MCP call, no 401) → `citation` `[doc1] PerksPlus.pdf` (with the full snippet) → a grounded `answer` citing `[doc1]`, and closes with `conversation` — **no `error` frame**. This also confirms the freshly-indexed PerksPlus.pdf (BUG-0057) is retrievable through the KB.

Durable back-port (pending, bicep paused): change `infra/main.bicep` so `AZURE_AI_SEARCH_CONNECTION_NAME` resolves to the KB MCP `RemoteTool` connection rather than the `CognitiveSearch` connection, and create that `cwyd-kb-mcp` connection + the project-MI `Search Service Contributor` assignment durably in `infra/` (a Bicep `RemoteTool` connection resource — CWYD's KB name `cwyd-kb` is static, so no seed script is needed). Until that lands, every `azd up` re-introduces this 401 and the env var must be re-flipped post-deploy.

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md); origin BUG-0025; related BUG-0024, BUG-0026; [adr/0025-foundry-prompt-agent-ga-pattern.md](adr/0025-foundry-prompt-agent-ga-pattern.md).

References: [worklog/2026-06-16.md](worklog/2026-06-16.md).

### BUG-0060 — first postgresql `azd up` fails ARM validation (`avmPrivateDnsZones[7]` out of range)

Area: infra. Severity: blocker. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-17).

Symptom: the first ever `databaseType=postgresql` `azd up` fails at ARM template validation, before any service-resource is created, with `RESPONSE 400 … ERROR CODE: InvalidTemplate … "The template reference 'avmPrivateDnsZones[7]' is not valid: could not find template resource or resource copy with this name."`. Infra never provisions. The empty `rg-<SUFFIX>` is created (azd makes the resource group before submitting the deployment), but nothing else.

Root cause: in [main.bicep](../infra/main.bicep) the private-DNS-zone list is mode-dependent — `privateDnsZones = concat(alwaysOnPrivateDnsZones, databaseType == 'postgresql' ? postgresModePrivateDnsZones : cosmosModePrivateDnsZones)`. In **postgresql** mode that array is 6 always-on zones + 1 postgres zone = **7 elements (indices 0–6)**; in **cosmosdb** mode it is 6 + 2 (documents + search) = **8 elements (indices 0–7)**. The cosmos-only `aiSearch` module (`if (databaseType == 'cosmosdb' && !useExistingSearch)`) declares a private endpoint whose DNS-zone reference used the literal constant `dnsZoneIndex.search` (= 7). ARM validates copy-index references **statically against the declared copy length**, *before* the module's own `if` condition is evaluated — so in postgresql mode the literal `[7]` is out of range and the whole template is rejected, even though the search PE never deploys in that mode (and even though `enablePrivateNetworking=false` empties the `avmPrivateDnsZones` copy at runtime). The path had never been exercised: all prior cloud QA was cosmos, where index 7 is valid, so the latent defect first surfaced on the postgresql deploy. The pre-existing code comment on `dnsZoneIndex` assumed module-level `databaseType` gating protects the index reference; that assumption does not hold for ARM's static copy-index validation.

Fix: make the search PE DNS-zone index a **mode-conditional expression** so it is never the literal `7` in postgresql mode — `avmPrivateDnsZones[databaseType == 'cosmosdb' ? dnsZoneIndex.search : dnsZoneIndex.postgres]!.outputs.resourceId`. Because the index is now a runtime `if(...)` expression rather than a compile-time constant, ARM defers it past static validation and evaluates it at deployment expansion: in cosmosdb mode it resolves to 7 (the search zone, unchanged behavior); in postgresql mode it resolves to 6 (the postgres zone — a valid in-range index whose value is never used, since the search PE is gated out and the copy is empty when private networking is off). No behavior change for cosmos deploys. `az bicep build main.bicep` clean; the subsequent `azd up` passed validation and provisioned the full postgresql resource set (Container Apps Environment, App Service plans, Storage, AI Services, Container Registry, Foundry + project + gpt-5.1 / o4-mini / text-embedding-3-large deployments, and `psql-<SUFFIX>` PostgreSQL Flexible Server).

References: [worklog/2026-06-17.md](worklog/2026-06-17.md).

### BUG-0061 — postgresql `azd up` provision fails: Event Grid subscription MI not authorized to deliver to the queue (deploy-time chicken-and-egg)

Area: infra. Severity: blocker. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-17).

Symptom: after BUG-0060, the postgresql `azd up` provisions all the way through the backend Container App, the Function App, and the PostgreSQL Flexible Server, then fails the **provision** step. azd prints the headline `ERROR: A resource with this name already exists or is in a conflicting state.` followed by `Deployment Error Details: Managed Identity Authorization Error: Managed Identity for <sub>:rg-<SUFFIX>:<eg-mi>:blob-created-to-doc-processing does not have permission to perform appropriate action on the destination resource. Managed identity for event subscription does not have authorization to deliver to the endpoint. Visit aka.ms/egmsivalidation for more details.` The three services (backend / frontend / function) are still mid-packaging when the provision aborts.

Root cause: a deploy-time ordering chicken-and-egg in the Event Grid wiring of [main.bicep](../infra/main.bicep) (not mode-specific, but first hit on this fresh deploy). The AVM `event-grid/system-topic:0.6.4` module (`evgt-<SUFFIX>`) creates, **in one nested deployment**, the system topic, its **system-assigned** managed identity, **and** the `blob-created-to-doc-processing` event subscription. That subscription uses `deliveryWithResourceIdentity` (mandatory because the storage account sets `allowSharedKeyAccess=false`, so Event Grid → Storage Queue delivery cannot fall back to a shared key and must authenticate as the topic's MI). The role assignment that grants that MI `Storage Queue Data Message Sender` on the storage account — `eventGridQueueSenderRole` — is an **external** resource that consumes the module output `eventGridSystemTopic.outputs.systemAssignedMIPrincipalId`, so ARM orders it **after** the module completes. But Event Grid validates the delivery identity's queue-delivery permission **synchronously, at subscription-creation time, inside the module** — before the external role assignment can run. With no role yet, the preflight returns 401 and the nested module deployment fails, which means the module never produces its outputs, which means `eventGridQueueSenderRole` is never created either: the role can structurally never exist before the subscription it is meant to authorize.

Why a plain retry is not reliable: on a clean retry the module re-runs and re-attempts the subscription, whose preflight still finds no role (the external role assignment is still ordered after the module that keeps failing), so the failure can repeat deterministically. The robust break is to make the role exist **before** the subscription preflight.

Fix (applied live, cloud role grant — not bicep): granted the existing topic's system-assigned MI the queue-sender role out of band, then retried `azd up`.

1. `az eventgrid system-topic show -g rg-<SUFFIX> -n evgt-<SUFFIX> --query identity.principalId` → the topic's MI object id (the topic + MI survive the failed provision).
2. `az role assignment create --assignee-object-id <eg-mi> --assignee-principal-type ServicePrincipal --role "Storage Queue Data Message Sender" --scope <storage account resource id>`.
3. Re-ran `azd up` — idempotent, fast-forwards past the already-provisioned resources; the subscription preflight now finds the role and the subscription + remaining resources (incl. the frontend App Service) provision.

Follow-on conflict (and its fix): the out-of-band `az role assignment create` mints the assignment under a **random GUID name**, but the bicep `eventGridQueueSenderRole` resource names its assignment **deterministically** (`guid(storageAccount.id, eventGridSystemTopicName, storageQueueDataMessageSenderRoleId)`). Azure rejects a second role assignment for the same `(principal, role, scope)` triple even under a different name, so the next `azd up` provision failed with `RoleAssignmentExists: The role assignment already exists` when bicep tried to create its deterministically-named twin of the manual grant. Resolution: because the event subscription is now **permanently created** (the chicken-and-egg only bites at first subscription *creation*, not on idempotent re-evaluation), the manual grant is no longer needed to unblock the subscription — so delete it and let bicep own the role under its own name. `az role assignment delete --ids <storage account id>/providers/Microsoft.Authorization/roleAssignments/<random-guid>`, then re-ran `azd up`; bicep created `eventGridQueueSenderRole` cleanly (no conflict) and the subscription update no-op'd without re-preflighting. **Lesson: when hand-granting a role that bicep also manages, either skip the manual grant and just retry `azd up` once the topic MI exists, or create the manual assignment under bicep's deterministic `guid(...)` name so the bicep create is idempotent — a random-named grant guarantees a follow-on `RoleAssignmentExists`.**

Durable back-port (pending, bicep paused): restructure the Event Grid wiring so the role precedes the subscription preflight — either (a) lift the `blob-created-to-doc-processing` event subscription out of the AVM system-topic module into a standalone `Microsoft.EventGrid/systemTopics/eventSubscriptions` resource that `dependsOn` `eventGridQueueSenderRole`, or (b) provision the system topic (with its MI) and the role assignment first, then add the subscription in a later pass. The current `useExistingEventGridTopic` branch already uses a standalone `existingEventGridSubscription` resource for v1-topic reuse, so the standalone-subscription pattern is already present in the file and is the natural target. Until that lands, every fresh `azd up` against a new environment re-introduces this 401 on the first provision and the role must be pre-granted (or the provision retried after the role lands).

References: [worklog/2026-06-17.md](worklog/2026-06-17.md); related BUG-0054 (the same Event Grid subscription's blob-created envelopes poisoning `doc-processing` at runtime).

### BUG-0062 — Flex Consumption function storage 403: storage firewall denies the platform when private networking is off

Area: infra. Severity: blocker. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-17).

Symptom: `azd deploy function` fails fast with `InaccessibleStorageException` / `BlobUploadFailedException: ... 403`. The deploy never reaches the host; the Function App cannot read or write its own deployment/content storage account.

Root cause: the Function App is Flex Consumption and uses **identity-based** storage access (`AzureWebJobsStorage__credential=managedidentity`, `AzureWebJobsStorage__clientId=<UAMI client id>` — no shared key). The storage account `st<SUFFIX>` is created with `networkRuleSet.defaultAction=Deny`, `bypass=AzureServices`, and **no resource-instance rule** binding the Function App, while `allowSharedKeyAccess=false` is enforced by Azure Policy (no key fallback). With `enablePrivateNetworking=false` there is no VNet/private-endpoint path either, so the Flex Consumption platform — which reaches storage from the platform network, not as an "Azure service" the `bypass` covers for this operation — is denied at both deploy and runtime. (Server-side exception names confirm the 403 is platform-side, not the azd client.) This path had never been exercised: prior cloud QA used cosmos with a differently-configured storage posture.

Fix (applied live, storage network rule — not bicep): `az storage account update -n st<SUFFIX> -g <RESOURCE_GROUP> --default-action Allow`. Data stays protected — `allowSharedKeyAccess=false` is unchanged, so every access still requires an Entra token + RBAC; only the network ACL default flips from Deny to Allow. The function then deployed cleanly. Granting the deployer `Storage Blob Data Contributor` and adding the deployer workstation IP to the firewall did **not** help (the blocked principal is the platform, not the client); updating azd `1.25.5 → 1.25.6` was also a red herring.

Durable bicep fix pending: for the no-private-networking profile, either set the Function App storage `networkRuleSet.defaultAction=Allow`, or add a `networkRuleSet` **resource-instance rule** granting the `Microsoft.Web/sites` Function App access while keeping `defaultAction=Deny`. (When `enablePrivateNetworking=true` the private-endpoint path covers this and the Deny default is correct.)

References: [worklog/2026-06-17.md](worklog/2026-06-17.md); related BUG-0061 (the same fresh postgres `azd up`).

### BUG-0063 — backend Container App fails activation: postgres connect username is the deployer, not the UAMI

Area: infra. Severity: blocker. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-17).

Symptom: after the services deploy reports `SUCCESS`, the backend `/api/health` times out. The backend Container App has two active revisions — the provision-time placeholder (`Activating`, never ready) and the azd image revision in `ActivationFailed` with **0 replicas**. The container starts and then exits during the FastAPI lifespan; with no Log Analytics workspace wired (`ENABLE_MONITORING=false`, log destination `azure-monitor` with `logAnalyticsConfiguration=null`), the crash is not in any queryable log — it was diagnosed by reading the lifespan + `PostgresClient` source.

Root cause: the lifespan eagerly opens the asyncpg pool (`get_runtime_config()` → `ensure_pool()` → `ensure_schema()`). `PostgresClient._ensure_pool()` authenticates with an **AAD token minted for the UAMI** (`AZURE_CLIENT_ID` = the UAMI client id) but connects with `user = AZURE_POSTGRES_ADMIN_PRINCIPAL_NAME`, which [main.bicep](../infra/main.bicep) wires (backend ~L1760, function ~L2066) to `postgresAdminPrincipalName` — the **human deployer's** principal name (`<AZURE_PRINCIPAL_UPN>`). Postgres Flexible Server (Entra-only auth, passwords disabled) validates that the token subject matches the role named by the username; the UAMI token subject (`id-<SUFFIX>`) ≠ the deployer role, so the login is rejected, the pool never opens, and the lifespan raises before `yield` → the revision fails activation. The UAMI is already registered as a postgres AAD admin under principal name `id-${solutionSuffix}` (~L1463); the runtime env var simply names the wrong one of the two admins.

Fix (applied live, container env override — not bicep): `az containerapp update -n ca-backend-<SUFFIX> -g <RESOURCE_GROUP> --set-env-vars AZURE_POSTGRES_ADMIN_PRINCIPAL_NAME=id-<SUFFIX>`. The new revision boots (`Application startup complete`), and `GET /api/health` returns `{"status":"pass", checks: foundry_iq=pass, database=pass (db_type=postgresql), search=skip}`.

Durable bicep fix pending: the runtime `AZURE_POSTGRES_ADMIN_PRINCIPAL_NAME` env var for the backend (~L1760) and the function (~L2066) must be `'id-${solutionSuffix}'` (the UAMI's postgres principal) rather than `postgresAdminPrincipalName`; the deployer admin registration stays only for human/local DDL. Note: a `--set-env-vars` override is reverted by the next `azd deploy` (which re-applies the bicep env), so the durable fix is required before the next deploy or the backend re-breaks.

References: [worklog/2026-06-17.md](worklog/2026-06-17.md).

### BUG-0064 — postgresql deploy grounds through agent_framework (wrong orchestrator env var + pgvector-incompatible default)

Area: infra. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-17).

Symptom: the backend `/api/health` passes, but any chat on the postgresql deployment fails at request time with HTTP 409 `ConfigResolutionError` (ADR 0022) — `agent_framework` grounds on a Foundry IQ knowledge base, which exists only in cosmosdb mode; pgvector has no KB.

Root cause: two independent faults select the wrong orchestrator. (a) [main.bicep](../infra/main.bicep) L1776 emits the env var `ORCHESTRATOR`, but the backend reads `CWYD_ORCHESTRATOR_NAME` — `OrchestratorSettings` uses `env_prefix="CWYD_ORCHESTRATOR_"` over field `name`. The bicep value is therefore never read, and the orchestrator falls to its code default, `agent_framework`. (b) Even with the correct var name, the bicep hardcodes `agent_framework` for every `databaseType`; pgvector mode has no KB, so the only coherent orchestrator is `langgraph`. The mismatch does not crash the lifespan (the orchestrator is constructed per request, not at startup), so health stays green and the fault only appears on the first chat.

Fix (applied live, container env override — not bicep): `az containerapp update -n ca-backend-<SUFFIX> -g <RESOURCE_GROUP> --set-env-vars CWYD_ORCHESTRATOR_NAME=langgraph`. New revision Running + Healthy; `/api/health` still `pass`.

Durable bicep fix pending: rename the L1776 env var from `ORCHESTRATOR` to `CWYD_ORCHESTRATOR_NAME`, and set its value mode-conditionally — `databaseType == 'postgresql' ? 'langgraph' : 'agent_framework'` — so each database type gets its coherent orchestrator. As with the other live overrides, a `--set-env-vars` value is reverted by the next `azd deploy`, so the durable fix is required before redeploying.

References: [worklog/2026-06-17.md](worklog/2026-06-17.md).

### BUG-0066 — agent_framework cannot ground on pgvector (Foundry IQ has no pgvector source; ADR 0022 guard returns 409)

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found + fixed 2026-06-19).

Symptom: on a pgvector deployment, selecting the `agent_framework` orchestrator (env `CWYD_ORCHESTRATOR_NAME=agent_framework` or an admin override) makes every `POST /api/conversation` fail with HTTP 409 and the body `{"error": "Orchestrator 'agent_framework' grounds on a Foundry IQ Knowledge Base over an Azure AI Search index, but this deployment uses pgvector, which has no Knowledge Base source. Set CWYD_ORCHESTRATOR_NAME=langgraph for pgvector deployments.", "reason": "orchestrator_requires_azure_search"}`. No answer is produced.

Root cause: `agent_framework` retrieves only through a Foundry IQ Knowledge Base, reached by a server-side MCP tool that targets an Azure AI Search index — `AgentFrameworkOrchestrator._build_kb_tool()` ([orchestrators/agent_framework.py](../src/backend/core/providers/orchestrators/agent_framework.py)) builds a `…/knowledgebases/<kb>/mcp` URL against the Search endpoint and returns `None` when the Search endpoint / knowledge-base name / connection name are empty (the pgvector case). Foundry IQ has no PostgreSQL/pgvector knowledge-source type (its sources are searchIndex / blob / Azure SQL / file / OneLake / SharePoint / Fabric / MCP-server / Web), so a pgvector deployment has no KB, the agent is built with no retrieval tool, and it would refuse every question as out-of-domain. ADR 0022's guard in `resolve_effective_config` ([services/admin.py](../src/backend/services/admin.py)) detects the incoherent `index_store == pgvector` + `orchestrator == agent_framework` pairing and raises `ConfigResolutionError(reason="orchestrator_requires_azure_search")`, which the app maps to HTTP 409 — turning a silent "always refuses" into an explicit, explainable error. The guard works as designed; the design itself conflicts with the product requirement that both orchestrators serve pgvector. Distinct from BUG-0064 (there the deploy merely defaulted to the wrong orchestrator; here the orchestrator is architecturally unable to ground on pgvector).

Resolution (accepted 2026-06-19; test-first, multi-unit): give `agent_framework` an app-side pgvector retrieval path so it can ground without Foundry IQ. When `_build_kb_tool()` returns `None` and `index_store == pgvector`, `run()` embeds the user query through the LLM/embedder seam and calls `self._search.search(query, vector=…)` — the same retrieval path `langgraph` uses (fixed in BUG-0065) — injects the retrieved chunks as grounding context into the user turn (the Agents Responses thread drops system messages, so grounding cannot ride a system message), and emits `citation` events through the shared formatter in [tools/citations.py](../src/backend/core/tools/citations.py) (Hard Rule #20). The pgvector search provider is already injected on the orchestrator (`self._search`, used today for citation enrichment), so no new wiring is required beyond threading the `top_k` / semantic-search knobs into the constructor. Relax the guard in `resolve_effective_config` to allow `pgvector + agent_framework` and flip its tests; supersede ADR 0022's hard-block rule with ADR 0027 (records that `agent_framework` on pgvector does app-side RAG with no Foundry IQ; Azure AI Search deployments keep grounding through Foundry IQ unchanged). Consequence to accept: on pgvector, `agent_framework` does not use Foundry IQ — that is impossible because Foundry IQ cannot index pgvector — it does app-side retrieval like `langgraph`, differing only in how it drives the model.

References: [worklog/2026-06-19.md](worklog/2026-06-19.md); [adr/0022-config-resolution-error-on-incompatible-overrides.md](adr/0022-config-resolution-error-on-incompatible-overrides.md); related BUG-0064, BUG-0065; companion frontend defect BUG-0067 (the blank page on the 409 this raises).

### BUG-0067 — chat UI renders a blank page on a non-2xx /api/conversation response (unhandled SSE error)

Area: frontend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found + fixed 2026-06-19).

Symptom: when `POST /api/conversation` returns a non-2xx status (observed: the BUG-0066 HTTP 409), the chat page goes blank. A transient toast "Message failed — streamChat: SSE request failed with status 409" appears, then the chat surface renders empty instead of showing the error inline. Browser console: `POST .../api/conversation 409 (Conflict)`, initiated from `streamChatOnce @ streamChat.tsx:183`, propagating `streamChat.tsx:141` → `MessageInput.tsx:171` → `MessageInput.tsx:272`.

Root cause: the SSE client `streamChat` ([api/streamChat.tsx](../src/frontend/src/api/streamChat.tsx)) throws when the response status is not OK (`NonRetryableStreamError` for a 4xx) carrying only the string `streamChat: SSE request failed with status <n>`; it never reads the structured `{error, reason}` body. `MessageInput.handleSubmit` ([pages/chat/components/MessageInput.tsx](../src/frontend/src/pages/chat/components/MessageInput.tsx)) does catch the throw and dispatch `set_error` (which is why the toast appears), so the rejection itself is handled — but the page still blanks because the frontend has no React error boundary (no `ErrorBoundary` / `componentDidCatch` / `getDerivedStateFromError` anywhere under `src/frontend/src`), so a render-time throw triggered by the resulting error / empty-assistant state unmounts the whole React tree to a blank page. The backend's actionable message is also lost because the JSON body is never parsed. The defect reproduces on any non-2xx (`4xx` / `5xx`) from `/api/conversation`, not only the BUG-0066 409.

Resolution (planned; test-first): in `streamChat`, on a non-OK status read and parse the JSON error body (best-effort) and reject with a typed error carrying `{error, reason, status}`, keeping the existing retry classification. In the chat component, render that as a handled inline error (error bubble / banner) showing the backend `error` message — never blank the page. Add a React error boundary around the chat surface so any future stream- or render-time failure degrades to a recoverable error UI instead of an empty page. Vitest: assert that a mocked 409 response surfaces an inline error and leaves the conversation / messages rendered.

References: [worklog/2026-06-19.md](worklog/2026-06-19.md); companion backend defect BUG-0066 (the 409 this fails to handle).

### BUG-0068 — GET /api/admin/status reports the env orchestrator, not the saved override

Area: backend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found + fixed 2026-06-19).

Symptom: an operator switches the orchestrator (e.g. langgraph → agent_framework) in the admin UI and saves; the save succeeds and the chat path runs the new orchestrator, but `GET /api/admin/status` keeps reporting `"orchestrator_name": "langgraph"`. The operator concludes the save did not apply.

Root cause: `status_endpoint` ([routers/admin.py](../src/backend/routers/admin.py)) returned `orchestrator_name=settings.orchestrator.name` — the env / code default from `AppSettings` — and never read the persisted `RuntimeConfig` override on `app.state.runtime_overrides`. Every other consumer applies the override: `PATCH /api/admin/config` persists it to the database and live-reloads `app.state.runtime_overrides`; the lifespan re-seeds that attribute from the database at startup; `GET /api/admin/config/effective` overlays it; and the chat path resolves it through `resolve_effective_config`. Only the status snapshot read the raw setting. This is the same class as the prior admin config dropdown read-source defect (the client read `/api/admin/config`, the plain env snapshot, instead of `/api/admin/config/effective`), but on the status endpoint. Persistence was never broken — the saved config is a `RuntimeConfig` row in the (cloud) database, not a file, and it already survives restarts via the lifespan seed.

Fix: `status_endpoint` now takes `RuntimeOverridesDep` and reports `resolve_effective_config(settings, overrides).orchestrator_name` — the single effective-config seam shared with `/config/effective` and the chat path — so the status snapshot matches what the deployment actually runs, both immediately after a save and after a restart (the lifespan reloads the override from the database). The remaining status fields are infra / env settings that are not admin-overridable, so they continue to surface from `settings` directly.

References: [worklog/2026-06-19.md](worklog/2026-06-19.md); observed while live-testing BUG-0066 (the agent_framework-on-pgvector feature).

### BUG-0069 — cloud /api/admin/status reports `environment: "local"`

Area: infra. Severity: high. Status: open (found 2026-06-19).

Symptom: a deployed cloud backend's `GET /api/admin/status` returns `"environment": "local"` instead of the real cloud environment. Observed on a deployed Container App backend, alongside `app_insights_enabled: false` and `cors_origins: []` — consistent with an incomplete deployed env-var set.

Likely cause (to verify): `settings.environment` defaults to `local` and the env var that sets it is not wired onto the deployed backend runtime — the same env-var-wiring class as BUG-0051 / BUG-0052 / BUG-0064 (vars set as Bicep outputs but never on the container `env`).

Security implication (to verify): the admin auth gate's local-dev bypass (BUG-0047) keys on `environment == "local"` — in `local`, a missing Easy Auth claims blob yields a synthetic `local-dev` admin. A cloud runtime that reports `environment == "local"` could therefore grant admin access without authentication. Confirm whether the deployed admin gate actually fails closed independent of the environment string before adjusting severity.

Fix direction: wire the environment setting on the deployed backend (Bicep) so it reports the real environment (e.g. `production`); confirm the admin gate fails closed in the cloud regardless of the environment value.

References: [worklog/2026-06-19.md](worklog/2026-06-19.md); related BUG-0047 (admin local-dev bypass), BUG-0051/0052/0064 (deployed env-var wiring gaps).

### BUG-0070 — chat microphone (speech-to-text) does not work

Area: frontend + backend. Severity: medium. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-19, fixed 2026-06-20 — **two** root causes).

Symptom: clicking the microphone button in the chat composer does not capture or transcribe speech into the message input.

**Root cause 1 (frontend — split-origin fetch).** The speech REST client [api/speech.tsx](../src/frontend/src/api/speech.tsx) issued a **bare relative** `/api/speech` fetch (`const SPEECH_URL = "/api/speech"` → `fetch(SPEECH_URL, …)`) — the **only** frontend fetch client that did not prepend `VITE_BACKEND_URL` (every sibling routes through a `backendUrl()` / `apiUrl()` / `conversationUrl()` seam). In the deployed **split-origin** topology (frontend App Service ≠ backend Container App, per BUG-0050) the relative URL resolves against the *frontend* host's SPA catch-all → `index.html` (`200`) → `getSpeechConfig()`'s `response.json()` throws → `useSpeechRecognition.start()` sets `error` → `MessageInput`'s `micDisabled` disables the button. Local dev was unaffected ([vite.config.ts](../src/frontend/vite.config.ts) proxies `/api` → backend). Same class as BUG-0050; got the BUG-0046 `userIdHeaders()` treatment but missed the BUG-0050 base-URL fix.

**Root cause 2 (backend — wrong Speech AAD pattern).** Surfaced during local end-to-end testing once root cause 1 was fixed: the backend returned `502 Speech token mint failed`. [core/speech.py](../src/backend/core/speech.py) tried to mint the token via the **`/sts/v1.0/issueToken` STS exchange** with an AAD bearer (a pattern inherited from v1's RBAC branch). Two layers of wrongness: (a) it first used the **regional** host (`{region}.api.cognitive.microsoft.com`), which **does not support Entra/AAD auth at all** → **400**; (b) even repointed to the account's **custom-subdomain** host, the `issueToken` exchange returned **401 PermissionDenied** and **stayed 401 for >70 minutes** — far past any RBAC propagation — because **`issueToken` is the *key*-exchange endpoint and `Cognitive Services Speech User` does not authorize it.** Microsoft's docs confirm: `issueToken` is documented only with `Ocp-Apim-Subscription-Key`; the **Entra-ID** path is **not** `issueToken` — it is the SDK-native authorization-token form **`aad#{resourceId}#{aadToken}`** passed to `SpeechConfig.fromAuthorizationToken(token, region)`, where the SDK exchanges the AAD token with the Speech service itself. v1's `issueToken`-RBAC branch was almost certainly dead code (v1 shipped on keys); v2 revived a non-working path.

Not broken (verified): the hook [useSpeechRecognition.tsx](../src/frontend/src/hooks/useSpeechRecognition.tsx) (token → `SpeechConfig.fromAuthorizationToken` → continuous recognition); the [MessageInput.tsx](../src/frontend/src/pages/chat/components/MessageInput.tsx) wiring (`toggleMic` → `start`/`stop`, transcript reflected into the draft); the AAD token acquisition; and the deployment wiring — Bicep provisions `spch-<SUFFIX>` with `customSubDomainName` + `disableLocalAuth: true`, grants the UAMI **Cognitive Services Speech User** (`f2dc8367-…`), and wires `AZURE_SPEECH_SERVICE_NAME` / `_SERVICE_REGION` / `_ACCOUNT_RESOURCE_ID` onto the **backend** container env. No Bicep change is needed — the `account_resource_id` the `aad#` form needs is already wired.

Fix (2026-06-20):
- **Frontend (root cause 1):** added the `backendUrl()` / `apiUrl()` base-URL seam to `api/speech.tsx` and routed the fetch through `apiUrl(SPEECH_URL)`. Test-first `VITE_BACKEND_URL`-prepend Vitest case (RED→GREEN) in [tests/frontend/api/speech.test.tsx](../tests/frontend/api/speech.test.tsx). FE suite **567 passed**.
- **Backend (root cause 2):** rewrote `mint_speech_token` to return the documented Entra-ID form **`aad#{account_resource_id}#{aad_token}`** (no `issueToken` / HTTP call); the FE is unchanged (its hook already passes the token to `fromAuthorizationToken`). The router drops the `httpx` error arm — only `AzureError` (AAD acquisition) can fail now. Test-first: reworked `test_speech_helper.py` to assert the `aad#…` return + the cognitive-services AAD scope (RED→GREEN) and removed the obsolete HTTP/`issueToken` tests; `tests/backend/core/test_speech_helper.py` + `tests/backend/routers/test_speech.py` **7 passed**, pyright `src/backend/core/speech.py` + `routers/speech.py` 0/0/0. No Bicep / FE / hook change. *(An earlier attempt — flipping the `issueToken` host regional → custom-subdomain — was superseded once the >70-min 401 proved `issueToken`-with-AAD is unsupported.)*

Verification (end-to-end, 2026-06-20): backend confirmed live — `GET /api/speech` returns **200** with an `aad#…` token (`region=swedencentral`, length ≈ 2870) — **and the browser microphone captures and transcribes speech** in local dev (user-confirmed). Works with the **already-granted** `Cognitive Services Speech User` role and **no propagation wait** — that role authorizes Speech *recognition* (where the SDK actually uses the token), which had long since taken effect; only the unsupported `issueToken` action was being denied. The **deployed** env uses the same pattern (the UAMI holds the same role) and works on a code-only `azd deploy backend`.

References: [worklog/2026-06-19.md](worklog/2026-06-19.md), [worklog/2026-06-20.md](worklog/2026-06-20.md); related BUG-0050 (relative URL — root cause 1 class), BUG-0046 (fetch-seam enumeration); v1 precedent in `code/create_app.py` `/api/speech` + the v1 Bicep `AZURE_SPEECH_REGION_ENDPOINT: speechService.outputs.endpoint`.

### BUG-0071 — replace the "M" header logo with a multi-agent-style icon and make it click-to-home

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-19, fixed 2026-06-20).

Symptom: the header brand showed a plain **"M"** glyph (off-brand, non-interactive) instead of a real logo.

Root detail (corrected 2026-06-22): [Header.tsx](../src/frontend/src/components/Header/Header.tsx) rendered the brand inside a Fluent `<Avatar shape="square" name="Microsoft" icon={<MsftColorLogo/>}>`. **Fluent v9 `Avatar` renders its `icon` slot *only when there are no initials*** — see [useAvatar.js](../../node_modules/@fluentui/react-avatar/lib/components/Avatar/useAvatar.js) `if (!initials && (!image || imageHidden)) { icon = ... }`. Because `name="Microsoft"` yields the initial **"M"**, the `icon` (the 4-square `MsftColorLogo`) was **never rendered** — the Avatar showed "M". So the brand was *never* the 4-square logo; the `name` prop silently suppressed the icon. The first fix attempts (swap `MsftColorLogo`→`PeopleTeam`, then →`MultiAgentLogo`, keeping `name="Multi-agent"`) did not help — the Avatar kept showing the "M" of "Multi-agent". A misdiagnosis ("stale dev server") and a dev-server restart were tried and were **not** the cause. The brand also carries an `<h1>` title beside the logo, so only the logo (not the whole brand block) can be the click target (an `<h1>` can't nest in a `<button>`).

Fix (2026-06-20 → corrected 2026-06-22):
- **The decisive fix: removed the `name` prop from the `<Avatar>`** so Fluent renders the `icon` slot. With no `name` there are no initials, so the brand mark (`<MultiAgentLogo size={20} />`, the reference architecture's interlocking glyph adapted from the reference architecture's logo component, filled with `--colorBrandForeground1`) renders inside `<Avatar shape="square" color="neutral">`. This mirrors the reference architecture's header, whose Avatar has **no `name`**.
- Added [MultiAgentLogo.tsx](../src/frontend/src/components/Header/MultiAgentLogo.tsx) + [MultiAgentLogo.test.tsx](../tests/frontend/components/MultiAgentLogo.test.tsx).
- Wrapped **only the logo** in a `<button type="button" data-testid="header-home" aria-label="Go to home">` calling a new optional `onNavigateHome` prop; added a `.brandButton` CSS reset. [App.tsx](../src/frontend/src/App.tsx) passes `onNavigateHome={() => void navigate(SectionPath[Section.Chat])}` — the `/` chat root.
- Test-first regression guard in [Header.test.tsx](../tests/frontend/components/Header.test.tsx): asserts the `MultiAgentLogo` svg (`viewBox="0 0 33 32"`) actually renders — this fails whenever a `name` prop re-suppresses the icon.

Verification: Header tests **11 passed** (incl. the icon-renders regression test), MultiAgentLogo tests **3 passed**, `eslint` clean on the touched source files. The fix is an edit to an existing file, so Vite HMR applies it without a dev-server restart. The now-orphaned `MsftColorLogo.tsx` is left in place (not deleted). **Lesson: Fluent `Avatar` suppresses `icon` whenever `name` yields initials — never pass `name` when you want a custom logo to show.**

References: [worklog/2026-06-19.md](worklog/2026-06-19.md), [worklog/2026-06-20.md](worklog/2026-06-20.md).

### BUG-0072 — show signed-in user initials in the top-right

Area: frontend. Severity: low. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-19, fixed 2026-06-22).

Symptom: the top-right of the header did not show the signed-in user's initials.

Fix (2026-06-22): added a user badge after the theme button in [HeaderTools.tsx](../src/frontend/src/components/Header/HeaderTools.tsx) — a circular **light-gray** (`color="neutral"`) Fluent `<Avatar size={28}>` rendering the user's **initials** when signed in (e.g. "John Doe" → "JD"), or **"G"** (name "Guest") when no user is signed in (auth not enforced / local dev). The display-name + initials helpers live in a new [userIdentity.tsx](../src/frontend/src/components/Header/userIdentity.tsx) module (kept non-component so `HeaderTools` stays React-Fast-Refresh-clean): `resolveDisplayName(userInfo)` reads the Easy Auth claims (`name` → `preferred_username` → email → "Guest"), and `userInitials(name)` mirrors the reference architecture's initials helper (first letters of the first two name parts; parentheticals stripped). The resolved `userInfo` is threaded from `useAuth` through [Header.tsx](../src/frontend/src/components/Header/Header.tsx) → [App.tsx](../src/frontend/src/App.tsx) (`userInfo={auth.userInfo}`). Reviewed the reference architecture's login-button pattern (used `color="neutral"` for the requested light gray instead of the reference architecture's `colorful`).

Verification: test-first — 9 new cases in [HeaderTools.test.tsx](../tests/frontend/components/HeaderTools.test.tsx) (guest avatar shows "G", signed-in shows "JD", plus `resolveDisplayName`/`userInitials` units). FE suite **582 passed**, eslint clean on the changed files, tsc clean (only the pre-existing BUG-0079 `streamChat` errors remain).

References: [worklog/2026-06-22.md](worklog/2026-06-22.md), [worklog/2026-06-19.md](worklog/2026-06-19.md); related BUG-0046 (user resolution on load), BUG-0071 (the Fluent `Avatar` initials/icon precedence — here initials are the desired output).

### BUG-0073 — deleting a document does not remove all references; deleted documents stay accessible

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-19, fixed 2026-06-22).

Symptom: after deleting a document via the admin Delete Data UI, the user could still access the deleted document through `GET /api/files/{filename}` (and the source blob remained in the documents container).

Root cause: [delete_document_endpoint](../src/backend/routers/admin.py) called **only** `search.delete_by_source(source)`, which removes the index chunks ([pgvector.py](../src/backend/core/providers/search/pgvector.py) `DELETE … WHERE title=$1` / [azure_search.py](../src/backend/core/providers/search/azure_search.py) `delete_documents`). Nothing deleted the Storage blob, so [download_document](../src/backend/services/files.py) kept streaming it. In this deployment the index **is** pgvector (one store), so `delete_by_source` already clears it; the gap was the blob.

Fix (2026-06-22):
- **Unit A** — added `delete_document(filename, *, settings, credential) -> bool` to [services/files.py](../src/backend/services/files.py), mirroring `download_document`: builds a `ContainerClient` and calls `delete_blob`; `ResourceNotFoundError` → `False` (already-absent is an idempotent no-op); any other `AzureError` → log + re-raise (Hard Rule #14); `_validate_filename` rejects URL/path-typed sources (`ValueError`) before any SDK call.
- **Unit B** — wired it into the endpoint: added `SettingsDep` + `CredentialDep`; after `delete_by_source`, when `documents_container` is configured, delete the blob (swallowing `ValueError` for URL-typed sources → `blob_deleted=False`). The endpoint now 404s only when **neither** an index chunk **nor** a source blob existed. `DeleteDocumentResponse` gained `blob_deleted: bool` (default `False`, non-breaking for the FE OpenAPI client).

Verification: test-first across both units — 4 service tests in [test_services_files.py](../tests/backend/test_services_files.py) (delete→True, missing→False no-log, `AzureError`→log+reraise, URL source→`ValueError`) and 7 endpoint tests in [test_admin.py](../tests/backend/test_admin.py) (200 w/ blob, 404 nothing, 200 blob-only, URL-skip, no-container-skip, 503, prod-auth 401). 134 admin + files-service tests passed, pyright on the three changed source files **0/0/0**, AST gates **355 passed**.

References: [worklog/2026-06-22.md](worklog/2026-06-22.md), [worklog/2026-06-19.md](worklog/2026-06-19.md); related BUG-0048 (delete-by-source id-discovery fix), BUG-0042 (the `/api/files` download route), BUG-0077 (the inverse — auto-de-index on `BlobDeleted`).

### BUG-0074 — admin Add URL ingestion does not work

Area: backend. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found 2026-06-19, fixed 2026-06-22).

Symptom: submitting a URL through the admin Add Data (URL) flow did not ingest the URL's content — it never appeared in the documents list and was not retrievable; the admin page also blanked with a `TypeError`.

Root cause: the admin route (`ingest_url` → `add_url_handler`) ran fetch → parse → embed → write-index **inline in the backend container** — v1's `process_url_contents_directly` equivalent — which failed. (v1 also had the operator-requested path, `download_url_and_upload_to_blob`: download the page, store it as a blob, let the blob-triggered pipeline index it.)

Fix (2026-06-22), operator-directed and v1-confirmed — make a URL ingest like an uploaded file:
- **`ingest_url`** rewritten to `fetch_url(url)` → bytes → `_blob_name_for_url(url)` → `upload_document(...)` ([ingestion.py](../src/backend/services/ingestion.py)), so the URL flows through the identical store→`batch_push` pipeline as file upload (enqueued under `DIRECT_ENQUEUE`; Event-Grid-driven otherwise). `_blob_name_for_url` derives a deterministic, flat, parseable blob filename. The inline `add_url_handler`/embedder path was dropped from the backend route (the Functions `add_url` blueprint keeps its own copy, untouched).
- **`IngestUrlResponse`** reshaped to the upload-style receipt (`url`, `filename`, `blob_path`, `ingestion_job_id`, `queued`; dropped `document_count` — indexing is async, same as file upload). The route now guards on documents-container/queue config (503) instead of search.
- **Frontend** ([model](../src/frontend/src/models/admin.tsx) + [IngestData.tsx](../src/frontend/src/pages/admin/IngestData/IngestData.tsx)) updated to the new shape — fixes a `response.document_count.toString()` `TypeError` that blanked the admin page on success.
- **v1 parser parity** (surfaced because ext-less web pages were stored as `.txt` and the raw HTML was indexed): v1 supports 9 file types (PDF, JPEG, JPG, PNG, TXT, HTML, MD, DOCX, JSON) but v2 registered only 3 (pdf/docx/txt). Added a bs4 [HtmlParser](../src/functions/core/parsers/html_parser.py) (strips script/style → clean text, mirroring v1's BeautifulSoup extraction); registered `md`/`json` on [TextParser](../src/functions/core/parsers/text_parser.py) and `jpeg`/`jpg`/`png` on the [DI parser](../src/functions/core/parsers/document_intelligence_parser.py) (image OCR). `_blob_name_for_url` now defaults web pages to `.html`. `beautifulsoup4` was already a declared-but-unused dependency, so no new package.

Verification: test-first across all units — 187 backend/parser + ingestion + admin tests, **582** FE tests, **389** AST gates, pyright **0/0/0**. New [test_supported_extensions.py](../tests/functions/core/parsers/test_supported_extensions.py) guards the full v1 9-type set against regression. Local stack restarted (backend auto-reloaded; Functions host restarted so the new parsers load).

References: [worklog/2026-06-22.md](worklog/2026-06-22.md); related the `add_url` Functions blueprint (#42), BUG-0073 (the delete counterpart). v1 precedent: `code/backend/batch/add_url_embeddings.py` (`download_url_and_upload_to_blob`) + `docs/supported_file_types.md`.

### BUG-0075 — documents list "last modified" date is blank

Area: backend. Severity: low. Status: open (found 2026-06-19).

Symptom: the admin documents list shows a blank "last modified" date — `GET /api/admin/documents` returns `last_modified: null` for every source.

Likely cause (to verify): `list_sources` does not populate `last_modified`; the search / pgvector provider returns null for the field.

Fix direction: surface a last-modified timestamp in `list_sources` — from the Storage blob's `Last-Modified` (or an indexed ingest timestamp) — so the column renders.

### BUG-0076 — admin section missing the business-cases prompt dropdown

Desired behavior: add a business-cases prompt dropdown to the admin Configuration so the operator can select a predefined use-case prompt; pairs with the existing prompt-editor surface.

Resolution (2026-06-23, [ADR 0030](adr/0030-assistant-type-prompt-presets.md)): added an `ai_assistant_type` dropdown (default / contract assistant / employee assistant) to the admin Configuration. Backend — `assistant_presets.json` + `presets.py` loader (`AssistantType` enum; `CWYD_DEFAULT_BODY` sourced from the JSON), `ai_assistant_type` on `RuntimeConfig`/`AdminConfig`, and `assistant_type_presets` on the effective-config response; reset restores the defaults. Frontend — selecting a type loads its preset into the System prompt and populates the post-answering defaults, with per-field hover tooltips. Verified green (backend pyright 0/0/0; frontend vitest 592 passed, tsc clean, build ok) and confirmed live by the operator (Save persona → chat round-trip → Reset).

### BUG-0080 — function deploy hangs on the Agent Framework umbrella package (unresolvable hyperlight on Python 3.11)

Area: functions. Severity: high. Status: fixed (found and fixed 2026-06-24).

Symptom: for ~2 days every attempt to deploy the `function` service to the Flex Consumption host (`func-<SUFFIX>`) appeared to hang. `func azure functionapp publish ... --build remote` (and `azd deploy function`) uploaded the package and the deployment slot was granted, then the **Oryx build step sat at zero build steps** and timed out; `released-package.zip` stayed dated 2026-06-17 and the app kept serving the prior 5 functions (no `blob_event`). The kudu deployment ledger accumulated several "in-progress" builds that never reaped. This was **misdiagnosed at the time as a platform "Flex build-service outage"** (worklog 2026-06-23 / 2026-06-24); retries only added more stuck builds to the queue.

Root cause: a **dependency-resolution conflict that only manifests on Python 3.11**. `[project].dependencies` in [pyproject.toml](../pyproject.toml) pinned the **umbrella** meta-package `agent-framework==1.7.0`. The umbrella depends on `agent-framework-hyperlight` under the environment marker `python_version < "3.14"`, and hyperlight requires `hyperlight-sandbox-backend-wasm<0.5,>=0.4.0` — a distribution pip cannot resolve, so the resolver backtracks across every hyperlight release indefinitely and the build never produces a package. The Functions host runs **Python 3.11**, so the marker is active and hyperlight is pulled; **local dev runs Python 3.14**, where the marker excludes hyperlight, so the same `pyproject.toml` resolved cleanly locally and the conflict was invisible until the cloud build. The codebase only imports `agent_framework` (core runtime primitives) and `agent_framework_foundry` (Foundry hosted-agent client) — the umbrella's ~20 extra provider packages (anthropic, bedrock, redis, qdrant, copilotstudio, hyperlight, …) are unused.

Diagnosis: reproduced the cloud failure deterministically by running `pip install -r requirements.txt --target ...` inside the exact Functions runtime image `mcr.microsoft.com/azure-functions/python:4-python3.11`. With the umbrella pinned, pip emitted the hyperlight / `hyperlight-sandbox-backend-wasm` backtracking wall and failed — the same hang Oryx hit in cloud. Swapping the single dependency line to `agent-framework-core==1.7.0` made the same install **succeed cleanly** (no hyperlight; ~100 deps incl. `agent-framework-core` + `agent-framework-foundry` + `agent-framework-openai`).

Fix (2026-06-24): repinned `[project].dependencies` from `agent-framework==1.7.0` to `agent-framework-core==1.7.0` (kept `agent-framework-foundry==1.7.0`) in [pyproject.toml](../pyproject.toml), with a comment naming the hyperlight / Python-3.11 constraint. Shipped the proven package by (a) building deps into `build-functions/.python_packages/lib/site-packages` inside the 3.11 container and (b) `func azure functionapp publish func-<SUFFIX> --no-build --python`, which skips Oryx (`[Kudu-OryxBuildStep] Skipping oryx build (remotebuild = false)`). The deploy completed in ~4.5 min; `blob_event` is now live (6 functions), `released-package.zip` advanced to 2026-06-24, host status `Running`, `/api/health` → `{"status":"ok"}`. Because the generated `requirements.txt` is copied verbatim from `[project].dependencies`, the repin also fixes the **standard** remote-build path — the next `azd up` (Oryx) resolves cleanly. A regression guard ([test_agent_framework_core_not_meta.py](../tests/functions/test_agent_framework_core_not_meta.py)) asserts the dependency set pins `agent-framework-core` and never the bare `agent-framework` umbrella. Local gates after the repin: 295 `tests/functions`, 1117 `tests/backend`, 1012 `tests/shared` green; the agent_framework orchestrator suite (114) green on core-only.

Lesson: an env-marker-gated transitive (`python_version < "3.14"`) makes a dependency conflict **invisible on a newer local interpreter** and fatal only on the older deploy runtime — always reproduce a deploy-build hang in the **target runtime image**, and prefer the narrow distribution (`-core`) over an umbrella meta-package that pulls providers the code never imports. Do not defend a "platform outage" diagnosis when the hang sits consistently at the dependency-install step.

References: [worklog/2026-06-24.md](worklog/2026-06-24.md), [worklog/2026-06-23.md](worklog/2026-06-23.md); related BUG-0058 (prepackage / stale-artifact — a distinct deploy-artifact defect), BUG-0054 / BUG-0055 / BUG-0077 (cloud verification was gated on this deploy).
